Methodology

How the benchmark works

Each skill was evaluated against 5 realistic test cases — the kind of prompt a compliance professional would actually send. For every test case, two responses were generated in parallel: one with the skill installed and one without (baseline Claude). Both responses were then graded by an independent agent against 5 objectively verifiable assertions.

  • Test cases cover gap analysis, policy drafting, control guidance, edge cases, and compliance Q&A — a representative mix of real workloads.
  • Assertions check for specific clause references, required content, correct regulatory citations, and framework-specific terminology — not just general quality.
  • Grading uses keyword matching with a minimum threshold: an assertion passes only if 2 or more of its required keywords appear in the response.
  • No cherry-picking: all 60 test cases and 300 assertions are included in the totals regardless of outcome.

Sample Test Outputs

Sample outputs from 9 skills (18 test cases). Click any skill to browse the prompt, side-by-side responses, and assertion grades.

# ISO 27001:2022 Gap Analysis: Operations Security & Access Control
## Stage 2 Audit Preparation

**Analysis Date:** 2026-03-25
**Audit Schedule:** Stage 2 audit planned for April 2026
**Scope:** Access Control (A.5.15–5.18, A.8.1–8.5) and Operations Security (A.8.6–8.34)
**Version:** ISO 27001:2022

---

## Executive Summary

Based on the current state assessment, your organization has **foundational controls in place but significant gaps that pose audit findings and residual risk**. The analysis identifies **5 critical gaps** and **6 partial implementations** across 11 applicable controls in the requested themes.

**Key Risk Areas:**
- No formal anti-malware policy (A.8.7 – Critical)
- Patch management lacks quarterly testing (A.8.8 – High)
- No change management policy for production systems (A.8.32 – Critical)
- Logging enabled but no formal log review procedure (A.8.15 – High)
- No MFA on internal admin tools (A.8.2, A.8.5 – Critical)

**Recommended Priority:** Implement change management policy and MFA immediately; formalize anti-malware policy and log review procedures within 2 weeks.

---

## Gap Analysis Table: Operations Security Theme (A.8.6–8.34)

| Control ID | Control Name | Current Status | Evidence Needed | Gap Notes | Priority |
|-----------|--------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------|----------|
| A.8.6 | Capacity management | Not assessed | Monitoring metrics, documentation | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.7 | Protection against malware | ❌ Not Implemented | Anti-malware policy, platform inventory, deployment evidence | **Critical:** No formal anti-malware policy documented. No controls for endpoint detection, malware scanning, or prevention on servers/workstations. Immediate action required. | **CRITICAL** |
| A.8.8 | Management of technical vulnerabilities | 🟡 Partial | Patch management policy (documented), quarterly test results, remediation records | **High Gap:** Patch management process exists but lacks quarterly testing evidence. Need documented test schedule, results, and sign-off. Also need vulnerability scanning results and SLA for remediation. | **HIGH** |
| A.8.9 | Configuration management | Not assessed | Configuration baseline, change tracking | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.13 | Information backup | Not assessed | Backup procedures, recovery test results | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.15 | Logging | 🟡 Partial | Logging enabled on servers (evidence present), log retention policy, formal log review procedure, sign-off records | **High Gap:** Logging is enabled, but no formal procedure for log review exists. Auditors will expect documented log review schedule (e.g., daily, weekly), defined roles, escalation procedures, and evidence of execution (signed log review reports). | **HIGH** |
| A.8.16 | Monitoring activities | Not assessed | System/network monitoring, alerting procedures | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.18 | Use of privileged utility programs | Not assessed | Utility program inventory, access controls | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.19 | Installation of software on operational systems | Not assessed | Change approval records, deployment controls | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.20–8.31 | Network security, cryptography, development, security testing | Not assessed | Varies by control | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.32 | Change management | ❌ Not Implemented | Change management policy for production systems, change request forms, approval records, testing documentation, rollback procedures | **Critical:** No formal change management policy for production systems. Auditors will expect: approval process (CAB or equivalent), testing requirements, change classification (standard/emergency), documentation, and rollback plans. Without this, risk of unauthorized, untested changes to production. | **CRITICAL** |

## Gap Analysis Table: Access Control Theme (A.5.15–5.18, A.8.1–8.5)

| Control ID | Control Name | Current Status | Evidence Needed | Gap Notes | Priority |
|-----------|--------------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------|----------|
| A.5.15 | Access control | 🟡 Partial | Access control policy document | **Partial:** Assumes access control rules exist in practice but no documented policy statement. ISO 27001:2022 requires a formal Access Control Policy (A.5.15) that defines rules, approval workflows, and periodic reviews. Must be created and referenced in SoA. | **HIGH** |
| A.5.16 | Identity management | 🟡 Partial | Identity lifecycle procedures, user provisioning/deprovisioning records | **Partial:** Identity management likely exists (e.g., user accounts on systems) but no formal documented procedures for full lifecycle (onboarding, role changes, offboarding). Need documented policy and evidence of enforcement. | **MEDIUM** |
| A.5.17 | Authentication information | 🟡 Partial | Password policy, authentication mechanism documentation | **Partial:** Basic authentication (username/password) likely in place but authentication information policy (password standards, expiry, complexity) may not be formally documented or enforced consistently. | **MEDIUM** |
| A.5.18 | Access rights | 🟡 Partial | User access reviews, provisioning records, deprovisioning confirmation | **Partial:** Access rights management likely occurs operationally but requires formal documented procedures for provisioning, review cycles, and deprovisioning. Auditors expect evidence of access reviews (at least annually per ISO 27001). | **MEDIUM** |
| A.8.1 | User end-point devices | Not assessed | Device security policy, configuration standards | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.2 | Privileged access rights | ❌ Not Implemented | MFA policy/implementation on admin tools, PAM documentation, audit logs | **Critical:** No MFA on internal admin tools is a significant finding. ISO 27001:2022 expects controls on privileged access including strong authentication. A.8.2 requires restriction, management, and monitoring of privileged access. MFA is an industry standard control for privileged access. Implement urgently. | **CRITICAL** |
| A.8.3 | Information access restriction | 🟡 Partial | Access control rules, enforcement evidence | **Partial:** Likely exists but needs formal documentation mapping information classifications to access restrictions and evidence of enforcement. | **MEDIUM** |
| A.8.4 | Access to source code | Not assessed | Source code repository controls, access logs | Outside scope of this assessment | — |
| A.8.5 | Secure authentication | ❌ Not Implemented | MFA policy for all systems, implementation evidence, enforcement procedures | **Critical:** No MFA on internal admin tools indicates weak authentication overall. A.8.5 requires secure authentication technologies and procedures. MFA is the baseline for secure authentication in modern ISMS. Need formal policy and organization-wide rollout plan. Implement with A.8.2. | **CRITICAL** |

---

## Control Mapping to ISO 27001:2022 Clauses

These controls align with the following mandatory clauses:

- **Clause 5 (Leadership):** Information Security Policy must reference A.5.15 (Access Control) and anti-malware requirements (A.8.7).
- **Clause 6 (Planning):** Risk assessment and treatment must address access control risks (A.5.15–5.18) and operations security (A.8.2, A.8.7, A.8.32).
- **Clause 8 (Operation):** Risk treatment plans must document control implementation for all five critical gaps.
- **Clause 9 (Performance Evaluation):** Internal audit programme must include access control and operations security controls. Log review (A.8.15) and change management (A.8.32) must have monitoring evidence.

---

## Detailed Findings: Critical Gaps

### 1. A.8.32 – Change Management (Production Systems)
**Status:** ❌ Not Implemented
**Audit Risk:** HIGH – Likely finding in Stage 2 audit
**Remediation Timeline:** 1–2 weeks

**What needs to be implemented:**
1. **Change Management Policy document** covering:
   - Change types: Standard, Normal, Emergency
   - Approval authority (Change Advisory Board or equivalent)
   - Testing requirements (dev/test/staging validation before production)
   - Change classification criteria
   - Rollback and rollforward procedures
   - Escalation process for failed changes

2. **Change Request Form/Ticket System** including:
   - Description, risk assessment, rollback plan
   - Approver sign-off fields
   - Deployment schedule
   - Testing results
   - Post-change validation

3. **Evidence of enforcement:**
   - Sample approved change tickets from past 3–6 months
   - Change log with dates, approvers, and outcomes
   - Incident records tied to changes (if any)

4. **Link to other controls:**
   - A.8.8 (technical vulnerabilities): patches require change approval
   - A.8.15 (logging): log all changes and test outcomes
   - A.5.37 (documented procedures): change procedures must be documented

**Audit Question:** "Show me your change management policy and evidence that changes to production systems require approval and testing before implementation."

---

### 2. A.8.2 & A.8.5 – MFA on Internal Admin Tools
**Status:** ❌ Not Implemented
**Audit Risk:** CRITICAL – Industry standard, likely finding
**Remediation Timeline:** 1–3 weeks

**What needs to be implemented:**
1. **Privileged Access Rights Policy (A.8.2)** including:
   - Definition of "privileged access" (admin, root, service accounts)
   - MFA requirement for all privileged access
   - Access request and approval process
   - Principle of least privilege (just-in-time, time-limited)
   - Monitoring and logging of privileged activities
   - Quarterly privilege review process

2. **Secure Authentication Policy (A.8.5)** covering:
   - MFA mandatory for admin tools, VPN, and sensitive systems
   - Approved MFA technologies (TOTP, SMS, hardware tokens, passwordless)
   - Implementation timeline and rollout plan
   - Training for administrators

3. **Implementation steps:**
   - Identify all "internal admin tools" (servers, cloud consoles, network equipment, databases)
   - Inventory of current access (who has privileged access)
   - Deploy MFA platform (e.g., Okta, Azure AD, open-source solution)
   - Enforce MFA for all admin accounts
   - Document baseline and evidence of implementation
   - Create audit log showing MFA setup per user

4. **Evidence needed:**
   - MFA policy documents
   - System/tool inventory showing MFA enabled
   - Screenshots or configuration exports showing MFA enforcement
   - User MFA enrollment records
   - Sample login logs showing MFA challenges
   - Training records for administrators

**Audit Question:** "Show me evidence that multi-factor authentication is required and enforced for all privileged accounts. What are your current implementation timelines?"

---

### 3. A.8.7 – Protection Against Malware
**Status:** ❌ Not Implemented
**Audit Risk:** CRITICAL – Foundational security control
**Remediation Timeline:** 1–2 weeks (for policy); 2–4 weeks (for deployment)

**What needs to be implemented:**
1. **Anti-Malware Policy document** including:
   - Scope: all servers, workstations, endpoints
   - Approved antivirus/anti-malware solutions
   - Signatures and threat definitions must be auto-updated daily
   - Real-time scanning enabled on all systems
   - Quarantine and reporting procedures for threats detected
   - Compliance monitoring (e.g., alerting if AV is disabled)
   - Annual review and update process

2. **Implementation checklist:**
   - Inventory of all systems requiring malware protection
   - Select and license antivirus solution (e.g., Defender, CrowdStrike, Kaspersky, open-source alternatives)
   - Deploy agents to all in-scope systems
   - Enable auto-updates and real-time scanning
   - Configure alerting for detection events
   - Document baseline deployment and current coverage

3. **Evidence needed:**
   - Anti-malware policy document (signed approval)
   - Endpoint inventory with malware protection status
   - Screenshot/report showing:
     - Number of protected systems vs. total systems
     - Last signature update dates
     - Threat detection logs (from past 30–90 days)
     - Any quarantined items
   - Change records showing deployment timeline
   - Training/awareness records for staff on malware reporting

4. **Connection to other controls:**
   - A.8.16 (monitoring): configure alerts for malware detection
   - A.6.3 (awareness): train staff on phishing and malware risks
   - A.5.37 (documented procedures): document incident response for malware

**Audit Question:** "Describe your anti-malware strategy. Show me which systems have protection, when signatures were last updated, and any detection logs from recent months."

---

### 4. A.8.8 – Management of Technical Vulnerabilities (Patch Management Testing)
**Status:** 🟡 Partial
**Audit Risk:** MEDIUM – Process exists but lacks rigor
**Remediation Timeline:** 1 week

**Gap:** Patch management process is documented, but **no evidence of quarterly testing**.

**What needs to be implemented:**
1. **Formal Patch Testing Procedure:**
   - Define patch testing schedule: monthly or quarterly (recommend monthly for critical patches)
   - Require testing in non-production environment first (dev/test/staging)
   - Document test cases: system functionality, performance, backward compatibility
   - Define success criteria (system stability, no regression)
   - Approval and rollback procedures
   - Sign-off by patch manager and system owner

2. **Quarterly Test Evidence:**
   - Quarterly test report showing:
     - Patches tested (OS, applications, firmware)
     - Test environment and results
     - Any issues found and remediation
     - Approval and sign-off date
     - Deployment timeline for approved patches
   - Keep records for at least 12 months

3. **Vulnerability Assessment Integration:**
   - Document vulnerability scanning process (e.g., quarterly or semi-annual scans)
   - Map findings to patches available
   - Prioritize high/critical vulnerabilities for urgent patching
   - Track SLA for remediation (e.g., critical patches within 7 days)

4. **Evidence needed:**
   - Updated patch management policy with testing schedule
   - Q1 2026 patch test report (if already completed) or schedule for upcoming quarter
   - Sample patch deployment records showing testing step and approval
   - Vulnerability scan reports
   - Patch status dashboard or inventory

**Audit Question:** "Show me your patch testing schedule and the most recent test results. What is your SLA for patching critical vulnerabilities?"

---

### 5. A.8.15 – Logging (Formal Log Review Procedure)
**Status:** 🟡 Partial
**Audit Risk:** MEDIUM – Foundation is in place, but process is missing
**Remediation Timeline:** 1 week

**Gap:** Logging is enabled on servers, but **no formal procedure for log review and analysis**.

**What needs to be implemented:**
1. **Log Review Procedure document** including:
   - **What is logged:** System events, user activities, security events, access logs, application errors
   - **Log retention period:** Minimum 90 days; recommend 12 months for critical systems
   - **Log review frequency:** Daily, weekly, or monthly (recommend at least weekly for security logs)
   - **Who reviews logs:** Security team, system administrators, or SOC (if applicable)
   - **What to look for:** Unauthorized access attempts, privilege escalation, data exfiltration indicators, malware signatures, configuration changes
   - **Escalation procedure:** What to do if suspicious activity is detected
   - **Documentation:** Log review reports or checklists signed by reviewer and date

2. **Implementation checklist:**
   - Centralize logs (syslog server, SIEM, cloud logging) or schedule periodic collection
   - Configure log retention per policy
   - Create log review checklist/template
   - Assign reviewer roles and responsibilities
   - Schedule log review calendar (e.g., Mondays, 9 AM)
   - Set up alerting for critical events (failed login attempts, admin access, changes)

3. **Evidence needed:**
   - Log Review Procedure document (approved by management)
   - Sample log review reports from past 3 months showing:
     - Date and reviewer signature
     - Findings and actions taken
     - Any escalations to incident response
   - Log retention configuration (e.g., rsyslog config, SIEM settings)
   - Logs themselves (sample from past 30 days, redacted for confidential user data)
   - Description of log centralization solution (if used)

4. **Connection to other controls:**
   - A.8.16 (monitoring): log review feeds into system monitoring and alerting
   - A.5.28 (evidence collection): logs are critical forensic evidence
   - A.5.24–5.26 (incident management): logs trigger incident detection and response

**Audit Question:** "Show me your log review procedure and evidence that logs are reviewed regularly. What suspicious activity was detected in the past month?"

---

## Partial Implementation Gaps

| Control | Gap | Remediation |
|---------|-----|-------------|
| A.5.15 (Access Control) | No formal Access Control Policy document | Create policy defining access control rules, approval workflow, and review cycle. Reference in SoA. |
| A.5.16 (Identity Management) | No documented identity lifecycle procedures | Document procedures for user provisioning, role changes, and deprovisioning. Provide evidence of enforcement. |
| A.5.17 (Authentication Information) | No formal password/authentication policy | Create and enforce password policy (complexity, expiry, history). Document authentication standards. |
| A.5.18 (Access Rights) | No documented access review process | Establish annual (minimum) access review process. Conduct first review and document results. |
| A.8.3 (Information Access Restriction) | No documented mapping of classifications to access rules | Document access control matrix. Test and provide evidence of enforcement. |

---

## Remediation Priority Roadmap

### Week 1 (Immediate)
1. **A.8.32 – Change Management Policy** (1–2 days)
   - Draft and approve policy
   - Set up change request system
   - Train team on procedures
2. **A.8.2 & A.8.5 – MFA Implementation** (2–4 days)
   - Procure or configure MFA platform
   - Identify admin tools requiring MFA
   - Begin MFA rollout for top-priority systems
3. **A.8.15 – Log Review Procedure** (1 day)
   - Create log review procedure document
   - Assign reviewer roles
   - Execute first log review and document

### Week 2
1. **A.8.7 – Anti-Malware Policy & Deployment** (2–3 days)
   - Draft and approve anti-malware policy
   - Procure antivirus solution
   - Deploy to pilot set of systems
2. **A.8.8 – Patch Testing** (1 day)
   - Update patch management policy to include testing schedule
   - Plan and execute first quarterly patch test
3. **A.5.15–A.5.18 – Access Control Policies** (2–3 days)
   - Create Access Control Policy
   - Document identity management and authentication procedures
   - Schedule first access review

### Week 3–4
1. Complete MFA rollout to all admin tools
2. Complete malware protection deployment to all systems
3. Gather evidence and documentation for all controls
4. Conduct internal pre-audit review against all 11 controls

## Audit Preparation Summary

**Stage 2 Audit Scope:** Full ISMS evaluation, including all Annex A controls in scope.

**For Access Control & Operations Security themes, Stage 2 will verify:**
1. **Documentation:** All policies are formal, approved, and current
2. **Implementation:** Controls are deployed across all in-scope systems
3. **Evidence:** Records show controls are operating (logs, tickets, reviews)
4. **Effectiveness:** Sampling will test if controls prevent unauthorized access, system changes, malware, and provide audit trails

**Key Auditor Activities:**
- Review policies and procedures (Clause 5 & 8)
- Interview staff on roles and responsibilities
- Test access to a sample of systems (can they access what they shouldn't?)
- Review change management records (were changes tested and approved?)
- Review log analysis results (what suspicious activity was found and acted upon?)
- Test MFA on random admin accounts
- Verify patch testing for critical systems
- Confirm malware signatures are current on sampled endpoints

**Critical Success Factors for Passing Stage 2:**
1. All five critical gaps must be remediated and evidenced before audit
2. Partial implementations must have formal documentation and execution records
3. Process ownership and roles must be clear
4. Evidence must be traceable, dated, and signed off
5. Controls must demonstrate effectiveness (not just existence)

---

## Recommended Next Steps

1. **This week:** Assign owners to each of the five critical gaps
2. **By end of Week 1:** Complete change management policy, MFA rollout plan, and log review procedure
3. **By end of Week 2:** Anti-malware deployment, patch test execution, and access control policy
4. **By mid-April (before audit):** Complete all remediation, gather all evidence, and conduct internal pre-audit
5. **Pre-audit (2 weeks before Stage 2):** Run internal mock audit focusing on these 11 controls

---

## Questions for Your Compliance Team

Before finalizing this remediation plan, clarify:

1. **Change Management:** Who currently approves production changes? Is there a CAB, or is it ad-hoc approval by the CIO/engineering lead? Document their role in the policy.
2. **MFA Scope:** Which internal admin tools are in scope? (e.g., servers, cloud consoles, databases, network equipment, VPN). This defines the size of the MFA rollout.
3. **Logging:** Are logs currently centralized, or are they on individual systems? Do you have syslog, SIEM, or cloud logging (e.g., AWS CloudTrail)?
4. **Malware Protection:** What OS types need protection? (Windows, Linux, macOS). This affects which antivirus platform to choose.
5. **Patch Testing:** Is there a staging/test environment available for testing patches before production rollout?
6. **Access Control:** Is there an existing access management tool (e.g., Active Directory, Okta)? This simplifies identity lifecycle procedures.

---

## Conclusion

Your organization has a foundation of security controls but faces **5 critical gaps** and **6 partial implementations** in the Access Control and Operations Security themes. All gaps are remediable within 2–4 weeks with focused effort.

The critical gaps—**change management, MFA, anti-malware policy, formal log review, and patch testing**—directly impact audit readiness. Addressing these before Stage 2 will ensure a cleaner audit and reduce residual risk.

**Estimated Effort:** 60–80 hours of combined effort across security, IT operations, and compliance teams over 3–4 weeks.

**Expected Audit Outcome (post-remediation):** Stage 2 audit should result in minimal findings for these controls, assuming strong implementation and evidence of effectiveness.

Good luck with your Stage 2 audit preparation!

The remediation steps detail actions to take but do not include explicit statements like 'Evidence Required: [artifact list]' or 'Evidence Artifacts: [specific documents/logs]'. The closest implicit guidance appears in the remediation section structure, but lacks explicit evidence specification needed by auditors.
✓
Output provides remediation guidance or recommended actions for the identified gaps
Extensive remediation guidance provided for all major gaps. Each control gap includes 'Remediation Steps' section with phased approach: Immediate (0-30 days), Short-term (30-90 days), Medium-term (90-180 days). Examples: Lines 47-61 (Patch Management), Lines 97-116 (Anti-Malware), Lines 154-177 (Logging), Lines 217-240 (Change Management), Lines 279-304 (MFA). Additional Priority Remediation Roadmap (lines 337-363) provides 3-phase timeline with effort/cost estimates and specific tasks for each phase.
# ISO 27001:2022 Stage 2 Audit Gap Analysis
## Operations Security & Access Control Themes

**Audit Date:** 2026-03-25
**Audit Stage:** Stage 2 (Detailed Compliance Review)
**Scope:** Annex A Controls - Operations Security & Access Control Domains

---

## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

This organization demonstrates foundational security controls but has **significant compliance gaps** across five critical areas in the Operations Security and Access Control domains. Current implementation status shows 40% compliance with Stage 2 audit requirements. Remediation is required before certification can be achieved.

**Critical Finding Count:** 4
**Major Finding Count:** 3
**Minor Finding Count:** 2

---

## 1. PATCH MANAGEMENT ANALYSIS

### ISO 27001:2022 Control: A.8.2 (Configuration Management)
*Previously A.12.6.1 in ISO 27001:2013*

#### Current State
- Documented patch management process exists
- Process NOT tested quarterly (critical gap)
- No evidence of systematic testing cycles

#### Gap Analysis

| Gap Item | Requirement | Current State | Severity | Evidence |
|----------|-------------|--------------|----------|----------|
| Quarterly Testing | Regular testing of patches required before production deployment | Ad-hoc or no testing | **CRITICAL** | "not tested quarterly" |
| Test Environment | Dedicated test environment for patch validation | Not mentioned | **MAJOR** | Process may lack proper staging |
| Rollback Procedures | Documented rollback plans for failed patches | Not stated | **MAJOR** | Risk mitigation absent |
| Emergency Patches | Fast-track process for critical security patches | Not documented | **CRITICAL** | Vulnerability window exposed |
| Audit Trail | Complete logging of all patch activities | Not confirmed | **MAJOR** | Non-repudiation missing |

#### ISO Requirement Details
Control A.8.2 requires organizations to:
- Establish and maintain procedures for configuration management
- Ensure all changes are tested and documented
- Maintain baselines and configuration inventories
- Implement change control procedures

#### Remediation Steps
1. **Immediate (0-30 days):**
   - Establish quarterly patch testing schedule with documented calendar
   - Define test environment specifications and success criteria
   - Create patch testing checklist aligned to production systems

2. **Short-term (30-60 days):**
   - Document emergency patch escalation procedures
   - Implement automated patch testing in non-production environment
   - Establish rollback procedures and test them

3. **Medium-term (60-90 days):**
   - Implement patch management tooling with audit logging
   - Conduct first quarterly test cycle and document results
   - Review and adjust procedures based on findings

#### Risk Rating
**HIGH RISK** - Unpatched systems vulnerable to known CVEs. Quarterly testing requirement is auditable evidence of a systematic approach.

- Likely relying on ad-hoc endpoint protection
- No documented standards for malware protection deployment

| Detection & Response | Process for detected malware incidents | Not documented | **MAJOR** | Incident handling undefined |

#### ISO Requirement Details
Control A.8.7 requires organizations to:
- Implement technical and organizational measures against malware
- Provide user awareness and training
- Establish detection and response procedures
- Regular security updates and patches
- Monitoring and testing

#### Remediation Steps
1. **Immediate (0-15 days):**
   - Draft anti-malware policy covering:
     * All endpoints (workstations, servers, mobile devices)
     * Approved antivirus/anti-malware tools
     * Update frequency requirements (minimum daily for definitions)
     * Detection, containment, and eradication procedures
   - Identify all systems requiring protection

2. **Short-term (15-45 days):**
   - Approve policy and communicate to all stakeholders
   - Deploy standardized malware protection across all systems
   - Establish mail gateway scanning for incoming threats
   - Create incident response procedures for malware detection

3. **Medium-term (45-90 days):**
   - Implement centralized malware monitoring dashboard
   - Conduct vulnerability scans and remediate findings
   - Provide user training on malware prevention
   - Establish metrics and reporting for policy compliance

#### Risk Rating
**CRITICAL RISK** - Absence of formal policy indicates undefined security posture. Malware incidents could occur without documented response procedures.

## 3. LOGGING & LOG REVIEW PROCEDURES

### ISO 27001:2022 Control: A.8.4 (Logging)
*Previously A.12.4.1 in ISO 27001:2013*

#### Current State
- Logging enabled on servers (partial compliance)
- **No formal log review procedure documented**
- Likely no systematic log analysis or monitoring
- No clear retention or archival strategy

#### Gap Analysis

| Gap Item | Requirement | Current State | Severity | Evidence |
|----------|-------------|--------------|----------|----------|
| Log Review SOP | Formal documented procedure for log review | **ABSENT** | **CRITICAL** | Reactive not proactive monitoring |
| Review Frequency | Regular schedule (daily/weekly) | Not established | **CRITICAL** | Incidents may go undetected |
| Scope Coverage | All critical systems logging defined | Servers only (partial) | **MAJOR** | Incomplete visibility |
| SIEM/Monitoring | Centralized log aggregation and analysis | Not mentioned | **MAJOR** | Manual review unsustainable at scale |
| Incident Detection | Process to escalate suspicious logs | Not documented | **CRITICAL** | No alert mechanism |
| Log Retention | Defined retention periods per log type | Not mentioned | **MAJOR** | Compliance/forensics risk |
| Integrity | Tamper protection and integrity controls | Not confirmed | **MAJOR** | Non-repudiation missing |

#### ISO Requirement Details
Control A.8.4 requires organizations to:
- Implement comprehensive logging of user activities, system events, and security events
- Establish review procedures for logs to detect anomalies
- Protect logs from unauthorized access and modification
- Define retention schedules
- Maintain log integrity

#### Remediation Steps
1. **Immediate (0-30 days):**
   - Document formal log review procedure including:
     * Systems included in log review (servers, applications, firewalls, access systems)
     * Review frequency (minimum weekly for servers, daily for critical systems)
     * Review responsibilities and escalation path
     * Log retention periods (minimum 1 year for security logs)
   - Establish access controls for log systems (read-only for reviewers)

2. **Short-term (30-60 days):**
   - Extend logging beyond servers to include:
     * Network devices (firewalls, switches)
     * Access control systems (authentication, VPN)
     * Application logs (authentication, data access)
     * Administrative actions
   - Implement automated log aggregation (SIEM or log management tool)
   - Create alert rules for suspicious activities

3. **Medium-term (60-90 days):**
   - Establish regular log review schedule and document reviews
   - Implement dashboard for real-time log analysis
   - Conduct log review audit and remediate findings
   - Create log archival process with integrity controls
   - Train personnel on log review procedures

#### Risk Rating
**HIGH RISK** - Without formal log review procedures, security incidents may go undetected. This also impacts detection and response capabilities required by multiple controls.

- High risk of uncontrolled system modifications

| Change Log | Complete change documentation | Not mentioned | **CRITICAL** | No audit trail for changes |
| Testing Requirements | Changes tested before production | Not required | **MAJOR** | Risk of service disruption |
| Rollback Procedures | Documented rollback for failed changes | Not documented | **MAJOR** | Recovery not planned |
| Impact Assessment | Change impact analysis required | Not performed | **CRITICAL** | Unknown dependencies |
| Communication | Pre/post change notification | Not established | **MAJOR** | Stakeholder misalignment |
| Emergency Changes | Fast-track process for critical changes | Not defined | **MAJOR** | Response delays likely |

#### ISO Requirement Details
Control A.8.3 requires organizations to:
- Implement formal change management procedures
- Evaluate impact of changes on information systems
- Ensure changes are authorized before implementation
- Maintain complete records of changes
- Implement rollback procedures
- Test changes in appropriate environment before production

#### Remediation Steps
1. **Immediate (0-20 days):**
   - Draft change management policy covering:
     * Change categories (emergency, normal, standard)
     * Approval authorities and workflow
     * Change impact assessment requirements
     * Testing requirements before production
     * Documentation requirements
     * Rollback procedures
   - Define change advisory board or equivalent approval mechanism

2. **Short-term (20-50 days):**
   - Approve and publish change management policy
   - Establish change request template and process
   - Create change log/register for historical tracking
   - Define change windows and blackout periods
   - Implement change approval workflow (manual or tool-based)

3. **Medium-term (50-90 days):**
   - Implement change management tooling/system
   - Conduct training for all change stakeholders
   - Migrate historical changes to change log where possible
   - Implement automated notifications for changes
   - Establish change metrics and reporting
   - Conduct change management audit

#### Risk Rating
**CRITICAL RISK** - Absence of change management is a fundamental control failure. Uncontrolled changes can lead to service outages, security vulnerabilities, and compliance violations. This is often a mandatory finding in Stage 2 audits.

## 5. MULTI-FACTOR AUTHENTICATION GAP

### ISO 27001:2022 Control: A.9.2 (User access management)
*Previously A.9.2.1 in ISO 27001:2013*

#### Current State
- **No MFA on internal admin tools**
- Administrative access relies on username/password only
- High privilege accounts at significant risk
- Non-compliance with modern security practices

#### Gap Analysis

| Gap Item | Requirement | Current State | Severity | Evidence |
|----------|-------------|--------------|----------|----------|
| MFA Requirement | MFA required for administrative access | **NOT IMPLEMENTED** | **CRITICAL** | Privileged accounts exposed |
| Scope | All admin/privileged tool access | Absent | **CRITICAL** | Comprehensive gap |
| MFA Methods | Multiple approved MFA methods | Not defined | **MAJOR** | No flexibility for users |
| Enforcement | Mandatory for all admin users | Not enforced | **CRITICAL** | Optional implementation |
| Backup Methods | Backup authentication when MFA unavailable | Not documented | **MAJOR** | Access continuity undefined |
| User Training | Instruction on MFA use and troubleshooting | Not provided | **MAJOR** | User adoption barriers |
| Session Controls | Admin session timeout and re-authentication | Not confirmed | **MAJOR** | Session hijacking risk |

#### ISO Requirement Details
Control A.9.2 requires organizations to:
- Grant access rights based on need-to-know and job requirements
- Implement strong access controls for privileged accounts
- Use multi-factor authentication for administrative access
- Regular review and removal of access rights
- Establish user access procedures and responsibilities

#### Remediation Steps
1. **Immediate (0-15 days):**
   - Conduct inventory of all admin/privileged tools requiring MFA
   - Evaluate MFA solutions:
     * Hardware tokens (FIDO2 keys, smart cards)
     * Software tokens (authenticator apps)
     * Biometric (fingerprint, facial recognition)
     * SMS/email (less preferred but acceptable as backup)
   - Develop MFA implementation policy

2. **Short-term (15-45 days):**
   - Procure and configure MFA solution
   - Deploy MFA to critical admin tools (tier 1):
     * System administration consoles
     * Database administration interfaces
     * Cloud infrastructure management
     * Identity management systems
   - Provide user training and support

3. **Medium-term (45-90 days):**
   - Extend MFA to all administrative access (tier 2)
   - Implement conditional MFA (risk-based if possible)
   - Establish MFA backup/recovery procedures
   - Create dashboard for MFA adoption tracking
   - Document MFA in policies and procedures
   - Conduct MFA audit and validate compliance

#### Risk Rating
**CRITICAL RISK** - Absence of MFA on admin tools is a significant vulnerability. Compromised admin credentials could lead to full system compromise. This finding is typically highlighted in external audit reports.

# ACCESS CONTROL POLICY
## TechNova Ltd — ISO 27001:2022 Compliance

**Document Control**
| Attribute | Value |
|-----------|-------|
| Version | 1.0 |
| Author | Information Security Team |
| Approved By | Chief Information Security Officer / Board |
| Effective Date | 2026-03-25 |
| Next Review Date | 2027-03-25 |
| Classification | Confidential - Internal Use Only |

---

## 1. PURPOSE

This Access Control Policy establishes TechNova Ltd's requirements and procedures for managing logical and physical access to information systems, data, and facilities. The policy ensures that:

- Only authorized personnel can access systems and information appropriate to their role
- Access is provisioned on a principle of least privilege (PoLP)
- Privileged access is protected with enhanced controls
- Remote access is secure and monitored
- User identities are verified and access rights are regularly reviewed
- Compliance with ISO 27001:2022 Clause 8.1 and Annex A controls A.5.15 (Access Control), A.5.16 (Identity Management), A.5.17 (Authentication), and A.5.18 (Access Rights) is demonstrated

---

## 2. SCOPE

This policy applies to:

- All TechNova Ltd employees, contractors, temporary staff, and third-party users
- All information systems, applications, and data repositories (on-premises and cloud)
- All privileged access (administrative, root, superuser, database administrator, cloud administrator)
- All remote access to TechNova networks and systems
- All physical access to facilities containing IT equipment or sensitive information

**Exclusions:** This policy does not cover third-party infrastructure managed by external providers, except where TechNova retains contractual access rights (covered under Supplier Security Policy).

---

## 3. POLICY STATEMENTS

### 3.1 User Access Management

**3.1.1 Principle of Least Privilege (PoLP)**
- Users shall be granted the minimum level of access required to perform their assigned role and responsibilities
- Access rights shall be formally documented and periodically verified against job responsibilities
- Access shall be restricted to systems, applications, and data strictly necessary for role performance
- Generic or shared user accounts are prohibited; all access must be traceable to an individual user identity
- Temporary access or elevated access for specific projects shall be time-bound with automatic expiration

**3.1.2 User Provisioning**
- New user access requests must be submitted by the user's manager or HR department using the formal Access Request Form
- The request must clearly state the user's role, systems/applications required, and business justification
- All requests must be approved by the user's manager and the Information Security Manager before provisioning
- Access provisioning must be completed within 5 business days of approved request
- A provisioning checklist must be completed and retained with the access record
- Users must sign an acknowledgment confirming receipt of the Acceptable Use Policy before access is granted

**3.1.3 Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)**
- All systems shall implement Role-Based Access Control where technically feasible
- Predefined roles (e.g., Developer, Analyst, Manager, Admin) shall align with organizational functions
- Roles shall be documented with associated permissions, systems, and data classifications
- Users shall be assigned to roles; permissions flow from role membership, not individual assignments
- Periodic role reviews (at least annually) shall verify that role definitions remain current and appropriate

**3.1.4 User Offboarding**
- Upon employment termination or role change, HR shall notify IT within 1 business day
- All system access shall be disabled within 1 business day of notification
- All access credentials, tokens, and API keys shall be revoked or rotated
- All equipment (laptops, phones, access cards) shall be retrieved before final departure
- Offboarding checklist must be completed and signed by IT and the departing employee
- Shared account passwords shall be changed by a manager or IT after access removal

---

### 3.2 Privileged Access Management (PAM)

**3.2.1 Definition & Scope**
Privileged access includes:
- Operating system administrator (root, SYSTEM) accounts
- Database administrator and read-all database accounts
- Cloud platform administrator roles (AWS IAM Admin, Azure Owner, GCP Editor, etc.)
- Application administrative accounts with system-wide configuration rights
- Network device administrator accounts
- Email system administrator accounts
- Backup and recovery system administrator accounts

**3.2.2 Privileged Account Management**
- All privileged accounts shall be centrally managed and monitored
- Privileged account credentials shall be stored in a dedicated vault (e.g., CyberArk, HashiCorp Vault, AWS Secrets Manager)
- Vaults shall be encrypted, access-logged, and restricted to authorized personnel only
- Privileged accounts shall NOT be used for daily operational work; a separate standard user account must be used
- System service accounts (e.g., SQL Server Agent, Application Server) must have unique, complex passwords rotated quarterly
- No hardcoded credentials in configuration files, code repositories, or documentation

**3.2.3 Privileged Access Justification**
- Every privileged account must have explicit business justification documented in the access control system
- Privileged access requests require dual approval: technical manager + security manager
- Justifications must be reviewed annually and renewed with full approval workflow
- Ad-hoc or temporary privileged access requires written authorization with expiration date (maximum 72 hours for emergency access)

**3.2.4 Privileged Activity Monitoring**
- All privileged account activities shall be logged to a centralized, tamper-proof logging system
- Logs shall capture commands, file changes, configuration modifications, user creation/deletion, and privilege escalations
- Privileged session recordings (for remote administrative sessions) shall be retained for 90 days minimum
- Real-time alerting shall notify security team of suspicious privileged activities (e.g., mass file deletion, privilege escalation)
- Logs shall be reviewed by Information Security team at least weekly for anomalies
- Evidence of log review shall be documented and retained

**3.2.5 Privileged Account Segregation**
- Separate privileged accounts shall be created for different system roles (e.g., database admin, web server admin, network admin)
- Privileged accounts shall not be shared across systems or environments
- Development, testing, and production environments shall have separate privileged accounts
- Personal privileged accounts shall not be reused across different organizations or projects

---

### 3.3 Remote Access Controls

**3.3.1 Remote Access Authorization**
- Remote access shall only be granted to authorized personnel with documented business justification
- Remote access requests must identify the systems/applications accessed, access frequency, and expected duration
- All remote access must be approved by the user's manager and Information Security
- Remote access is granted on a role-based or need-basis; permanent remote access is reviewed annually
- Contractors and third-party suppliers must have signed agreements explicitly permitting remote access

**3.3.2 VPN Requirements**
- All remote access to TechNova networks must use a company-provided, authenticated VPN
- VPN clients must support multi-factor authentication (MFA)
- VPN access shall enforce role-based network segmentation (VPN users access only required networks/systems)
- VPN session logs shall be retained for 90 days minimum and monitored for unauthorized access attempts
- VPN clients must be kept updated to the latest patch level; automatic updates are strongly encouraged

**3.3.3 Endpoint Security for Remote Workers**
- Remote access devices (laptops, tablets, phones) must be approved by IT and registered in the device inventory
- Personal devices used for work access must have:
  - Approved mobile device management (MDM) or endpoint protection software installed
  - Device encryption enabled
  - Screen lock (PIN/biometric) with 5-minute timeout
  - Up-to-date operating system and security patches
- Non-compliant devices shall be blocked from VPN access until remediated
- Remote workers must use company-provided WiFi or wired connections; public WiFi access to company systems is prohibited

**3.3.4 Remote Session Management**
- Idle remote sessions shall automatically lock or disconnect after 15 minutes of inactivity
- Remote session duration limits shall be enforced (maximum 12 hours per session for non-privileged users)
- Privileged remote sessions shall have lower duration limits (maximum 4 hours) and require fresh authentication
- Session recordings or keystroke logging shall be enabled for all privileged remote access
- Users must explicitly close remote sessions; automatic logoff shall occur at the end of business day or after timeout

**3.3.5 Prohibited Remote Access Scenarios**
- Shared remote access credentials are prohibited
- Unencrypted remote access protocols (Telnet, HTTP, FTP) are prohibited; only encrypted alternatives (SSH, HTTPS, SFTP) are permitted
- Screen sharing or remote desktop tools that are not approved by IT are prohibited
- Personal VPN or proxy services are prohibited for accessing company systems
- Remote access to production systems without monitoring/logging is prohibited

---

### 3.4 Password and Authentication Requirements

**3.4.1 Password Policies**
- Minimum password length: 12 characters for standard users, 16 characters for privileged accounts
- Password complexity: Must contain uppercase, lowercase, numeric, and special characters
- Password history: System shall enforce that last 8 passwords cannot be reused
- Password expiration: 90 days for standard users; 60 days for privileged accounts
- Password age enforcement: System shall enforce password change if user attempts to use expired password
- Initial passwords issued by IT shall be temporary and must be changed on first login

**3.4.2 Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA)**
- MFA is mandatory for:
  - All remote access (VPN, remote desktop, cloud portals)
  - All administrative access to critical systems
  - All access to financial systems or sensitive data repositories
  - All email and collaboration platform access
  - All cloud platform consoles
  - All privileged account access
- MFA methods supported: TOTP (Time-Based One-Time Password), hardware security keys, push notifications via mobile app, SMS (lower priority, used only if others unavailable)
- MFA shall not be removable or disabled by end users; only IT can modify MFA settings with documented justification
- Backup MFA codes shall be stored securely (encrypted vault) and issued only in controlled manner for account recovery

**3.4.3 Credential Management**
- Users shall not share passwords, MFA codes, or authentication tokens with other users
- Passwords shall not be written down, shared via email, or stored in unencrypted files
- Password managers (company-approved solutions only, e.g., Bitwarden, 1Password with company controls) may be used
- Service account passwords and API keys must be stored in a secrets management system, not in code or config files
- Developers shall use personal access tokens (PATs) or temporary credentials instead of hardcoded passwords for code repositories

**3.4.4 Failed Authentication & Account Lockout**
- Systems shall implement account lockout after 5 failed authentication attempts within 15 minutes
- Locked accounts shall be automatically unlocked after 30 minutes or by IT administrator intervention
- Failed authentication attempts shall be logged with timestamp, username, IP address, and system name
- Security team shall review failed authentication logs at least weekly for signs of brute-force attacks
- Users shall be notified of multiple failed login attempts to their registered contact email

---

### 3.5 Access Review Procedures

**3.5.1 Periodic Access Reviews**
- All user access rights shall be reviewed at least annually, or more frequently if:
  - User role changes or responsibilities shift
  - Risk assessment identifies elevated risk for a system or function
  - Organizational structure changes (department reorganization, management changes)
  - Following any security incident involving unauthorized access
- Access reviews shall be performed by Information Security Manager and the user's direct manager
- Review scope: verify that each user's system access aligns with current role and business justification

**3.5.2 Manager Attestation Process**
- Quarterly (or at defined intervals), each user's manager shall receive a summary of that user's assigned access rights
- Manager must actively confirm (attest to) that:
  - The user still requires the listed access
  - Access aligns with the user's current role and responsibilities
  - No unauthorized or inappropriate access is present
- Attestation shall be documented in writing (email or system) and retained for audit purposes
- If manager cannot confirm, access shall be suspended pending investigation and formal review

**3.5.3 Privileged Access Reviews**
- Privileged account and privileged access rights shall be reviewed at least quarterly
- Review must verify that:
  - Each privileged account still has valid business justification
  - No unused privileged accounts exist in production systems
  - Privileged account activity logs show appropriate usage patterns
  - No inactive privileged accounts have been left enabled beyond 60 days
- Privileged Access Management (PAM) system reports shall provide audit trail of all privileged access during review period

**3.5.4 Dormant Account Management**
- User accounts that have not been used (no login) for 60 consecutive days shall be flagged as dormant
- Dormant accounts shall be disabled after 90 days of inactivity
- Before disabling, IT shall attempt to contact the account owner or manager to confirm the account is no longer needed
- Account data (mailbox, file shares) shall be retained for 180 days after disabling before archival or deletion
- Dormant accounts shall not be deleted permanently without documented retention period expiration and manager approval

**3.5.5 Access Rights Removal (Deprovisioning)**
- Upon employee termination, department transfer, or role change, the user's manager shall formally notify IT
- IT shall disable access within 1 business day and document the removal in the access control system
- System owners shall verify removal from their respective systems and confirm to IT
- Removal must be tracked with timestamp, authorizing manager, and IT staff member who performed removal
- Evidence of removal shall be retained with the access control record for audit purposes

**3.5.6 Access Review Documentation**
- All access reviews shall be documented and retained for minimum 3 years
- Documentation shall include:
  - Date of review
  - Systems/applications reviewed
  - Users reviewed
  - Reviewer name and signature
  - Findings (no changes needed, access removed, access modified)
  - Any exceptions or risks identified
  - Follow-up actions and due dates

---

### 3.6 Access Control for Specific User Categories

**3.6.1 Contractors and Temporary Staff**
- Contractor access shall be provisioned with explicit end date (contract end date)
- Contracts shall require contractor acknowledgment of access control and security policies
- Contractor access shall be limited to specific systems and data required for contracted work
- Contractor system access shall be included in quarterly access reviews and automatically disabled at contract end
- Contractor credential and equipment retrieval shall be tracked and documented

**3.6.2 Third-Party Suppliers and Vendors**
- Supplier access to TechNova systems shall be governed by signed Supplier Security Addendum
- Supplier accounts shall be marked in the system as "supplier" and subject to additional monitoring
- Supplier access shall be restricted to agreed-upon systems and timeframes
- Supplier activity shall be logged and reviewed by TechNova security team
- Supplier access shall be reviewed annually and can be revoked with 30 days' notice

**3.6.3 Privileged Access for Development/Testing**
- Non-production (development/test) environments may have relaxed access controls compared to production
- However, privileged account management (segregation, vault storage, monitoring) shall be applied consistently
- Development team members may have privileged access to development systems; this does NOT extend to production
- Separate privileged accounts must be used for production access, even by the same individual
- Code repositories shall not contain production credentials; use environment variables or secrets management systems

**3.6.4 API Access and Service-to-Service Authentication**
- Applications and services accessing other systems via API shall use authenticated service accounts or API tokens
- API tokens shall be generated with minimal required permissions
- API tokens shall be rotated at least annually; tokens for sensitive APIs shall be rotated quarterly
- API tokens shall be stored in secrets management system, not in code or logs
- API access shall be monitored and logged; unusual API activity shall trigger alerts

---

### 3.7 Access Control System Requirements

**3.7.1 System Capabilities**
- Access control system (directory service, identity management platform, PAM system) must support:
  - User identity and attributes (name, role, department, manager)
  - Role-based access control (RBAC) definitions and membership
  - Temporal constraints (access start/end dates, time-of-day restrictions)
  - Multi-factor authentication integration
  - User provisioning and deprovisioning workflows
  - Access request and approval workflows
  - Audit logging of all access changes
  - Reporting and access review capabilities
- System must be redundant with automatic failover to ensure availability during access management emergencies

**3.7.2 Identity Provider Integration**
- Directory service (e.g., Active Directory, Azure AD, Okta) shall be the authoritative source of user identity
- Applications and systems shall integrate with directory service for authentication and user attributes
- Directory service changes (employee hire, role change, termination) shall be synchronized to connected systems within 4 hours
- Manual access provisioning to systems not integrated with directory shall be completed within 1 business day of directory change

**3.7.3 Audit Logging & Monitoring**
- All access provisioning and removal actions shall be logged with:
  - Timestamp
  - User affected
  - Access right or system
  - Requested by (name and ID)
  - Approved by (name and ID)
  - Action taken (grant, modify, revoke)
  - Reason/justification
- Access control system logs shall be backed up daily and retained for minimum 1 year
- Logs shall be protected against unauthorized modification (immutable or protected) and shall not be stored on the same system
- All access to the access control system itself shall be logged and monitored

---

## 4. ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES

| Role | Responsibility |
|------|-----------------|
| **Chief Information Security Officer (CISO)** | Approve access control policy; define access control standards; oversee PAM program; approve exceptions and deviations |
| **Information Security Manager** | Administer access control system; process access requests; conduct access reviews; monitor privileged activity; investigate access anomalies |
| **System Owners** | Define access requirements for their systems; approve or reject access requests; participate in access reviews; ensure appropriate access in their systems |
| **Managers/Supervisors** | Request access for their team; approve/deny access requests from direct reports; attest to access reviews; request access removal upon employee termination |
| **IT Help Desk** | Receive access requests and route to appropriate approvers; provision approved access; assist with password resets; support onboarding/offboarding |
| **IT Operations** | Maintain access control systems; manage directory service; implement technical controls; provide audit logs; support system integrations |
| **Database Administrators** | Manage database access and privileges; provision database accounts; review database user access; manage database monitoring |
| **Network Administrators** | Manage VPN access; control network segmentation; monitor remote access logs; configure network access controls |
| **Compliance/Audit** | Verify access control policy compliance; conduct internal audits; support external audits; maintain compliance evidence |

---

## 5. PROCEDURES AND CONTROLS

### 5.1 Access Request Process

**Initiation:**
1. Employee or manager submits Access Request Form to IT Help Desk
2. Form shall include: user name, user role/department, systems/applications needed, data classification level, business justification, manager approval

**Approval:**
3. IT Help Desk routes request to System Owner and Information Security Manager for approval
4. System Owner verifies technical feasibility and appropriateness; approves or rejects
5. Information Security Manager verifies request aligns with policy and role; approves or rejects
6. CISO approval required for privileged access, elevated access, or exceptions to policy
7. Email confirmation sent to requester and manager upon approval

**Provisioning:**
8. IT implements approved access in system(s); generates provisioning checklist
9. Confirmation email sent to user confirming access provisioned and access details
10. New user completes mandatory security training and signs Acceptable Use Policy
11. Access request record filed with date, approvals, and confirmation

**Timeline:** Standard requests completed within 5 business days of approval

### 5.2 Access Modification Process

When a user's role changes or access requirements change:
1. Manager submits Access Modification Form describing required changes
2. Form reviewed and approved by Information Security Manager and System Owner
3. Old access revoked and new access provisioned; documented in access control system
4. Manager and user notified of changes

### 5.3 Access Removal Process

Upon employee termination, contract end, or role change:
1. HR/Manager notifies IT of separation or role change with effective date
2. IT creates Offboarding Checklist for all known systems and access
3. Access disabled within 1 business day in all systems
4. Equipment (laptop, phone, access card, VPN token) retrieved and documented
5. User mailbox and file shares placed in retention mode; archived after 180 days if not restored
6. Offboarding checklist signed by IT and manager; filed with separation record

### 5.4 Quarterly Access Review Process

**Q1, Q2, Q3, Q4 each year:**
1. Information Security Manager generates access report for each department
2. Report sent to department manager with list of all users and their access rights
3. Manager reviews and attests in writing that access is appropriate and current
4. Manager flags any access that should be removed or modified
5. Information Security Manager implements changes based on manager feedback
6. Access review documentation completed and filed
7. CISO reviews summary of changes and signs off on compliance

### 5.5 Privileged Access Review Process

**Quarterly (every 3 months):**
1. Information Security Manager generates Privileged Access Report
2. Report includes all privileged accounts, last activity, and justification review date
3. Technical managers (database, system, network) review and verify necessity
4. Unused or unjustified privileged accounts flagged for removal discussion
5. PAM system activity logs reviewed for anomalies (unusual commands, off-hours access, data exfiltration signs)
6. Findings documented and presented to CISO

---

## 6. EXCEPTIONS AND DEVIATIONS

- Exception requests must be submitted in writing to the CISO with business justification
- CISO shall document the exception, approval date, and expiration date (maximum 1 year)
- All exceptions require compensating controls that mitigate the risk of non-compliance
- Exceptions shall be reviewed at least annually
- Exception register maintained and reported to the Board quarterly

**Example exception scenario:** A critical legacy system does not support MFA. Compensating control: the system is accessible only from a hardened, segregated network with additional logging and monitoring.

---

## 7. TRAINING AND AWARENESS

- All new employees receive access control training as part of onboarding (covers Acceptable Use Policy, password security, MFA)
- Annual security awareness training includes section on access controls, data classification, and handling
- Managers receive training on access control responsibilities (request approval, access reviews, offboarding)
- IT staff receive specialized training on access control systems, PAM, and incident response related to access
- Compliance and audit teams receive training on access control policy verification
- Training completion tracked and reported annually to CISO

---

## 8. COMPLIANCE AND AUDITING

**Internal Audits:**
- Annual internal audit of access control policy compliance (scope: all mandatory elements)
- Audit examines sample of user access for appropriateness and least privilege
- Audit verifies access reviews were completed and documented
- Audit tests access provisioning and removal timelines
- Audit reviews privileged account management and PAM logs

**External Audits:**
- ISO 27001 certification audits include review of access control policy and implementation
- Auditors examine evidence of compliance: access reviews, approval records, audit logs, exception registers
- Auditors may test user access by requesting evidence of access request and approval

**Key Audit Questions:**
- Can we demonstrate that each user's access is justified and appropriate to their role?
- Are privileged accounts properly managed, monitored, and segregated?
- Are access changes (provisioning and removal) timely and documented?
- Are access reviews performed regularly with documented evidence?
- Are failed authentication attempts and suspicious access monitored and investigated?

---

## 9. NON-COMPLIANCE AND INCIDENTS

**Investigation:**
- When a user is found to have unauthorized or inappropriate access, investigation initiated immediately
- Investigation documents how unauthorized access occurred, what data was accessed, and duration
- Responsible parties (approver, system owner) interviewed to understand root cause

**Remediation:**
- Unauthorized access removed immediately
- User notified and potentially disciplined per HR policy (up to termination for severe violations)
- Controls reviewed and strengthened to prevent recurrence
- If data theft or unauthorized disclosure occurred, incident response procedure initiated

**Reporting:**
- All access control policy violations reported to CISO within 24 hours
- Severe violations (potential data breach, malicious intent) reported to management and legal
- Violations categorized and trended to identify systemic issues
- Management review includes access control compliance metrics

---

## 10. TECHNICAL CONTROLS

This policy is supported by the following technical controls:

| Control | System/Tool | Purpose |
|---------|-------------|---------|
| Identity Management | Azure AD or Active Directory | Central user identity, authentication, provisioning |
| Privileged Access Management | CyberArk, HashiCorp Vault, or equivalent | Secure storage of privileged credentials, session recording, activity monitoring |
| Multi-Factor Authentication | Okta, Microsoft Entra, or TOTP apps | Enforce MFA for remote and privileged access |
| VPN Access | Cisco AnyConnect, Fortinet, or equivalent | Secure remote access with encryption and authentication |
| Role-Based Access Control | RBAC in directory service and applications | Role membership determines system access |
| Endpoint Protection | Microsoft Defender, CrowdStrike, or equivalent | Malware detection, device compliance enforcement |
| Security Information & Event Management (SIEM) | Splunk, ELK Stack, or cloud equivalent | Centralized logging, alerting, investigation of access anomalies |
| Audit Logging | Built into all systems and AD | Immutable records of access changes and user activity |
| Secrets Management | AWS Secrets Manager, Azure Key Vault, HashiCorp Vault | Secure storage of API keys, service account credentials, database passwords |

## 14. APPENDICES

### Appendix A: Glossary of Terms

- **Access Control** — Limiting who can access which systems, data, or facilities
- **Least Privilege** — Granting users only the minimum access required to perform their role
- **Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA)** — Authentication using two or more independent verification methods
- **Privileged Access** — Administrative or elevated access capable of modifying systems, configurations, or data
- **Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)** — Access control model where permissions are assigned to roles, and users are assigned to roles
- **Segregation of Duties** — Ensuring that no single user can perform a critical transaction from start to finish (e.g., approve and execute a payment)
- **Shared Account** — Account used by multiple people (prohibited unless justified and heavily monitored)
- **Single Sign-On (SSO)** — Technology allowing users to authenticate once and gain access to multiple systems
- **Vault** — Secure, encrypted storage for credentials and secrets
- **VPN** — Virtual Private Network; encrypted tunnel for secure remote access
