# Target Organizational Profile: Regional Healthcare Network
## NIST CSF 2.0 — Implementation Tier 3 (Repeatable)

---

## Executive Summary

This document defines a **Target Organizational Profile** for a regional healthcare network (hypothetical 5-facility system with ~2,500 clinical staff and 1,500 administrative users) operating at **NIST CSF 2.0 Implementation Tier 3 (Repeatable)**. The profile focuses on two foundational functions:

- **Govern (GV)**: Establishing and monitoring cybersecurity risk management strategy and organizational governance
- **Identify (ID)**: Understanding cybersecurity risks to assets, systems, and data

This profile is designed for an organization that has moved beyond ad-hoc risk management (Tier 1) and informal risk-informed practices (Tier 2), and now operates with **formally approved, organization-wide cybersecurity policies and consistently applied risk management processes**.

---

## Organizational Context

### Business Profile
- **Industry**: Healthcare (regional delivery network)
- **Scope**: 5 acute-care hospitals, multiple clinics, centralized EHR system
- **Critical Assets**: Electronic health records (EHRs), patient identity data, medical devices (diagnostics, infusion pumps, ventilators), telemedicine infrastructure
- **Regulatory Environment**: HIPAA Security Rule, HITRUST CSF, state healthcare board requirements
- **Mission-Critical Objectives**: Ensure patient safety through continuous system availability; protect patient privacy; support clinical decision-making; maintain provider trust
- **Workforce**: Clinicians (nurses, physicians, technicians), IT/security staff, administrative personnel; varying cybersecurity awareness

### Risk Tolerance & Appetite
At Tier 3, the organization articulates explicit risk tolerance statements:
- **Data confidentiality**: Low tolerance for unauthorized access to PHI; encryption of data at-rest and in-transit is mandatory
- **Availability**: Medium-low tolerance; clinical systems require 99.5% uptime; administrative systems 99% uptime
- **Integrity**: Low tolerance; audit trails required for all PHI changes; cryptographic verification of critical data
- **Supply chain**: Medium risk tolerance; third-party EHR vendors and cloud healthcare providers are managed with formal assessment and monitoring protocols

---

## GOVERN (GV) Function — Target Profile

### Overview
The Govern function establishes the cybersecurity governance structures, policies, and risk management strategy that inform all other functions. At **Tier 3**, governance is **formalized, approved organization-wide, and consistently enforced**.

---

### Category: GV.OC — Organizational Context

Understanding the circumstances surrounding the organization's cybersecurity risk management decisions.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Organizational mission informs cybersecurity risk management** | GV.OC-01 | Fully Implemented | Mission statement explicitly defines regulatory obligations (HIPAA, HITRUST), patient safety criticality, and technology dependencies. Cybersecurity governance committee formally maps mission to risk priorities quarterly. |
| **Internal and external stakeholders' cybersecurity needs are understood and considered** | GV.OC-02 | Fully Implemented | Formal stakeholder analysis (clinicians, IT, compliance, board, vendors) conducted annually. Requirements documented in governance charter. Feedback loops established (e.g., incident surveys, clinician advisory groups). |
| **Legal, regulatory, and contractual cybersecurity requirements are understood and managed** | GV.OC-03 | Fully Implemented | Comprehensive regulatory mapping: HIPAA Security Rule controls → CSF subcategories; HITRUST v9.4 controls → CSF; state data breach notification laws. Compliance gaps tracked in centralized register; remediation plans approved by legal and compliance leadership. |
| **Critical objectives and services stakeholders depend on are understood and communicated** | GV.OC-04 | Fully Implemented | Formal documentation of Crown Jewels: EHR availability, medication administration systems, diagnostic imaging systems, emergency department operations. Recovery Time Objectives (RTOs) and Recovery Point Objectives (RPOs) defined per system and approved by clinical leadership. Communicated in governance policy and annually refreshed. |
| **Outcomes and services the organization depends on are understood and communicated** | GV.OC-05 | Fully Implemented | Supply chain inventory: cloud infrastructure providers (EPIC EHR hosting), internet connectivity vendors, medical device vendors, laboratory information systems. Dependencies mapped to business continuity; risks recorded and monitored through formal third-party risk program. |

---

### Category: GV.RM — Risk Management Strategy

Establishing organizational priorities, risk tolerance and appetite statements, and assumptions to inform operational decisions.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Risk management objectives established and agreed by stakeholders** | GV.RM-01 | Fully Implemented | Annual risk management objectives approved by Board Risk Committee: e.g., "Achieve 95% remediation of high-risk vulnerabilities within 90 days," "Maintain clinical system uptime ≥99.5%," "Reduce third-party risk assessment cycle to 6 months." Aligned with business strategy. |
| **Risk appetite and tolerance statements established, communicated, and maintained** | GV.RM-02 | Fully Implemented | Formal risk appetite statements per risk category: PHI access (low appetite), system downtime (low-medium appetite), third-party compromise (medium appetite). Published in governance policy; reviewed annually. All staff trained on risk tolerance thresholds. |
| **Cybersecurity risk management activities included in enterprise risk management** | GV.RM-03 | Fully Implemented | Cybersecurity risks consolidated into enterprise risk register (alongside clinical, operational, financial risks). Cybersecurity risk metrics (e.g., remediation metrics, incident rates) reported to Board Risk Committee quarterly. ESG/risk committees aligned. |
| **Strategic direction describing appropriate risk response options is established and communicated** | GV.RM-04 | Fully Implemented | Risk response strategy framework: Avoid, Mitigate, Transfer (insurance), Accept. Documented policy specifies when each approach applies (e.g., "PHI breaches avoided; operational risk mitigated through controls; liability transferred through cyber insurance"). Communicated in governance handbook. |
| **Lines of communication established for cybersecurity risks, including supplier risks** | GV.RM-05 | Fully Implemented | Formal communication channels: Executive steering committee (monthly), operational risk forums (weekly), vendor escalation protocol. Supplier incidents reported through formal intake process; tracked in centralized incident/risk register. Board/audit committee briefed on systemic risks quarterly. |
| **Standardized method for calculating, documenting, categorizing, and prioritizing cybersecurity risks is established and communicated** | GV.RM-06 | Fully Implemented | CVSS v3.1 scoring adopted organization-wide for vulnerability severity. Risk matrix (likelihood × impact) used consistently across threat, vulnerability, and third-party assessments. Risk scores drive remediation prioritization; methodology documented in Cybersecurity Risk Assessment Procedure. All staff trained annually. |
| **Strategic opportunities (positive risks) included in cybersecurity risk discussions** | GV.RM-07 | Fully Implemented | Annual strategy review considers positive risks: e.g., "adoption of zero-trust architecture reduces insider threat exposure and enables future operational agility." Opportunities documented in strategic roadmap; resourced as strategic initiatives. |

---

### Category: GV.RR — Roles, Responsibilities, and Authorities

Establishing cybersecurity roles and accountability structures to foster continuous improvement.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Organizational leadership is responsible and accountable for cybersecurity risk** | GV.RR-01 | Fully Implemented | Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) reports directly to Chief Information Officer (CIO) with dotted line to Board Audit Committee. CISO performance metrics in annual objectives; included in executive compensation committee agenda. Board Chair, CEO, and department heads sign annual cybersecurity governance acknowledgment. |
| **Cybersecurity roles, responsibilities, and authorities are established, communicated, understood, and enforced** | GV.RR-02 | Fully Implemented | RACI matrix (Responsible, Accountable, Consulted, Informed) documented for all GV, ID, PR, DE, RS, RC functions. Roles defined across: CISO, IT Security Manager, Network/Infrastructure owners, Clinical IT liaisons, Incident Commander, Third-Party Risk Manager, Privacy Officer. Responsibilities published in role descriptions and governance policy; signed acknowledgment required at hire and annually. |
| **Adequate resources allocated commensurate with risk strategy and roles** | GV.RR-03 | Fully Implemented | Annual budget cycle allocates dedicated resources to cybersecurity: FTE count (CISO, 3 security engineers, 1 risk analyst), tooling (SIEM, vulnerability scanner, endpoint detection and response [EDR]), training. Resource allocation justified through risk assessment findings; approved by CFO and Board. |
| **Cybersecurity included in human resources practices** | GV.RR-04 | Fully Implemented | HR policies updated: cybersecurity clearance required for clinical IT roles; annual security awareness training mandatory for all staff; security competency evaluation in IT staff annual reviews; termination procedures include account deprovisioning checklist reviewed by security. Background checks include reference to previous cybersecurity incidents. |

---

### Category: GV.PO — Policy

Establishing, communicating, and enforcing organizational cybersecurity policies.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Policy for managing cybersecurity risks is established, communicated, and enforced** | GV.PO-01 | Fully Implemented | Comprehensive Cybersecurity Governance Policy (approved by Board, effective organization-wide) covers: risk tolerance, roles/responsibilities, accountability, escalation, external communication, policy review schedule. Mandatory annual attestation by all staff. Non-compliance tracked and escalated; disciplinary procedures in place for violations. |
| **Policy reviewed, updated, communicated, and enforced to reflect changes** | GV.PO-02 | Fully Implemented | Formal annual policy review cycle (calendar Q4); change control process for emergency updates. Updates communicated via email, intranet, lunch-and-learns. Staff trained on changes; attestation renewed. Previous policy versions retained in audit archive. |

---

### Category: GV.OV — Oversight

Using performance outcomes to adjust risk management strategy.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Cybersecurity risk management strategy outcomes are reviewed to inform and adjust strategy** | GV.OV-01 | Fully Implemented | Quarterly governance review (Board Risk Committee) of key metrics: incident frequency/severity, vulnerability remediation timeliness, risk posture changes, third-party risk events. Strategy adjustments proposed and documented; changes communicated to all relevant stakeholders. |
| **Risk management strategy reviewed and adjusted to ensure coverage of organizational requirements and risks** | GV.OV-02 | Fully Implemented | Annual comprehensive strategy review cross-references new regulatory requirements, threat landscape changes (monitored through threat intelligence subscriptions), emerging technology risks (e.g., AI/ML security implications). Gap analysis performed; strategy updated and re-approved. |
| **Organizational cybersecurity risk management performance is evaluated and reviewed for adjustments** | GV.OV-03 | Fully Implemented | Performance dashboard (CISO KPIs): asset coverage, vulnerability closure rate, incident response time, compliance audit findings, training completion rates. Reviewed monthly by leadership; quarterly by Board. Underperforming metrics trigger root cause analysis and corrective actions. |

---

### Category: GV.SC — Cybersecurity Supply Chain Risk Management

Managing supply chain cybersecurity risks across all suppliers and third parties.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Supply chain risk management program, strategy, and processes established and agreed** | GV.SC-01 | Fully Implemented | Formal Third-Party Risk Management Program with charter, objectives, and governance. Program includes: assessment methodology, monitoring schedule, escalation process. Reviewed and approved annually by Board. |
| **Cybersecurity roles and responsibilities for suppliers, customers, and partners are established and communicated** | GV.SC-02 | Fully Implemented | Supplier Cybersecurity Requirements Document specifies expectations: incident notification timelines (24 hours for critical incidents), HITRUST certification (for EHR vendors), annual penetration testing, audit rights for cloud infrastructure providers. Responsibilities incorporated into master service agreements (MSAs). |
| **Supply chain risk management integrated into cybersecurity and enterprise risk management processes** | GV.SC-03 | Fully Implemented | Supplier risk scores incorporated into overall organizational risk register. Supplier incidents trigger threat modeling for potential cascade impact. Supplier risk assessment findings inform Protect, Detect, Respond capabilities (e.g., monitoring third-party network traffic, incident response coordination). |
| **Suppliers are known and prioritized by criticality** | GV.SC-04 | Fully Implemented | Supplier inventory maintained in centralized register with criticality ratings: Tier 1 (mission-critical: EHR vendor, cloud infrastructure) → annual assessment; Tier 2 (important: network equipment, medical device vendors) → biennial; Tier 3 (standard: office equipment) → on-demand. Risk-based prioritization guides assessment frequency and depth. |
| **Cybersecurity requirements established and integrated into supplier contracts** | GV.SC-05 | Fully Implemented | Standard security clauses in all new contracts: data protection obligations, incident notification, audit rights, security certification requirements. Legal review checklist ensures compliance. SLAs for incident response (e.g., "Critical incidents acknowledged within 4 hours"). |
| **Planning and due diligence performed before entering supplier relationships** | GV.SC-06 | Fully Implemented | Pre-vendor assessment checklist: HITRUST or ISO 27001 certification verification, security questionnaire (CSF alignment), reference checks from peer organizations, proof of cyber liability insurance. Documentation retained; findings tracked in risk register. |
| **Supplier risks understood, recorded, prioritized, assessed, responded to, and monitored** | GV.SC-07 | Fully Implemented | Annual supplier security assessment (HITRUST audit, security questionnaire, breach history check) for Tier 1 vendors. Findings documented in supplier risk scorecard. Remediation plans for gaps tracked with due dates. Continuous monitoring: automated alerts for vendor breach disclosures. |
| **Suppliers included in incident planning, response, and recovery activities** | GV.SC-08 | Fully Implemented | Supplier incident response procedure defines escalation (e.g., if EHR vendor incident affects availability). Incident response team includes supplier liaison role. Suppliers participate in annual tabletop exercises; communication templates pre-established. |
| **Supply chain security practices integrated into cybersecurity and enterprise risk management programs** | GV.SC-09 | Fully Implemented | Supplier security metrics (e.g., mean time to acknowledge a vulnerability report) reported to governance committee quarterly. Supplier incidents trigger post-incident reviews and process improvements. New supplier technologies (e.g., cloud expansion) trigger risk assessment. |
| **Supply chain risk management plans include provisions for end-of-relationship activities** | GV.SC-10 | Fully Implemented | Contract exit clauses mandate: data return/destruction procedures, credential revocation timeline (24-48 hours), knowledge transfer period (30-60 days). Decommissioning checklist tracked by IT; sign-off by security and legal. |

---

## IDENTIFY (ID) Function — Target Profile

### Overview
The Identify function enables organizations to understand their cybersecurity risks to systems, assets, data, and people. At **Tier 3**, risk identification, assessment, and improvement are **consistent, documented, and regularly reviewed**.

---

### Category: ID.AM — Asset Management

Identifying, inventorying, and prioritizing assets based on organizational risk and mission criticality.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Inventories of hardware are maintained** | ID.AM-01 | Fully Implemented | Comprehensive hardware inventory (servers, workstations, medical devices, network equipment) maintained in configuration management database (CMDB). Discovery tools (network scanning, asset tagging) used to validate inventory quarterly. Lifecycle tracking: procurement → deployment → decommissioning. Inventory accuracy ≥95%. |
| **Inventories of software, services, and systems are maintained** | ID.AM-02 | Fully Implemented | Application inventory includes: EHR (EPIC), laboratory information system (LIS), pharmacy system, medical imaging (PACS), telemedicine platform, email, collaboration tools. For each: version, deployment locations, owner, criticality, SLA. Automated software discovery tools (e.g., endpoint detection and response [EDR]) supplement manual tracking. Updates tracked; sunset versions identified. |
| **Network communication and data flow representations are maintained** | ID.AM-03 | Fully Implemented | Network architecture diagrams (L2/L3) updated annually. Data flow diagrams for critical systems (EHR, medical devices) show: data sources, intermediaries, destinations, encryption status. Network segmentation documented (e.g., clinical network, administrative network, guest network). Firewall rules mapped to data flows. |
| **Inventories of services provided by suppliers are maintained** | ID.AM-04 | Fully Implemented | Supplier services inventory: vendor name, service (cloud hosting, software licensing, managed security), contract start/end dates, criticality, data processed, security certifications. Reviewed annually; changes flagged for risk reassessment. Integration points with internal systems documented. |
| **Assets prioritized based on classification, criticality, and mission impact** | ID.AM-05 | Fully Implemented | Asset classification scheme: Tier 1 (critical to patient safety or PHI security: EHR, medical devices), Tier 2 (important but not immediately critical: administrative systems, office productivity), Tier 3 (standard: development systems, test networks). Priority informed by HIPAA risk assessment, clinical workflow dependencies, and regulatory requirements. Criticality reviewed annually. |
| **Inventories of data and corresponding metadata are maintained** | ID.AM-07 | Fully Implemented | Data inventory identifies: data types (PHI, financial, operational), location (database, file share, cloud), volume, classification (confidential, internal), retention period, owner. PHI inventory aligned with HIPAA Security Rule requirements. Metadata includes: creation date, last accessed, change history. Quarterly validation; undocumented data sources identified through scanning. |
| **Systems, hardware, software, services, and data are managed throughout their life cycles** | ID.AM-08 | Fully Implemented | Lifecycle management policy defines: procurement (security evaluation), configuration (hardening standards), operation (patching schedule, monitoring), and decommissioning (data destruction, certification). Change management process tracks all transitions. Maintenance windows communicated to clinical leadership; downtime impacts assessed. |

---

### Category: ID.RA — Risk Assessment

Understanding cybersecurity risks through systematic identification and analysis of threats, vulnerabilities, and impacts.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Vulnerabilities in assets are identified, validated, and recorded** | ID.RA-01 | Fully Implemented | Automated vulnerability scanning (quarterly or monthly for critical assets): network vulnerability scanner, application-level scanning, medical device inventory scans. Manual penetration testing (annually for Tier 1 systems). Vulnerability management workflow: identified → assessed for false positives → prioritized (CVSS v3.1) → tracked to remediation. SLA: high-severity vulnerabilities remediated within 30 days; critical within 15 days. |
| **Cyber threat intelligence is received and analyzed from sharing forums and sources** | ID.RA-02 | Fully Implemented | Threat intelligence subscriptions: healthcare ISACs (H-ISAC), vendor alerts (Microsoft, EPIC), public threat feeds (CVE databases, Shodan). CISO or security analyst reviews daily and triages to relevant teams (e.g., "new vulnerability in EHR plugin" → clinical IT team). High-impact threats escalated to leadership within 24 hours. Threat intelligence integrated into risk assessments and audit planning. |
| **Internal and external threats are identified and recorded** | ID.RA-03 | Fully Implemented | Annual risk assessment documents threats: external (ransomware targeting healthcare, supply chain compromise, DDoS), internal (insider threat, configuration error, inadequate access controls). Threat scenarios developed for each asset criticality level. Assessed threats recorded in risk register with likelihood and impact ratings. Assessment reviewed quarterly for new threat emergence. |
| **Potential impacts and likelihoods of threats exploiting vulnerabilities are identified and recorded** | ID.RA-04 | Fully Implemented | For each material vulnerability: impact assessed (business continuity, PHI exposure, patient safety risk) and likelihood estimated (based on threat data, asset exposure). Risk scores (impact × likelihood) calculated using standard methodology (GV.RM-06). Example: "Unpatched EHR vulnerability with public exploit (high likelihood) + patient safety impact (critical) = Critical risk requiring immediate remediation." |
| **Threats, vulnerabilities, likelihoods, and impacts are used to understand inherent risk and inform response priorities** | ID.RA-05 | Fully Implemented | Consolidated risk register (threats × vulnerabilities) reviewed monthly by operations and security teams. Top 20 risks escalated to governance committee quarterly. Risk scores directly drive remediation prioritization: critical risks addressed within 2 weeks; high within 30 days. Risk trends analyzed to identify systemic issues (e.g., "medical device vendors with poor patching practices"). |
| **Risk responses are chosen, prioritized, planned, tracked, and communicated** | ID.RA-06 | Fully Implemented | Risk response strategy (GV.RM-04) guides selection: patch/update (mitigate), compensating controls (mitigate), isolate system (avoid), accept with monitoring. Responses documented in action plan: owner, target completion, success criteria. Progress tracked in monthly dashboard; risks exceeding SLA flagged for escalation. Status communicated monthly to relevant stakeholders (clinical leadership for availability risks, compliance for regulatory risks). |
| **Changes and exceptions are managed, assessed for risk impact, recorded, and tracked** | ID.RA-07 | Fully Implemented | Formal change control process for all systems and infrastructure: impact assessment (does this affect risk profile?), security review (does this introduce new risks?), approval, implementation, testing. Risk exception tracking: if a vulnerability can't be patched (e.g., legacy medical device incompatibility), exception request documents risk acceptance by business owner and security leadership, with monitoring plan and re-assessment schedule (annual or sooner if conditions change). |
| **Processes for receiving, analyzing, and responding to vulnerability disclosures are established** | ID.RA-08 | Fully Implemented | Vendor disclosure program: security researchers can report vulnerabilities through disclosure@organization.health. Intake process: triage for severity, assignment to vendor liaison, tracking through resolution. SLA: critical vendor disclosures acknowledged within 24 hours; coordinated disclosure timeline (30-90 days) respected. Public disclosure coordinated with vendor and regulatory notifications. Post-disclosure root cause analysis conducted. |
| **Authenticity and integrity of hardware and software are assessed prior to acquisition and use** | ID.RA-09 | Fully Implemented | Procurement security checklist includes: software license verification, checksum validation against vendor source, malware scanning of installation media, vendor identity verification (pre-authorization). Hardware: manufacturer authenticity verified; supply chain provenance checked (e.g., "did this device transit through high-risk geography?"). Critical systems (EHR servers) undergo additional integrity validation at deployment. |
| **Critical suppliers are assessed prior to acquisition** | ID.RA-10 | Fully Implemented | Pre-acquisition security assessment for Tier 1 suppliers (>$500K contract or PHI access): HITRUST audit results, security questionnaire responses, reference calls, public breach history check, financial stability review (Dun & Bradstreet). Assessment findings documented; gaps require remediation timeline in contract. Annual re-assessments of active critical suppliers. |

---

### Category: ID.IM — Improvement

Identifying and managing improvements to cybersecurity processes and capabilities across all functions.

#### Target Subcategories and Tier 3 Implementation:

| Subcategory | ID | Target State | Tier 3 Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Improvements are identified from evaluations** | ID.IM-01 | Fully Implemented | Annual cybersecurity program evaluation (self-assessment against CSF 2.0 subcategories): maturity scoring (0-5 scale), gap identification, improvement recommendations. External audit every 2-3 years (HITRUST or SOC 2 audit) provides third-party validation. Evaluation findings documented in improvement roadmap with prioritization and resource allocation. |
| **Improvements are identified from security tests and exercises** | ID.IM-02 | Fully Implemented | Annual penetration testing: external (network and web application), internal (post-compromise scenario), physical (badge cloning, tailgating). Tabletop exercises: incident response scenarios (quarterly), supply chain disruption (annual). Post-test reports document findings; remediation plans tracked. Exercise participants trained on identified gaps; training priorities updated. |
| **Improvements are identified from operational execution** | ID.IM-03 | Fully Implemented | Operational improvements tracked through: monthly security metrics dashboard (patch compliance, vulnerability closure rate, access review completion), incident post-mortems (every incident reviewed within 5 business days), control effectiveness monitoring (e.g., failed authentication attempts, unauthorized data access attempts). Improvement ideas from frontline staff (security hotline) solicited and reviewed. Top improvements resourced in quarterly planning. |
| **Incident, vulnerability, and other findings are communicated to designated stakeholders** | ID.IM-04 | Fully Implemented | Communication plan per finding type: security incidents → incident response team immediately, clinical leadership within 2 hours; high-risk vulnerabilities → patching team, relevant system owners within 24 hours; compliance audit findings → leadership and Board within governance reporting cycle; improvement recommendations → governance committee quarterly. Feedback loop ensures stakeholder awareness and accountability. |

---

## Tier 3 (Repeatable) Characteristics Applied to GV + ID

### What Tier 3 Means for This Healthcare Network:

| Dimension | Tier 3 Characteristic | Applied to Healthcare Network |
|---|---|---|
| **Risk Management Process** | Risk management practices are formally approved and expressed as policy. Cybersecurity practices regularly updated based on risk management processes and changing threat/technology landscape. | Cybersecurity governance policy Board-approved; annual updates required. Risk assessment process standardized (CVSS v3.1, risk matrix methodology); conducted annually for all assets and third parties. Vulnerability management SLAs enforced; metrics tracked. Threat intelligence systematically integrated into risk decisions. |
| **Integrated Risk Management Program** | Organization-wide approach to managing cybersecurity risk. Risk-informed policies, processes, and procedures are defined, implemented as intended, and reviewed. Consistent methods to respond to changes in risk. Personnel possess knowledge/skills for appointed roles. | All staff required to complete annual cybersecurity training; clinical IT staff specialized training quarterly. Cybersecurity risk metrics reported to Board quarterly; integrated into enterprise risk management. Policies consistently enforced (non-compliance escalated). Incident response, asset management, vulnerability management procedures documented and regularly tested. |
| **External Participation** | Organization understands dependencies and dependents; contributes to community understanding of risks. Collaborates with and receives information from supply chain partners. | Formal third-party risk program: all Tier 1 suppliers assessed pre-contract and monitored annually. Suppliers included in incident response planning and tabletop exercises. Participation in healthcare ISACs and threat intelligence sharing. Incident coordination protocols established with key vendors. |

---

## Implementation Priorities and Quick-Wins for Healthcare Network at Tier 3

### Maintain and Strengthen (Already Tier 3):
1. **GV.OC-01 to GV.OC-05**: Refresh organizational context documentation annually (mission, stakeholders, regulatory obligations, critical services).
2. **GV.RM-01 to GV.RM-07**: Review risk management objectives, appetite statements, and risk response strategy quarterly; update based on threat landscape and incident learnings.
3. **GV.RR-01 to GV.RR-04**: Conduct annual cybersecurity effectiveness evaluation; ensure roles/responsibilities alignment with organizational structure; allocate resources to address capability gaps.
4. **ID.AM-01 to ID.AM-08**: Maintain asset inventory accuracy (≥95%) through quarterly discovery scans and lifecycle tracking; prioritize critical assets (Tier 1 medical devices, EHR systems).
5. **ID.RA-01 to ID.RA-10**: Execute vulnerability management program to SLA (critical within 15 days, high within 30 days); conduct annual penetration testing; assess critical suppliers pre-contract and annually.

### Advance Toward Tier 4 (Continuous Improvement):
1. **GV.OV-01 to GV.OV-03**: Add real-time risk dashboards; shift from quarterly to monthly governance reviews.
2. **GV.SC-01 to GV.SC-10**: Enhance supplier risk monitoring with continuous data feeds (e.g., automated breach alerts); shift to quarterly supply chain risk committee reviews.
3. **ID.IM-01 to ID.IM-04**: Formalize a continuous improvement program with monthly metrics reviews and quarterly strategic planning; capture lessons learned systematically.
4. **Threat Intelligence**: Move from reactive to predictive: subscribe to healthcare-specific threat feeds; conduct quarterly threat modeling exercises.

---

## Conclusion

A regional healthcare network implementing NIST CSF 2.0 at **Tier 3 (Repeatable)** establishes formal, organization-wide cybersecurity governance and consistently applies risk management processes. This profile emphasizes:

- **Governance excellence**: Board-approved policies, defined roles, enterprise risk integration
- **Systematic risk understanding**: Asset inventories, vulnerability management, threat intelligence
- **Supplier accountability**: Formal third-party risk program with annual assessments and incident coordination
- **Organizational consistency**: Standardized methodologies, documented procedures, regular testing and training
- **Continuous monitoring and improvement**: Metrics-driven oversight, post-incident reviews, annual strategic evaluation

Achieving Tier 3 positions the healthcare network to support patient safety through reliable systems, protect patient privacy through systematic data safeguards, and maintain clinical leadership confidence through transparent, risk-informed cybersecurity governance.

# Target Organisational Profile: Regional Healthcare Network
## Implementation Tier 3 - Govern & Identify Functions

---

## Executive Summary

This Target Organisational Profile establishes cybersecurity and risk management objectives for a regional healthcare network implementing the NIST Cybersecurity Framework (CSF) at Implementation Tier 3. Tier 3 represents a Standards-Based approach where the organisation applies a mix of industry standards, best practices, and customised processes adapted from established frameworks. This profile focuses on the critical Govern (GV) and Identify (ID) functions essential for healthcare operations.

---

## Organisation Context

**Sector:** Healthcare (Regional Network)
**Target Implementation Tier:** Tier 3 (Standards-Based)
**Scope:** Multi-facility network with diverse IT infrastructure
**Key Considerations:**
- HIPAA and HITECH Act compliance
- Patient data protection and privacy
- Operational continuity for critical health services
- Integration of legacy and modern systems
- Regulatory oversight requirements

---

## Implementation Tier 3 Definition

Tier 3 (Standards-Based) represents an organisation that:
- **Has established policies and processes** based on industry standards and frameworks
- **Uses defined risk management approaches** adapted from established methodologies
- **Applies structured governance** with documented roles and responsibilities
- **Implements standardised controls** from recognised frameworks (NIST SP 800-53, ISO 27001, HIPAA Security Rule)
- **Monitors and reviews** compliance and performance through defined metrics
- **Coordinates across functions** with documented communication and collaboration
- **Updates practices regularly** based on emerging threats and organisational changes
- **Maintains documentation** of risk decisions and control implementations
- **Balances security with operations** through formalised trade-off analysis

---

## Govern (GV) Function - Tier 3 Profile

### Governance Structure (GV-ST)

**Target Subcategory: GV-ST-01 - Organizational Context**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish documented governance framework aligned with industry standards
- Define organisational mission, objectives, and risk tolerance in writing
- Document healthcare-specific regulatory requirements (HIPAA, state privacy laws)
- Map strategic objectives to cybersecurity and risk management priorities
- Establish cross-functional steering committee with representation from clinical, IT, compliance, and administrative leadership
- Review and update governance documentation annually
- Ensure cybersecurity strategy is visible in IT and operational strategic plans

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create documented information security strategy aligned with NIST CSF
- Establish Healthcare Information Security Committee (HISC)
- Define risk tolerance for patient safety, data breach, and operational disruption
- Map regulatory requirements to specific framework functions and categories

---

**Target Subcategory: GV-ST-02 - Roles, Responsibilities, and Authorities**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish formal role definitions with clear cybersecurity responsibilities
- Document decision-making authorities and escalation paths
- Define accountability for risk management decisions
- Create explicit security roles in job descriptions
- Establish data classification authority and ownership structure
- Communicate roles across the organisation through training and documentation
- Review and update role definitions as infrastructure and threats evolve

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Appoint Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) reporting to CIO/IT Director
- Define security officer roles at each major facility
- Establish data steward roles for clinical and administrative data
- Document escalation procedures for security incidents
- Create matrix of approval authorities for security exceptions and changes

---

**Target Subcategory: GV-ST-03 - Policies, Procedures, and Processes**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Develop comprehensive written policies adapted from industry standards
- Ensure policies address regulatory requirements and organisational context
- Document standard operating procedures (SOPs) for key security processes
- Include information security, data protection, and incident response procedures
- Make policies available and understandable to all personnel
- Include disciplinary measures and enforcement mechanisms
- Review and update policies at least annually or when regulations change
- Maintain audit trail of policy changes and approvals

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create Information Security Policy Framework covering:
  - Access control and authentication
  - Data classification and handling
  - Incident reporting and response
  - Acceptable use of IT resources
  - Password and credential management
  - Mobile device and remote access
  - Vendor and third-party management
- Develop SOPs for critical processes:
  - Access provisioning and deprovisioning
  - Vulnerability scanning and patch management
  - Backup and disaster recovery
  - Investigation and containment procedures
- Establish annual policy review calendar
- Document enforcement actions and lessons learned

---

### Risk and Oversight (GV-RO)

**Target Subcategory: GV-RO-01 - Risk Management Program**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish formal risk management program based on recognised framework (NIST RMF, ISO 31000)
- Define risk assessment methodology adapted from industry standards
- Document risk tolerance and appetite for the organisation
- Conduct risk assessments at least annually or when significant changes occur
- Maintain risk register with documented risk treatments
- Assign ownership for each identified risk
- Communicate risk information to relevant stakeholders
- Review and update risk assessments based on monitoring results

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Adopt NIST Risk Management Framework (RMF) tailored for healthcare
- Create risk assessment procedure covering:
  - Asset inventory and criticality classification
  - Threat analysis based on healthcare-specific threat landscape
  - Vulnerability assessments using standardised tools
  - Impact analysis considering patient safety, operations, and compliance
  - Risk scoring using defined probability and impact matrices
- Establish risk registers at:
  - Enterprise level (strategic risks)
  - Business unit level (operational risks)
  - System level (technical risks)
- Document risk treatment decisions:
  - Risk acceptance with documented justification
  - Risk mitigation through controls
  - Risk avoidance through changes to operations
  - Risk transfer through insurance or outsourcing
- Conduct quarterly risk register reviews

---

**Target Subcategory: GV-RO-02 - Oversight and Accountability**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish formal oversight mechanisms for cybersecurity and risk management
- Create governance committee structure with documented charters
- Define metrics and KPIs for security posture and risk management
- Conduct regular reporting to senior management and board level
- Establish performance measurement and monitoring processes
- Review metrics at least quarterly for effectiveness and trending
- Ensure accountability for risk decisions and control implementation
- Document oversight activities and decisions

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Establish Board-level Cybersecurity/Risk Committee:
  - Quarterly reporting on:
    - Critical risks and risk trend analysis
    - Significant incidents or near-misses
    - Regulatory compliance status
    - Security metrics and KPI trends
    - Capital and budget needs for security programs
    - Emerging threats and required adaptations
- Create Management-level Security Steering Committee:
  - Monthly meetings reviewing:
    - Incident status and trends
    - Vulnerability and patch management status
    - Risk assessment findings
    - Control effectiveness metrics
    - Changes to policies and procedures
    - Training and awareness program effectiveness
- Establish Key Performance Indicators (KPIs):
  - Incident detection time
  - Mean time to remediation (MTTR)
  - Vulnerability scan coverage and remediation rate
  - Access review completion rate
  - Training completion percentage
  - Policy compliance assessment scores
  - Number of active risks and risk trend

---

## Identify (ID) Function - Tier 3 Profile

### Asset Management (ID-AM)

**Target Subcategory: ID-AM-01 - Inventory and Control of Assets**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Maintain comprehensive inventory of hardware, software, and data assets
- Use standardised asset management tools or processes
- Document asset ownership and classification
- Include end-of-life processes for asset retirement
- Reconcile inventory periodically (semi-annually minimum)
- Track asset location and physical custody
- Document configuration baselines for critical assets
- Maintain audit trail of inventory changes

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Implement IT asset management system covering:
  - Hardware inventory:
    - Servers and network devices
    - Workstations and laptops
    - Medical devices and biomedical equipment
    - Mobile devices (phones, tablets, wearables)
    - Peripherals and accessories
  - Software inventory:
    - Operating systems and versions
    - Applications and versions
    - Licenses and compliance tracking
    - Open-source components
  - Data asset inventory:
    - Databases and data repositories
    - File shares and storage locations
    - Electronic health record (EHR) systems
    - Medical imaging repositories
    - Administrative data systems
- Document asset attributes:
  - Owner (individual or department)
  - Location and physical custody
  - Business criticality
  - Sensitivity classification
  - Maintenance and support status
  - Configuration baseline
- Establish asset retirement procedures:
  - Data sanitization standards (NIST SP 800-88)
  - Device decommissioning process
  - Certificate of destruction documentation
- Conduct inventory reconciliation:
  - Physical inventory verification annually
  - System-generated reports monthly
  - Discrepancy investigation and resolution
  - Documentation of unaccounted assets

---

**Target Subcategory: ID-AM-02 - Software Platforms and Applications**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Maintain inventory of software platforms and applications
- Document business purpose and operational criticality
- Track software licensing and support status
- Identify and monitor deprecated software versions
- Document application dependencies and data flows
- Include vendor and third-party applications
- Implement controls for authorised vs. unauthorised software
- Establish baseline configurations for common platforms

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create software inventory including:
  - Clinical applications (EHR, PACS, Laboratory Information System, Pharmacy)
  - Administrative applications (billing, HR, payroll)
  - Infrastructure software (databases, middleware, web servers)
  - Communication tools (email, messaging, collaboration)
  - Security tools (antivirus, EDR, firewalls, identity management)
- Document for each software:
  - Vendor name and support status
  - Current version and end-of-support date
  - Business owner and primary users
  - Critical data accessed or processed
  - Known vulnerabilities or compatibility issues
  - License type and compliance status
  - Integration dependencies
- Establish software baseline configurations:
  - Approved versions with security patches
  - Hardening standards aligned with CIS Benchmarks
  - Disabled unnecessary services and features
  - Audit and logging configuration requirements
- Implement application whitelisting/management:
  - Define authorised software for each device type
  - Monitor and alert on unauthorised software execution
  - Escalate non-compliant applications for review

---

**Target Subcategory: ID-AM-03 - Data and Information**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish data classification scheme aligned with healthcare requirements
- Document data types and sensitivity levels
- Identify and inventory data repositories and data flows
- Define handling requirements for each classification level
- Track data ownership and stewardship
- Document data retention and disposal requirements
- Include personally identifiable information (PII) and protected health information (PHI)
- Implement data discovery tools for shadow IT detection

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create data classification framework:
  - **Public:** Non-sensitive healthcare information, general organisational communications
  - **Internal:** Organisational data with limited external risk (internal policies, operational data)
  - **Confidential:** PHI, PII, clinical information, financial/administrative sensitive data
  - **Restricted:** Highly sensitive data requiring maximum protection (genetic information, substance abuse records, psychiatric data)
- Establish data handling requirements by classification:
  - **Access Control:** Limitation to authorised personnel with business need
  - **Encryption:** In-transit and at-rest encryption requirements
  - **Transmission:** Secure transmission channels and approval requirements
  - **Retention:** Minimum and maximum retention periods
  - **Disposal:** Sanitization and destruction standards
  - **Audit Logging:** Logging levels and monitoring requirements
- Identify and document data repositories:
  - EHR systems and related clinical databases
  - Medical imaging repositories (PACS)
  - Laboratory and radiology information systems
  - Billing and claims systems
  - Medical records storage (paper and electronic)
  - Backup and archival systems
  - Communication systems (email, messaging)
- Create data flow diagrams showing:
  - Data sources and origination points
  - Processing and transformation locations
  - Storage locations (primary and backup)
  - Access points and users
  - Data sharing with external entities
  - Data destruction/disposal endpoints
- Assign data stewards:
  - Clinical data steward (Chief Medical Information Officer or designee)
  - Administrative data steward (Finance/Operations)
  - IT data steward (Technology/IS leadership)
  - Each system owner responsible for detailed data governance
- Conduct data discovery assessments:
  - Scan file shares and repositories for unclassified data
  - Identify shadow IT and unauthorised data stores
  - Review cloud usage and external data repositories
  - Assess structured and unstructured data

---

### Business Environment (ID-BE)

**Target Subcategory: ID-BE-01 - Organisational Context**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Document healthcare network structure and relationships
- Identify key business processes and criticality
- Document dependencies (internal and external)
- Define operational requirements and constraints
- Identify critical suppliers and service providers
- Assess third-party relationships and data flows
- Document regulatory and legal requirements
- Review and update business context annually

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Document organisational structure:
  - Facility locations and operational models
  - Clinical departments and service lines
  - Administrative divisions
  - IT infrastructure and operations
  - External relationships (affiliated entities, partners)
- Identify critical business processes:
  - **Emergency Services:** 24/7 availability requirement
  - **Surgical Services:** Scheduled operations, pre-operative coordination
  - **Medication Management:** Pharmacy operations and medication dispensing
  - **Patient Monitoring:** Continuous monitoring systems (ICU, telemetry)
  - **Diagnostic Services:** Laboratory and imaging services
  - **Medical Records:** Access to patient history and documentation
  - **Communication:** Internal coordination and external coordination
- Document dependencies:
  - Interdependencies between clinical systems
  - Dependencies on external vendors and cloud services
  - Communication infrastructure dependencies
  - Power and cooling infrastructure
  - Internet connectivity requirements
- Define operational requirements:
  - Availability requirements (uptime percentages, RTO targets)
  - Performance requirements (response times, throughput)
  - Scalability requirements (user load, data volume growth)
  - Compliance requirements (HIPAA, state laws, accreditation)
  - Interoperability requirements (EHR integration, care coordination)
- Identify critical suppliers:
  - EHR and clinical software vendors
  - Medical device manufacturers
  - Telecommunications providers
  - Cloud service providers
  - Security and monitoring service providers
  - Managed service providers
- Document third-party relationships:
  - Data shared (type, volume, sensitivity)
  - Service dependencies and criticality
  - Security requirements and obligations
  - Audit and compliance rights
  - Incident notification and response procedures

---

**Target Subcategory: ID-BE-02 - Supply Chain Relationships**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish formal vendor management program
- Document security requirements in contracts
- Assess vendor security posture and controls
- Monitor vendor compliance with security obligations
- Include incident notification and response requirements
- Document business continuity and disaster recovery arrangements
- Conduct regular vendor assessments and re-assessments
- Maintain records of vendor security evaluations

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create vendor management framework:
  - Vendor on-boarding process:
    - Security questionnaire completion
    - Assessment of security controls and certifications
    - Contract review for security obligations
    - Verification of insurance and liability coverage
    - References and background checks
  - Categorize vendors by criticality:
    - **Critical:** Direct access to systems, data, or infrastructure
    - **High:** Important services with potential security impact
    - **Medium:** Supporting services with limited direct impact
    - **Low:** Minimal security impact or redundant services
- Define security contract requirements:
  - Data protection and confidentiality obligations
  - HIPAA Business Associate Agreement (BAA) requirements
  - Incident notification and response procedures
  - Audit and compliance rights
  - Data breach liability and notification requirements
  - Subcontractor management and oversight
  - Term and termination conditions
  - Data return and destruction requirements
- Establish vendor assessment procedures:
  - Security questionnaires adapted for healthcare sector
  - Reviews of security certifications (SOC 2, ISO 27001)
  - Assessment of controls aligned with NIST CSF
  - Incident history and response capability
  - Financial stability and business continuity arrangements
  - Incident and vulnerability disclosure practices
- Document vendor monitoring:
  - On-site assessments for critical vendors (annually)
  - Questionnaire updates for ongoing reassessment
  - Incident tracking and trending
  - Contractual compliance monitoring
  - Performance metrics and KPIs
  - Regular communication and relationship management
- Address business continuity:
  - Backup plans for critical services
  - Disaster recovery procedures and testing
  - Redundancy arrangements
  - Communication during outages
  - Recovery time objectives (RTO) and recovery point objectives (RPO)

---

### Risk Assessment (ID-RA)

**Target Subcategory: ID-RA-01 - Risk Assessment Process**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Establish documented risk assessment methodology
- Apply systematic approach to identify threats and vulnerabilities
- Assess risk at multiple levels (enterprise, business unit, system, process)
- Include both qualitative and quantitative analysis
- Document assumptions and methodologies
- Use industry-standard risk assessment frameworks
- Conduct assessments at least annually
- Update assessments when significant changes occur
- Maintain assessment documentation and evidence

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Create risk assessment framework:
  - Align with NIST RMF and CSF
  - Reference healthcare-specific threat models
  - Incorporate lessons from healthcare sector incidents
  - Address regulatory compliance requirements
- Develop risk assessment methodology:
  - **Asset Identification:** Inventory of systems, data, and infrastructure
  - **Threat Analysis:**
    - Healthcare sector threats (ransomware, insider threats, phishing)
    - Technology-specific threats (unpatched systems, weak authentication)
    - Environmental threats (natural disasters, power failures)
    - Human threats (user error, malicious insiders)
  - **Vulnerability Assessment:**
    - Technical vulnerability scanning
    - Configuration review against security baselines
    - Application security testing
    - Physical security assessment
  - **Impact Analysis:**
    - Patient safety impact
    - Operational disruption impact
    - Financial impact
    - Regulatory/compliance impact
    - Reputation impact
  - **Risk Scoring:** Probability × Impact matrix with defined scale
- Establish risk assessment scope:
  - Enterprise-level strategic risk assessment
  - Business unit/functional area assessments
  - System-level risk assessments for critical applications
  - Process-level assessments for high-risk operations
- Implement risk assessment tools:
  - Vulnerability scanning tools (Nessus, Qualys)
  - SIEM tools for threat analysis
  - Risk assessment software (Archer, LogicGate)
  - Network analysis and mapping tools
- Document assessment outcomes:
  - Risk register with all identified risks
  - Risk scoring and prioritization
  - Risk treatment decisions and rationale
  - Risk owner assignments
  - Monitoring and review schedules
  - Evidence of assessment (scans, interviews, documentation)

---

**Target Subcategory: ID-RA-02 - Threat and Vulnerability Identification**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Conduct regular threat and vulnerability identification activities
- Use multiple methods (scanning, testing, intelligence, assessment)
- Include external and internal threat perspectives
- Document known and emerging threats relevant to healthcare
- Assess vulnerabilities at multiple levels (infrastructure, application, process)
- Prioritize threats and vulnerabilities based on exploitability and impact
- Monitor threat intelligence from industry sources
- Track vulnerability status and remediation progress

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Establish threat identification activities:
  - **Industry Threat Monitoring:**
    - CISA healthcare sector alerts
    - Healthcare Information Sharing and Analysis Center (H-ISAC) bulletins
    - Vendor security advisories
    - Public vulnerability databases (CVE, NVD)
  - **Internal Threat Assessment:**
    - Interviews with clinical and administrative staff
    - Review of audit logs and security events
    - Analysis of failed access attempts and policy violations
    - User behavior analysis
  - **Competitive/Environmental Threat Analysis:**
    - Dark web monitoring
    - Threat actor research
    - Industry breach analysis
    - Geopolitical and regulatory threat landscape
- Define healthcare-relevant threat scenarios:
  - **Ransomware attacks:** Against operational systems, medical devices
  - **Phishing and social engineering:** Targeting staff for credentials/data
  - **Insider threats:** Unauthorized access to sensitive patient data
  - **Denial of service:** Against critical clinical systems
  - **Medical device compromise:** Vulnerabilities in connected devices
  - **Supply chain attacks:** Through vendors and third parties
  - **Data exfiltration:** Theft of patient data or intellectual property
- Implement vulnerability identification:
  - **Scanning Program:**
    - Network vulnerability scanning (weekly minimum)
    - Web application scanning (per-release)
    - Mobile application scanning
    - Configuration compliance scanning
    - Database vulnerability assessment
  - **Testing Activities:**
    - Penetration testing (annual minimum for critical systems)
    - Code security review (for custom development)
    - Wireless security assessment
    - Physical security testing
  - **Disclosure Process:**
    - Responsible disclosure policy
    - Coordination with researchers and security professionals
    - Tracking of disclosed vulnerabilities
- Create vulnerability prioritization framework:
  - CVSS scoring and interpretation
  - Asset criticality and data sensitivity
  - Threat context (active exploitation, known attacks)
  - Ease of exploitation and remediation
  - Business impact and operational urgency
- Establish vulnerability tracking:
  - Vulnerability management system (Rapid7, ServiceNow)
  - Categorization by system, severity, and business unit
  - Assignment to remediation owners
  - Tracking of remediation progress
  - Metrics on vulnerability age and closure rate

---

**Target Subcategory: ID-RA-03 - Risk Assessment Scope**

*Tier 3 Requirements:*
- Define scope of risk assessments to cover all critical assets and operations
- Include all systems, data, and infrastructure in scope
- Address both technical and non-technical risks
- Include third-party risks in assessment scope
- Consider risks to clinical operations and patient safety
- Document rationale for scope decisions
- Review and update scope as organisation changes
- Ensure assessments address regulatory requirements

**Implementation for Healthcare Network:**
- Define assessment scope boundaries:
  - **Systems in Scope:**
    - Clinical systems (EHR, PACS, LIS, pharmacy, infusion pumps)
    - Infrastructure (servers, network, database, storage)
    - End-user devices (workstations, laptops, mobile devices)
    - Medical devices (monitors, ventilators, infusion pumps, diagnostic equipment)
    - Communication systems (phones, pagers, video conferencing)
  - **Data in Scope:**
    - Protected Health Information (PHI)
    - Personally Identifiable Information (PII)
    - Financial and billing information
    - Intellectual property and research data
    - Administrative and operational data
  - **Locations in Scope:**
    - All regional hospital facilities
    - Clinic locations and offices
    - Data centers and cloud infrastructure
    - Disaster recovery and backup sites
    - Vendor facilities (as applicable)
  - **Third Parties in Scope:**
    - Software vendors and SaaS providers
    - Infrastructure vendors and cloud providers
    - Business associates and data processors
    - Consultants with system access
    - Managed service providers
- Address compliance scope:
  - HIPAA Security Rule compliance
  - State privacy law requirements
  - HITECH Breach Notification Rule
  - Healthcare accreditation standards
  - Federal and state regulations
- Document scope exclusions:
  - Rationale for exclusion of specific systems/data
  - Residual risks from excluded areas
  - Plans to include excluded areas in future assessments
- Review scope changes:
  - Quarterly review of new systems and acquisitions
  - Regulatory changes affecting scope
  - Organisational restructuring or facility changes
  - Third-party additions and changes

---

## Integration of Govern and Identify Functions

### Cross-Function Coordination

The Govern (GV) and Identify (ID) functions work synergistically to establish the cybersecurity foundation:

- **GV determines risk tolerance and governance requirements** that shape ID assessment scope and methodology
- **ID informs governance decisions** through risk assessments that inform policy and oversight priorities
- **Governance policies from GV** mandate the identification and assessment processes in ID
- **ID findings feed back to GV** through risk reporting and oversight mechanisms

### Healthcare-Specific Considerations

1. **Patient Safety Integration:**
   - Risk assessment must address clinical impact and patient safety
   - Governance must prioritise operational continuity for life-critical systems
   - Controls must balance security with clinical workflow efficiency

2. **Regulatory Compliance:**
   - Govern function must document compliance with HIPAA, state laws, accreditation standards
   - Identify function must assess risks to compliance status
   - Regular assessments verify ongoing compliance

3. **Workforce Engagement:**
   - Governance establishes accountability for clinicians and staff
   - Identification of risks includes user behaviour and training needs
   - Policies must be clinically practical to enable compliance

4. **Third-Party Ecosystem:**
   - Healthcare networks depend on numerous vendors and partners
   - Governance establishes vendor management requirements
   - Identify function assesses supplier risks and data flows

# PCI DSS Compliance Assessment: Stripe.js E-Commerce Store

## Executive Summary

Your e-commerce store using Stripe's hosted payment fields represents a **minimal cardholder data environment (CDE)** scope. You are eligible for **SAQ A-EP** (E-commerce with Partial Outsourcing), do **not require a ROC**, and your CDE scope is **limited to internet-connected systems that interact with Stripe payment tokens and customer data**.

---

## Question 1: Which SAQ Type Applies?

### Answer: SAQ A-EP

**Rationale:**

Your organisation meets the eligibility criteria for SAQ A-EP:

1. **E-commerce only** — You process card-not-present transactions exclusively through an e-commerce store
2. **All cardholder data capture outsourced** — Stripe's hosted payment fields (Stripe.js) handle PAN capture directly; your servers never receive card numbers
3. **Merchant controls payment page** — Your website hosts the Stripe payment widget or iFrame, which means you exercise some control over how/where the customer authenticates
4. **No card-present transactions** — All transactions occur online

**SAQ A vs. SAQ A-EP distinction:**

- **SAQ A** applies when you use a fully hosted redirect (e.g., "Pay with Stripe" button redirects to Stripe's domain entirely — merchant never controls the page)
- **SAQ A-EP** applies when you embed Stripe.js payment elements within your own checkout page — you control the page, Stripe handles the data capture

Since you are using Stripe's **hosted payment fields** (Stripe.js Elements or Payment Request Button embedded in your page), you own the checkout domain/page, making **SAQ A-EP** the correct choice.

**Controls covered by SAQ A-EP:** ~191 controls across Requirements 2, 6, 8, 9, 10, 11, and 12, with emphasis on:
- System configuration and hardening (Req 2)
- Secure development and change management (Req 6) — including script integrity for Req 6.4.3 and 11.6.1
- Access control and authentication (Req 8)
- Logging and monitoring (Req 10)
- Security testing (Req 11)
- Information security policy (Req 12)

---

## Question 2: Do We Need a ROC?

### Answer: No, ROC Not Required

**Rationale:**

ROCs are required only for **Level 1 Merchants** and **Level 1 Service Providers**:

| Merchant Level | Transaction Volume | Validation Requirement |
|---|---|---|
| **Level 1** | >6 million Visa/MC transactions/year OR breach history | ROC by QSA + quarterly ASV scan |
| **Level 2** | 1–6 million Visa/MC transactions/year | Annual SAQ + quarterly ASV scan |
| **Level 3** | 20,000–1 million Visa e-commerce/year | Annual SAQ + quarterly ASV scan |
| **Level 4** | <20,000 Visa e-commerce/year | Annual SAQ + quarterly ASV scan (optional) |

**Your status:** 15,000 transactions per year = **Level 4 Merchant**

**Compliance requirement:** Annual SAQ A-EP (self-assessment) + quarterly external vulnerability scans by an Approved Scanning Vendor (ASV). You do **not** require an on-site assessment by a Qualified Security Assessor (QSA).

**Annual validation process:**
1. Complete SAQ A-EP annually (self-assessment questionnaire)
2. Achieve passing quarterly ASV scans (no unresolved critical vulnerabilities)
3. Submit Attestation of Compliance (AOC) to your acquiring bank or card brands
4. Retain evidence (SAQ, ASV scan reports, supporting documentation)

---

## Question 3: What is Our CDE Scope?

### Answer: Limited Scope — Payment Token Integration Layer

Your **Cardholder Data Environment (CDE)** includes only systems that **store, process, or transmit cardholder data or sensitive authentication data (SAD)** — or systems connected to them without adequate network segmentation.

### In-Scope Systems (CDE):

1. **Web Application / E-Commerce Platform**
   - Reason: Accepts Stripe payment tokens and customer data (names, emails); hosts the Stripe.js payment widget
   - Cardholder data handled: Customer names, emails, Stripe payment tokens (tokenised PAN substitutes)
   - Sensitive data NOT present: Full PANs, CVV/CVC codes, magnetic stripe data

2. **Web Server / API Gateway**
   - Reason: Receives and processes payment token callbacks from Stripe; transmits tokens to payment processor for authorisation
   - Data flows: Stripe tokens only; never sees PAN

3. **Database (Customer & Order Data)**
   - Reason: Stores customer names, emails, order history, and Stripe payment tokens
   - Sensitive data NOT stored: PANs, expiry dates, CVV codes (SAD)

4. **Network Infrastructure (firewalls, load balancers, routers)**
   - Reason: Controls traffic between web application and Stripe's API; must restrict unauthorised access to CDE systems
   - Controlled access: Outbound HTTPS only to Stripe API endpoints

5. **Logging and Monitoring Systems**
   - Reason: Must capture logs from CDE systems per Req 10
   - Sensitive data restriction: Logs must NOT contain PANs, tokens, or CVV codes

### Out-of-Scope Systems (NOT CDE):

- **Stripe infrastructure** — Stripe is a PCI DSS-compliant service provider; they handle PAN protection
- **Internal business systems** (HR, finance, CRM, analytics) — NOT connected to CDE or payment processing
- **Customer web browsers** — While they transmit payment data, the browser itself is not managed by your organisation
- **Third-party analytics or advertising platforms** — If not connected to CDE systems

### CDE Scope Diagram (Logical):

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     INTERNET (Untrusted)                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                           ↓
        ┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐
        │  Stripe Hosted Payment API (Out of Scope)|
        │  (PCI-compliant; handles PAN protection)│
        └──────────────────────────────────────────┘
                           ↓
                      HTTPS/TLS
                           ↓
        ╔════════════════════════════════════════╗
        ║       YOUR CDE (In-Scope)             ║
        ║                                        ║
        ║  ┌──────────────────────────────────┐ ║
        ║  │  E-Commerce Web App (Stripe.js)  │ ║
        ║  │  - Hosts payment widget          │ ║
        ║  │  - Receives tokens from Stripe   │ ║
        ║  │  - Stores: names, emails, tokens│ ║
        ║  └──────────────────────────────────┘ ║
        ║           ↓                             ║
        ║  ┌──────────────────────────────────┐ ║
        ║  │  Backend API / Web Server        │ ║
        ║  │  - Processes payment tokens      │ ║
        ║  │  - Calls Stripe API              │ ║
        ║  └──────────────────────────────────┘ ║
        ║           ↓                             ║
        ║  ┌──────────────────────────────────┐ ║
        ║  │  Database                        │ ║
        ║  │  - Customer data (name, email)   │ ║
        ║  │  - Order history                 │ ║
        ║  │  - Stripe payment tokens         │ ║
        ║  └──────────────────────────────────┘ ║
        ║           ↑                             ║
        ║  ┌──────────────────────────────────┐ ║
        ║  │  Logging & Monitoring            │ ║
        ║  │  (must exclude PAN/CVV/tokens)  │ ║
        ║  └──────────────────────────────────┘ ║
        ╚════════════════════════════════════════╝
                           ↑
                  Firewall Rules:
              - Inbound: HTTPS only (443)
              - Outbound: Stripe API only
```

---

## Key Scope Reduction Factors

### Why Your CDE is Minimal:

1. **Stripe.js Hosted Fields** — PAN never touches your servers
   - Customer enters card data into an iFrame hosted by Stripe
   - Stripe returns a tokenised reference (payment token) to your server
   - Your systems never handle, store, or transmit the raw PAN

2. **Tokenisation** — Payment tokens replace PANs in storage
   - Your database stores `stripe_payment_token_1234` instead of `4532123456789012`
   - Tokens are non-reversible and useless without Stripe's decryption key
   - Reduces scope significantly per PCI DSS tokenisation rules (Req 3.4.1)

3. **No SAD Storage** — You do not store sensitive authentication data
   - No full magnetic stripe data
   - No CVV/CVC codes
   - No PINs or PIN blocks
   - Compliant with Req 3.3.1

4. **Stripe as Service Provider** — Stripe assumes PCI compliance responsibility
   - Stripe is a PCI DSS-compliant service provider
   - Your acquiring bank and Stripe have a contract defining their responsibilities
   - You do not assess Stripe's compliance; you trust their attestation

---

## Annual Compliance Obligations (SAQ A-EP)

### 1. Self-Assessment Questionnaire (SAQ A-EP)
- Complete annually
- ~191 controls to review and attest
- Can be completed by your security or compliance team; QSA involvement is optional
- Timeline: Before end of calendar year, or by card brand deadline

### 2. Approved Scanning Vendor (ASV) External Scans
- **Quarterly** external vulnerability scans required
- ASV must be PCI SSC-approved
- Must achieve "passing" scans (no unresolved critical/high vulnerabilities)
- Retain scan reports for evidence

### 3. Attestation of Compliance (AOC)
- Signed declaration of compliance status
- Completed after SAQ is finished
- Signed by your officer and submitted to acquiring bank

### 4. Key Documentation to Maintain
- SAQ A-EP questionnaire (completed and signed)
- ASV scan reports (4 per year)
- Network diagram (CDE boundaries)
- Data flow diagrams (payment token flows)
- Stripe service provider attestation (for evidence of third-party compliance)
- Information security policies (Requirements 2, 6, 8, 10, 12)
- Change management records
- Logs from CDE systems (per Req 10)

---

## Critical Controls for SAQ A-EP

### Requirement 6: Secure Development & Change Management
**Most important for your environment:**
- Requirement 6.4.3 — Inventory and integrity verification of all scripts on payment page
- Requirement 11.6.1 — Script integrity checks (e.g., Subresource Integrity, CSP)
- Because you host the Stripe.js widget within your page, you must ensure no malicious scripts are injected

**Implement:**
- Content Security Policy (CSP) headers to whitelist only Stripe and your CDN
- Subresource Integrity (SRI) checks on all script includes
- Automated inventory of all scripts loaded on checkout page
- Change control for any payment page modifications

### Requirement 8: User Authentication & Access Control
- Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) for all access into the CDE systems
- Unique user IDs for all personnel with access
- Password policy: minimum 12 characters

### Requirement 10: Logging & Monitoring
- Log all access to CDE systems (web app, API, database)
- Monitor for suspicious activity
- Logs must NOT contain PANs, CVV codes, or payment tokens
- Automated log review required (new in v4.0)

### Requirement 11: Penetration Testing & ASV Scans
- Quarterly external scans by ASV (critical)
- Annual penetration testing (recommended, may be part of SAQ)
- Address any findings; re-test until passing

---

## Risk Considerations

### What Could Expand Your CDE Scope?

Your scope could grow if:

1. **You process card-present transactions** — Would require SAQ B, B-IP, C, C-VT, or P2PE (larger scope)
2. **You store raw PANs or CVV codes** — Would require encryption/tokenisation per Req 3.4; if not encrypted, you'd need SAQ D (full scope)
3. **You connect CDE systems to untrusted networks** — Without segmentation, more systems become in-scope
4. **You develop custom payment application** — Instead of using Stripe.js, would require SAQ C or D
5. **You implement P2PE solution** — Could reduce scope further to SAQ P2PE (~33 controls only)

### What Helps Maintain Minimal Scope?

- **Continue using Stripe.js** — Do not attempt to handle card data directly
- **Maintain network segmentation** — Keep CDE systems separate from internal networks
- **Do not store SAD** — Never retain CVV, full magnetic stripe, or PIN data
- **Implement script integrity controls** — Protect against malicious injections on payment page
- **Conduct annual penetration testing** — Identify vulnerabilities before they become breaches

---

|---------|----------|
| **Q1** | Engage ASV for quarterly scan; begin SAQ A-EP documentation |

| **Q4** | Complete full SAQ A-EP questionnaire; obtain final ASV scan 4; sign AOC; submit to acquiring bank |
| **Year 2+** | Repeat annually; maintain quarterly ASV scans |
