   - Name, title, organisation, email, and 24/7 phone number of backup coordinator
   - Statement confirming 24/7 availability

3. **Baseline Cybersecurity Practices Review Report**
   - Current state assessment of your cybersecurity practices
   - Inventory of Critical Cyber Systems
   - Identification of gaps vs. expected TSA requirements
   - Prioritised remediation roadmap

### Phase 2 Documents (Required for CRMP Implementation)

4. **Cybersecurity Implementation Plan (CIP) or Cybersecurity Operational Implementation Plan (COIP)**
   - Comprehensive document describing how your organisation will meet all CRMP requirements
   - Must be submitted to TSA for formal review and approval
   - Cannot be used as compliance evidence until TSA approves

5. **Incident Response Plan (IRP)**
   - Documented procedures for detecting, responding to, and recovering from incidents
   - Includes roles, responsibilities, escalation procedures, CISA/TSA notification process
   - Must be tested at least twice annually with documented evidence

6. **Architecture Design Review (ADR) Report (Annual)**
   - Assessment of IT/OT network architecture and segmentation effectiveness
   - Updated network topology diagrams
   - Identification of vulnerabilities and segmentation gaps
   - Remediation action plan

7. **Cybersecurity Assessment Plan (CAP)**
   - Formal plan for conducting annual assessments of CRMP effectiveness
   - Defines scope, methodology, schedule, and reporting requirements
   - Annual submission of assessment results and findings

### Phase 3 Documents (Ongoing/Supporting)

8. **Network Segmentation Policy**
   - Formal policy governing IT/OT network separation
   - Defines segmentation architecture, exception process, testing requirements

9. **Access Control Policy**
   - Policy governing user accounts, authentication, privilege management on CCS
   - Defines MFA requirements, account lifecycle, access review procedures

10. **Patch Management Policy**
    - Policy governing vulnerability identification and patch deployment
    - Defines SLAs, risk-based prioritisation, OT-specific procedures

11. **Continuous Monitoring Policy**
    - Policy governing network monitoring, log collection, anomaly detection
    - Defines tools, baselines, alerting, and escalation procedures

12. **Change Management Policy (OT-specific)**
    - Policy governing changes to OT systems and CCS
    - Defines change request, approval, testing, and rollback procedures

13. **Vendor/Third-Party Access Policy**
    - Policy governing remote access by vendors and service providers to CCS
    - Defines approval, monitoring, time-limiting, and revocation procedures

14. **Critical Cyber Systems Inventory Policy and Inventory**
    - Policy defining what constitutes a CCS and how the inventory is maintained
    - Current inventory of all CCS in scope

15. **Evidence of IRP Testing**
    - Documentation of at least two annual IRP tests
    - Test scenarios, dates, participants, findings, corrective actions

16. **Incident Response Procedure Playbook**
    - Step-by-step procedures for different incident types (malware, unauthorised access, ransomware, DDoS)
    - Escalation trees, communication templates, CISA/TSA reporting forms

## Part 7: Critical Next Steps

### 1. Confirm TSA Designation
**Action:** Contact TSA to formally confirm that your specific facilities are designated as critical infrastructure and subject to Security Directive requirements.
- **Contact:** TSA Office of Security and Hazmat Safety (OSHS)
- **Verify:** Designation status, applicable directive revisions, and any previously issued orders or communications

### 2. Establish Cybersecurity Governance
- Designate a primary and backup Cybersecurity Coordinator (24/7 availability)
- Establish an executive sponsor (Accountable Executive) with C-suite authority
- Create a cybersecurity governance committee or steering group to oversee CIP implementation

### 3. Conduct Baseline Assessment
- Inventory all Critical Cyber Systems
- Map current IT and OT network architecture
- Document existing cybersecurity tools, policies, and personnel
- Identify gaps relative to TSA requirements

### 4. Develop Compliance Strategy
- Engage TSA early to clarify expectations and timelines
- Consider hiring a TSA-experienced cybersecurity consultant to assist with CIP/COIP development
- Prioritise network segmentation and access controls (highest-risk gaps for most organisations)
- Plan for third-party assessments (penetration testing, vulnerability scanning) to support CAP

## Part 8: Key Definitions & Clarifications

### Critical Cyber Systems (CCS)
Systems whose compromise or exploitation could result in:
- **Operational disruption** — Inability to safely operate, monitor, or control physical assets
- **Safety impact** — Risk to employees, passengers, or public
- **Environmental impact** — Uncontrolled release of hazardous materials
- **National security impact** — Disruption to critical infrastructure

CCS include both IT systems (corporate networks, enterprise systems that touch OT) and OT systems (SCADA, DCS, PLCs, RTUs, HMIs, safety systems).

### IT vs. OT Distinction
- **IT:** Corporate email, ERP systems, HR systems, office networks — typically windows/Linux-based, updated frequently
- **OT:** SCADA systems, DCS, PLCs, RTUs, HMIs, historian servers — often proprietary, mission-critical, cannot tolerate disruption or frequent updates
- **ICS:** Industrial Control Systems — a subset of OT, specifically systems that control physical processes

### Cybersecurity Coordinator
Must be available 24/7 (or have a backup designee) and serve as the single point of contact for TSA and CISA on all cybersecurity matters.

---

## Part 9: Important Disclaimers & Next Steps

**This assessment provides informational guidance based on publicly available TSA Security Directive summaries and DHS/CISA publications.** TSA Security Directives are Sensitive Security Information (SSI) — full directive text is not publicly available.

**This guidance is not legal, regulatory, or professional compliance advice.** Your organisation must:
- Work directly with TSA to confirm your designation and clarify expectations
- Consult with your legal counsel on regulatory obligations
- Engage qualified OT/ICS cybersecurity professionals to design and implement controls
- Always verify against the current revision of applicable directives from TSA

**Immediate action:** Contact TSA's Office of Security and Hazmat Safety to confirm your designation and request the latest directive revisions (SD Pipeline-2021-01G and SD Pipeline-2021-02F, or newer if available).

# TSA Cybersecurity Compliance for TransGulf Pipeline LLC

## Executive Summary

TransGulf Pipeline LLC, as a natural gas transmission pipeline operator based in Texas, is subject to Transportation Security Administration (TSA) Pipeline and Hazardous Materials Safety Administration (PHMSA) cybersecurity requirements. This assessment outlines the applicable Security Directives, immediate compliance obligations, and required documentation.

---

## Applicable TSA Security Directives

### Primary Regulatory Framework

**1. CISA Security Directives (Most Current)**
- **Security Directive 21-02** (effective since 2021): Addresses cybersecurity requirements for the oil and natural gas sector
- **Security Directive 22-02** (updated requirements): Establishes cybersecurity requirements for rail, transit, and over-the-road bus modes
- **Security Directive 23-01** (latest iteration): May apply depending on current TSA updates

**2. PHMSA Cybersecurity Requirements**
- Pipeline Safety Regulations under 49 CFR Parts 192 and 195
- Requirements for pipeline operators to implement cybersecurity programs
- Applies to natural gas transmission pipelines

**3. Applicable Thresholds for TransGulf**
- As a natural gas transmission operator, you are likely subject to CISA's pipeline-specific directives
- The presence of Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition (SCADA) systems triggers mandatory compliance
- Operating in critical infrastructure sector makes you a covered entity

---

## Immediate Compliance Obligations

### Phase 1: Immediate Actions (0-30 days)

1. **Security Program Documentation**
   - Establish a written cybersecurity program
   - Designate a Chief Information Security Officer (CISO) or equivalent
   - Appoint a Cyber Security Coordinator

2. **Inventory and Assessment**
   - Identify all Information Technology (IT) and Operational Technology (OT) systems
   - Map network architecture and all connected systems
   - Identify critical systems and data flows
   - Document all SCADA/control system interfaces

3. **Risk Assessment**
   - Conduct a baseline risk assessment of cybersecurity posture
   - Identify vulnerabilities in critical systems
   - Document existing security controls
   - Prioritize high-risk systems

4. **Notification to TSA**
   - Identify your TSA Regional Coordinator
   - Notify TSA of your cybersecurity compliance program initiation
   - Request clarification on specific applicability if necessary

### Phase 2: 30-90 Days

1. **Access Control Implementation**
   - Implement role-based access controls (RBAC)
   - Establish multi-factor authentication (MFA) requirements
   - Document privileged account management procedures
   - Implement least-privilege access principles

2. **Network Segmentation**
   - Implement network segmentation between IT and OT systems
   - Create demilitarized zones (DMZs) where appropriate
   - Document all network connections and data flows

3. **Monitoring and Logging**
   - Establish continuous monitoring of critical systems
   - Implement centralized logging and audit trails
   - Configure intrusion detection systems (IDS)
   - Establish security incident logging protocols

4. **Incident Response Plan**
   - Develop a formal cybersecurity incident response plan
   - Define roles and responsibilities
   - Establish communication protocols for incidents
   - Define coordination with law enforcement and CISA

### Phase 3: 90+ Days (Ongoing)

1. **Employee Training and Awareness**
   - Develop cybersecurity training program for all personnel
   - Implement annual refresher training requirements
   - Provide role-specific training for IT and OT staff

2. **Vulnerability Management**
   - Establish patch management procedures
   - Implement regular vulnerability scanning
   - Create remediation timelines for identified vulnerabilities
   - Document all security updates and patches

3. **Testing and Validation**
   - Conduct penetration testing and red team exercises
   - Perform tabletop exercises for incident response scenarios
   - Validate security controls through testing
   - Document all test results and remediation actions

---

   - Part 192.612: Cybersecurity Program Requirements
   - Requires operators to establish a cybersecurity program
   - Mandates documented procedures for protecting against cybersecurity threats

2. **TSA's Role**
   - TSA provides pipeline-specific security guidance
   - Coordinates with PHMSA on cybersecurity requirements
   - May issue additional Security Directives based on threat assessments

### Critical Infrastructure Implications

- Pipeline operators are designated Critical Infrastructure
- Subject to CISA coordination and potential emergency directives
- May be required to participate in information sharing activities
- Potential obligations under CISA authorities and PHMSA joint requirements

# TRANSGULF PIPELINE LLC
## Cyber Risk Management Program (CRMP)
### Incident Reporting Section
#### TSA Security Directive SD Pipeline-2021-02 Compliance

---

## 1. SCOPE AND APPLICABILITY

This Incident Reporting section of TransGulf Pipeline LLC's Cyber Risk Management Program establishes mandatory procedures for identifying, reporting, and responding to cybersecurity incidents affecting Critical Cyber Systems (CCS) in accordance with the Transportation Security Administration (TSA) Security Directive SD Pipeline-2021-02.

**Covered Systems**: All Critical Cyber Systems, including:
- Operational Technology (OT) systems: SCADA, Distributed Control Systems (DCS), Programmable Logic Controllers (PLCs), Remote Terminal Units (RTUs), and Human-Machine Interfaces (HMIs) controlling pipeline operations
- Information Technology (IT) systems whose compromise could result in operational disruption, safety impact, or unauthorized access to OT systems
- Network infrastructure, communications systems, and data repositories supporting CCS operations

**Applicable to**: All TransGulf Pipeline LLC personnel, including operational staff, cybersecurity teams, IT personnel, contractors, vendors, and third-party service providers with access to CCS.

**Regulatory Authority**: TSA Security Directive SD Pipeline-2021-02 (current revision); CISA incident reporting requirements; Cyber Incident Reporting for Critical Infrastructure Act (CIRCIA).

---

## 2. INCIDENT DEFINITION AND REPORTABILITY CRITERIA

### 2.1 What Constitutes a Reportable Cybersecurity Incident

A cybersecurity incident is reportable to CISA if it results in — or is **reasonably likely to result in** — operational disruption, safety impact, environmental impact, or unauthorized access to a Critical Cyber System.

**The reporting threshold is intentionally low**: When in doubt, report. TSA and CISA expect entities to report early with limited information; final investigation details are provided in follow-up reports.

### 2.2 Definite Reportable Incidents

The following incidents must be reported to CISA within 24 hours:

1. **Ransomware Infection**
   - Confirmed ransomware or encryption malware on IT systems
   - Confirmed ransomware or encryption malware on OT systems
   - Suspected ransomware with evidence of encryption in progress
   - *Example*: Malware detected on corporate IT network attempting to encrypt files; OT systems at risk of lateral movement

2. **Unauthorized Access to Critical Cyber Systems**
   - Confirmed unauthorized access to any CCS (IT or OT)
   - Breach of access controls resulting in privilege escalation
   - Unauthorized access to operator accounts, historian systems, or engineering workstations
   - *Example*: Compromised employee credentials used to access SCADA monitoring system outside normal hours

3. **Malware Detection on CCS**
   - Any confirmed malware (virus, worm, trojan, rootkit) on CCS, even if immediately contained
   - Detection of malware with command-and-control (C2) capability
   - Malware capable of modifying system files or configurations
   - *Example*: Trojan detected on server supporting pipeline control systems

4. **Denial of Service Affecting Operational Capability**
   - DoS attack preventing normal pipeline operations or monitoring
   - Loss of network connectivity to OT systems due to cyber attack
   - Flooding or resource exhaustion affecting OT control capability
   - *Example*: Network flooding attack causing loss of real-time SCADA data feeds

5. **Confirmed Phishing Attack with System Access**
   - Phishing campaign resulting in credential theft and confirmed CCS access
   - Phishing emails leading to malware installation on CCS-connected systems
   - Social engineering attack resulting in unauthorized system access
   - *Example*: Targeted phishing email to operations staff; credential compromise confirmed; system logon detected outside normal parameters

6. **Insider Threat with CCS Access**
   - Confirmed malicious insider activity with access to CCS
   - Disgruntled employee with administrative credentials accessing systems outside job responsibilities
   - Unauthorized data exfiltration from CCS or operational databases
   - *Example*: Departing employee accessing OT historian after termination paperwork initiated

7. **Physical Security Breach with Suspected Cyber Access**
   - Unauthorized physical access to control room, server room, or OT infrastructure
   - Evidence that unauthorized person accessed networked equipment or systems
   - Tampering with network cables, access controls, or physical security measures
   - *Example*: Unauthorized individual observed in control center; network cable repositioned; unexplained system access detected within same timeframe

8. **Loss or Suspected Loss of Operational Control**
   - Evidence of unauthorized commands sent to OT systems
   - Inability to verify operator credentials for actions observed on SCADA
   - Safety instrumented system (SIS) activation without legitimate operational cause
   - Unexpected valve operations, pump commands, or pressure changes without corresponding operator action
   - *Example*: Pressure relief valve operated remotely; no corresponding work order; no operator acknowledged the command

9. **Detection of Reconnaissance Activity Targeting CCS**
   - Port scans specifically targeting SCADA networks or OT infrastructure
   - Probing of industrial control protocols (Modbus, DNP3, EtherNet/IP)
   - Network scanning from external sources mapping internal OT topology
   - *Example*: Passive Nmap scan of internal OT network detected; source traced to external IP; scan specifically enumerated Modbus devices

### 2.3 Potentially Reportable Incidents (Apply Judgment; When in Doubt, Report)

The following incidents should trigger a preliminary assessment and likely CISA notification:

1. **Phishing with Credential Theft (No Confirmed CCS Access Yet)**
   - Phishing campaign confirmed to harvest credentials
   - No system logon verified yet, but breach of email/credential is confirmed
   - *Assessment*: Report if credentials compromised belong to users with CCS access

2. **Suspicious Login Attempts with Partial Success Indicators**
   - Failed login attempts followed by unusual account activity
   - Multiple password reset requests for a single account
   - Successful login from unusual location or device
   - *Assessment*: Report if account belongs to system administrator or OT operator

3. **Discovery of Unknown Devices on OT Network**
   - Unauthorized device detected on industrial control network
   - Device not in CCS inventory; purpose unknown
   - Device communicating with OT systems using industrial control protocols
   - *Assessment*: Report if device has potential for lateral movement to critical systems

4. **Evidence of Lateral Movement from IT to OT**
   - Security alert indicating movement from corporate IT network boundary toward OT network
   - Suspicious outbound connection from IT system to known OT device IP addresses
   - Privilege escalation in IT environment with OT network access implications
   - *Assessment*: Report if path to OT systems is not fully segmented

5. **Vendor/Third-Party Breach Notification**
   - Notification from software vendor that their product used in your environment is compromised
   - Notification from cloud service provider of potential exposure of your operational data
   - Third-party managed OT service affected by breach
   - *Assessment*: Report if breach affects systems connected to CCS or handles operational data

### 2.4 Non-Reportable Incidents (Generally)

The following incidents do **not** require CISA notification:

- **Spam email** with no credential compromise or malware payload
- **Blocked phishing attempt** with no evidence of user interaction or credential compromise
- **Routine vulnerability assessments** conducted by authorized security testing firms
- **Failed brute-force attacks** with no evidence of account compromise
- **Operational alerts** that are not security-related (e.g., normal system downtime, maintenance activity)
- **False positive security alerts** confirmed to be legitimate system behavior

---

## 3. INCIDENT DISCOVERY AND INITIAL ASSESSMENT

### 3.1 Incident Detection Mechanisms

TransGulf Pipeline LLC monitors for cybersecurity incidents through multiple channels:

**Automated Detection**:
- Network-based intrusion detection system (IDS) alerts on suspicious traffic patterns
- Endpoint detection and response (EDR) tools identifying malware, lateral movement, or suspicious behavior
- OT-specific monitoring tools (passive network monitoring, anomaly detection) alerting on deviations from OT communication baselines
- Log collection and Security Information and Event Management (SIEM) analysis identifying authentication anomalies, privilege escalation, or data exfiltration
- Firewall and access control alerts on unauthorized connection attempts

**Manual Detection**:
- Operations or IT staff reporting suspicious system behavior to the Cybersecurity Coordinator
- Third-party vendor or service provider notifying TransGulf of potential breach or exposure
- User report of suspected phishing, social engineering, or unauthorized access
- Unexpected system behavior (e.g., unexplained reboots, performance degradation, system unavailability)

**Regulatory or External Notification**:
- CISA or TSA advisory notification of vulnerability affecting TransGulf systems
- Law enforcement notification of attack targeting TransGulf or sector peers
- ISAC (Information Sharing and Analysis Center) notification of threat targeting energy sector infrastructure

### 3.2 Initial Triage and Assessment

**Immediate Actions Upon Incident Detection**:

1. **Preserve Evidence** (First Minute)
   - Do not shut down affected systems unless necessary to preserve safety
   - Capture live system memory if safe to do so
   - Log all user actions, commands, and observations
   - Do not alter or delete files or logs

2. **Preliminary Classification** (First 15 Minutes)
   - Assess whether the alert represents a confirmed incident or false positive
   - Determine which CCS, if any, are affected
   - Assess operational impact: Is normal pipeline operation maintained?
   - Assess safety impact: Could the incident affect safety-instrumented systems or personnel safety?

3. **Escalation Decision** (Within 30 Minutes)
   - If confirmed incident affecting CCS: Escalate immediately to Cybersecurity Coordinator
   - If potential incident with unclear CCS impact: Escalate to Cybersecurity Coordinator for determination
   - If false positive with low operational impact: Document and log; no external escalation required

### 3.3 Preliminary Incident Severity Assessment

Incidents shall be initially classified by severity to guide response urgency:

| **Severity Tier** | **Definition** | **Response Activation** | **CISA Reporting Timeline** |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Critical** | Active threat to operational capability or safety; confirmed CCS compromise; potential for immediate operational disruption | Immediate activation of full incident response team; all hands response | Within 24 hours of identification |
| **High** | Confirmed unauthorized access to CCS; confirmed malware on CCS; confirmed operational impact occurring | Incident Commander activated within 1 hour; OT and IT response teams assembled | Within 24 hours of identification |
| **Medium** | Suspected compromise of CCS with investigation underway; indicators of compromise on CCS-connected systems; potential path to CCS not yet verified | Incident Commander activated within 4 hours; focused investigation; potential escalation to High if additional evidence emerges | Within 24 hours if confirmed; continue investigation if unconfirmed |
| **Low** | Indicator of compromise detected on non-critical IT systems; failed attack attempts; vulnerability exposure without confirmed exploit | Investigation by assigned analyst; documentation of findings | Document and monitor; escalate to higher tier if additional evidence emerges |

**Reassessment**: Incidents are reassessed hourly during active response. Severity tier may be elevated or downgraded as investigation progresses. Escalation is always preferred over downward reassessment when evidence is ambiguous.

---

## 4. INCIDENT REPORTING ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES

### 4.1 Cybersecurity Coordinator — Primary Reporting Authority

**Identity and Authority**:
- **Primary Cybersecurity Coordinator**: [Name], [Title], reporting to the Accountable Executive
- **Backup Cybersecurity Coordinator**: [Name], [Title], available 24/7 when primary is unavailable
- The Cybersecurity Coordinator has decision authority to report incidents to CISA and TSA independent of other corporate functions
- The Coordinator has escalation authority to the Accountable Executive and Chief Operating Officer

**Primary Responsibilities for Incident Reporting**:

1. **Incident Confirmation**: Upon notification of potential incident, coordinates triage and confirms whether a reportable incident has occurred
2. **24-Hour CISA Reporting**: Personally responsible for ensuring CISA is notified within 24 hours of incident identification; owns the reporting timeline
3. **TSA Notification**: Ensures TSA Operations Center is notified per directive requirements
4. **Initial Report Submission**: Provides initial CISA report with all available information at the time of notification
5. **Follow-Up Communications**: Maintains communication with CISA and TSA throughout incident investigation and recovery
6. **Documentation**: Maintains incident notification log (see Section 6) with all reporting timestamps and case references

**24/7 Availability**:
- Primary and backup coordinators maintain 24/7 availability via dedicated phone line: [Phone Number]
- Cell phone contacts maintained in secure facility; updated quarterly
- Escalation path to Accountable Executive available if Cybersecurity Coordinator unreachable

### 4.2 Accountable Executive

**Authority and Responsibilities**:
- Accountable Executive: [Name], [Title], Chief Operating Officer or designee
- Roles: Approves all corrective actions; authorizes incident response costs; oversees communication with TSA and law enforcement
- Notification: Accountable Executive is notified immediately upon confirmation of reportable incident (concurrent with or before CISA notification)
- Authority: Can override operational decisions if required for incident containment and CISA compliance

### 4.3 Incident Response Team Lead (Incident Commander)

**Role and Responsibilities**:
- Typically the Cybersecurity Coordinator or senior IT/OT security personnel designated by the Coordinator
- Commands the incident response activities; assigns tasks to IT, OT, and forensic teams
- Maintains incident timeline and chain of custody for evidence
- Coordinates containment, eradication, and recovery procedures with OT operations
- Updates Cybersecurity Coordinator on progress; triggers CISA report updates based on investigation findings

### 4.4 Operational Technology (OT) Response Team

**Role and Responsibilities**:
- Senior OT engineers and operations supervisors
- Assess operational impact; advise on containment procedures that maintain operational capability or safely shut down operations
- Execute containment and recovery procedures for SCADA, DCS, PLCs, and field devices
- Coordinate with OT vendors for emergency patching or system restoration
- Provide operational timeline information for incident investigation and reporting

### 4.5 Information Technology Response Team

**Role and Responsibilities**:
- IT security, network, and systems administrators
- Contain compromised IT systems; isolate from network; preserve evidence
- Conduct forensic analysis and identify root cause
- Test patches and recovery procedures before deployment
- Monitor IT/OT firewall for suspicious activity during and after incident

### 4.6 Legal and Compliance

**Role and Responsibilities**:
- Advises on regulatory notification obligations (TSA, CISA, CIRCIA, state data breach laws, etc.)
- Coordinates with law enforcement if criminal activity suspected (FBI Cyber Division)
- Prepares incident disclosure language for external communications
- Documents privileged communications if litigation or regulatory action anticipated
- Reviews incident closure report before CISA submission

### 4.7 Communication and Crisis Management

**Role and Responsibilities**:
- Public relations or communications team
- Coordinates public statements if incident becomes known to media or customers
- Supports CISA/law enforcement communications
- Documents all external communications related to incident for regulatory record

---

## 5. CISA INCIDENT REPORTING PROCEDURES

### 5.1 Reporting Requirement and Timeline

**Mandatory Reporting Deadline**: All confirmed cybersecurity incidents affecting CCS **must be reported to CISA within 24 hours** of identification.

**Key Principle**: The 24-hour clock starts when TransGulf Pipeline LLC identifies the incident, not when investigation is complete. Initial report may be based on limited information; detailed findings and corrective actions follow in subsequent reports as investigation matures.

**No delays permitted**: Do not delay reporting while conducting internal investigation, root cause analysis, or obtaining legal review. Initial CISA notification is a regulatory obligation that supersedes internal process approval.

### 5.2 CISA Reporting Channels (24/7 Operations Center)

**Primary Reporting Method — Phone**:
- **Phone Number**: 1-888-282-0870
- **Call Type**: Direct call to CISA 24/7 Operations Center
- **Expected Response**: Incident intake specialist receives call; documents initial information; provides case reference number
- **Best for**: Time-sensitive incidents requiring immediate acknowledgment

**Secondary Reporting Method — Email**:
- **Email Address**: CISAgov@mail.dhs.gov
- **Subject Line**: "URGENT: Cybersecurity Incident Report - [Entity Name] - [Date/Time]"
- **Best for**: Situations where phone communication is not feasible; supplements phone reporting

**Web-Based Reporting Portal**:
- **URL**: https://myservices.cisa.gov/report
- **Access**: CISA portal allows submission of structured incident report forms
- **Best for**: Follow-up reports with detailed information; not recommended for initial 24-hour notification

**Recommended Approach**: Phone call to CISA 24/7 Operations Center (1-888-282-0870) within 24 hours; follow up with detailed information via email or portal within 48 hours.

### 5.3 Parallel TSA Notification

**Requirement**: In addition to CISA reporting, TransGulf Pipeline LLC shall notify TSA within the same 24-hour window.

**TSA Operations Center Contact**:
- **Phone Number**: 1-866-289-9673
- **Describe**: Incident details similar to CISA report; reference CISA case number if available
- **Escalation**: If TSA does not respond to initial notification within 2 hours, escalate to designated TSA Regional Security Officer

### 5.4 Internal Escalation Sequence (Before or Concurrent with CISA Notification)

The following escalation sequence ensures proper internal notification while meeting the 24-hour CISA reporting deadline:

| **Sequence** | **Party** | **Notification Timing** | **Method** | **Information** |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Cybersecurity Coordinator (Primary or Backup) | Immediate upon incident identification | Phone call | Initial incident description, affected systems, operational impact, preliminary severity assessment |
| 2 | Accountable Executive | Within 15 minutes of Coordinator notification | Phone call | Executive summary of incident, operational impact, whether CISA/TSA notification is required |
| 3 | Legal Counsel | Within 15 minutes of Coordinator notification | Phone call or email | Incident description, regulatory notification obligations, preliminary legal assessment |
| 4 | OT Operations Management | Concurrent with Coordinator notification if OT systems affected | Phone call | Operational impact assessment, containment options, operational capability implications |
| 5 | CISA (Incident Reporting) | Within 24 hours of incident identification | Phone call to 1-888-282-0870 | Initial CISA report (see Section 5.5) |
| 6 | TSA (Incident Reporting) | Within 24 hours of incident identification | Phone call to 1-866-289-9673 | TSA notification with CISA case reference |

**No internal approval required**: The Cybersecurity Coordinator is authorized to proceed with CISA notification without awaiting legal review, executive approval, or investigation completion.

### 5.5 Initial CISA Report — Required Information

The initial 24-hour report to CISA should include as much of the following information as is available at the time of notification. **Incomplete information does not justify delay**; report what is known and provide updates as investigation progresses.

**Essential Information Elements**:

| **Element** | **Detail** | **Example** |
|---|---|---|
| **Organization Name** | Legal entity name; sector | TransGulf Pipeline LLC; Natural Gas Pipeline Operator |
| **Contact Name and Title** | Cybersecurity Coordinator or designated representative | John Smith, Cybersecurity Coordinator |
| **Contact Phone Number** | Direct 24/7 phone number for follow-up communications | 555-123-4567 |
| **Date and Time of Identification** | When incident was first detected; time zone | March 15, 2026, 14:32 UTC; identified by automated SIEM alert |
| **Incident Description** | Brief, clear description of what was observed | "Ransomware detected on corporate IT network server; encrypted files with .ransomXYZ extension; C2 communication detected to external IP; potential lateral movement to OT network" |
| **Systems Affected** | Which IT and/or OT systems are affected or potentially affected | "IT: Mail server, file servers; OT: Potential risk to SCADA network — IT/OT firewall is monitoring; OT systems operational at this time" |
| **Operational Impact** | Description of impact to pipeline operations at time of reporting | "No operational impact currently; pipeline operations continue normally; monitoring in progress; containment procedures underway" OR "Pipeline operations disrupted; unable to control pressure remotely; manual operation in progress" |
| **Containment Status** | What actions have been taken to contain the incident | "Affected IT server disconnected from network; SCADA network monitored continuously; incident response team assembled; forensic imaging in progress" |
| **Law Enforcement Notification** | Whether FBI or other law enforcement has been notified | "Not notified yet" OR "Contacted FBI Cyber Division at [time]; FBI case reference ABC-2026-12345" |
| **Investigation Status** | Current status of investigation; anticipated timeline for updates | "Investigation underway; preliminary root cause analysis in progress; expect forensic findings within 48 hours" |

**Sample Initial CISA Report Language**:

> "TransGulf Pipeline LLC, a natural gas pipeline operator designated as critical by TSA, is reporting a cybersecurity incident identified on March 15, 2026 at 14:32 UTC. Our monitoring systems detected ransomware on a corporate IT file server; the malware is creating encrypted files with a .ransomXYZ extension and communicating with external command-and-control servers. We have immediately disconnected the affected server from the network. Our IT/OT firewall is configured with default-deny rules and is actively monitoring for attempts to access our SCADA network. Pipeline operations are currently unaffected and continue under normal operation. We are conducting forensic analysis and have engaged our IT vendor. Our Cybersecurity Coordinator is John Smith, reachable at 555-123-4567. We expect to provide an update within 48 hours as our investigation matures."

### 5.6 Follow-Up Reporting

After the initial 24-hour report, TransGulf Pipeline LLC shall maintain ongoing communication with CISA and TSA regarding incident status, investigation progress, and corrective actions.

**Follow-Up Report Triggers**:
1. **Root Cause Identified**: Report findings regarding how the attacker gained initial access, what systems were traversed, and what ultimately triggered detection
2. **Scope Change**: Report if additional systems are discovered to be compromised beyond initial report
3. **Operational Impact Change**: Report if operational impact increases (pipeline operations disrupted) or decreases (containment successful, operations stabilized)
4. **Significant Milestones**: Report recovery milestones, e.g., "All ransomware-encrypted systems restored from clean backup," "Affected system returned to operation," "Patching of vulnerability completed"
5. **Incident Closure**: Final report with complete incident summary (see Section 5.7)

**Follow-Up Report Frequency**: At minimum, contact CISA every 7 days with status update until incident is closed; contact more frequently if situation is actively changing.

### 5.7 Incident Closure Report

Upon completion of incident investigation, containment, eradication, and recovery, TransGulf Pipeline LLC shall submit a comprehensive incident closure report to CISA that includes:

**Required Closure Report Elements**:

1. **Timeline**
   - Date/time of initial incident identification
   - Date/time of initial detection alert (automated or manual)
   - Date/time of CISA notification
   - Date/time of containment (affected systems isolated or threat eliminated)
   - Date/time of eradication (all malware removed; all unauthorized access revoked)
   - Date/time of recovery (affected systems restored to normal operation)
   - Date/time of incident closure

2. **Root Cause Analysis**
   - How the attacker gained initial access (e.g., phishing credential compromise, unpatched vulnerability, insider access)
   - Technical path of the attack (systems traversed, lateral movement techniques, privilege escalation)
   - Why the attack was successful (missing compensating control, unpatched system, weak access control, etc.)
   - Vulnerability or control failure that enabled the attack

3. **Systems Affected (Final Scope)**
   - Complete list of confirmed compromised systems
   - List of systems with potential exposure (not confirmed compromised but in attack path)
   - Network zones or segments impacted
   - Any OT systems that were at risk but not directly compromised

4. **Data Involved**
   - What data (if any) was exposed, exfiltrated, or encrypted
   - Volume of data and sensitivity level (operational data, customer data, PII, trade secrets, etc.)
   - Assessment of data exposure impact; any notifications required to customers or regulators

5. **Actions Taken**
   - Containment procedures: What systems were isolated? What network connections were severed?
   - Eradication procedures: How was malware removed? How were unauthorized accounts revoked?
   - Recovery procedures: How were systems restored? What backups were used? How was backup integrity verified?
   - Hardening: What patches, configuration changes, or architectural improvements were made to prevent recurrence?

6. **Lessons Learned**
   - What worked well in incident response (detection, coordination, communication, escalation)
   - What did not work well; what response procedures failed or slowed response
   - What technical controls should have prevented the incident (had they been in place)
   - Recommendations for improving cybersecurity posture, incident response capability, or monitoring

7. **Corrective Actions and Prevention**
   - Immediate corrective actions implemented (patches, access control changes, architectural changes)
   - Long-term corrective actions planned or in progress (e.g., network segmentation project, monitoring tool deployment, OT hardening initiative)
   - Timeline for completion of corrective actions
   - Owner of each corrective action
   - How success will be measured

**Closure Report Submission Deadline**: CISA closure report shall be submitted within 30 days of incident closure (or earlier if investigation completes sooner).

---

## 6. INCIDENT NOTIFICATION LOG

### 6.1 Regulatory Notification Documentation

TransGulf Pipeline LLC maintains a **Cyber Incident Notification Log** documenting all regulatory notifications, internal escalations, and law enforcement contacts for each incident. This log provides evidence of compliance with TSA reporting obligations and serves as a master record for incident tracking.

### 6.2 Notification Log Fields

Each incident entry in the notification log shall include the following fields:

| **Field** | **Description** | **Example** |
|---|---|---|
| **Incident ID** | Unique internal identifier for tracking | INC-2026-001 |
| **Incident Title** | Brief description of incident | "Ransomware on Corporate File Server" |
| **Date/Time Identified (UTC)** | When incident was first detected; time zone specified | 2026-03-15 14:32 UTC |
| **Identified By** | Who or what detected the incident | SIEM automated alert; Operations staff report |
| **Initial Severity Assessment** | Preliminary tier (Critical/High/Medium/Low) | High |
| **Systems Affected** | Which CCS or systems involved | IT: File servers; OT: SCADA network (potential) |
| **Date/Time CISA Notified (UTC)** | When CISA was called; timestamp of notification | 2026-03-15 22:15 UTC |
| **CISA Reporting Channel** | Phone or email | Phone: 1-888-282-0870 |
| **CISA Case Number** | Reference number provided by CISA | CISA-2026-0047392 |
| **Name of CISA Intake Specialist** | If available | Jane Williams, CISA Operations Center |
| **Date/Time TSA Notified (UTC)** | When TSA was called | 2026-03-15 22:30 UTC |
| **TSA Case Reference** | Reference number from TSA | TSA-INFRA-2026-XXXX |
| **TSA Point of Contact** | TSA regional officer or analyst | [Regional Officer Name] |
| **Date/Time Law Enforcement Notified** | If applicable; FBI Cyber Division or local law enforcement | 2026-03-15 23:00 UTC (FBI Cyber Division) |
| **Law Enforcement Case Reference** | FBI case number or local police report number | FBI Case: 2026-CYBER-0123456 |
| **Internal Legal Counsel Notified** | Date/time legal team was advised of incident | 2026-03-15 14:45 UTC |
| **Accountable Executive Notified** | Date/time executive leadership briefed | 2026-03-15 14:40 UTC |
| **OT Operations Notified** | Date/time operations management aware of incident | 2026-03-15 14:35 UTC |
| **Follow-Up Reports Submitted** | Dates of all follow-up CISA/TSA reports | 2026-03-17, 2026-03-22, 2026-03-30 (closure report) |
| **Incident Declared Closed** | Date/time incident response completed and systems normalized | 2026-03-25 |
| **Closure Report Submitted to CISA** | Date closure report was sent | 2026-03-30 |
| **Notes** | Additional context: external assistance, significant findings, ongoing investigation items | CISA Rapid Response Team deployed; FBI conducting forensic analysis on external servers |

### 6.3 Notification Log Maintenance and Retention

**Responsibility**: Cybersecurity Coordinator maintains the notification log

**Update Frequency**: Log is updated real-time as notifications are made and responses received

**Storage**: Log maintained in secure, access-controlled location (e.g., encrypted shared drive with access restricted to Cybersecurity Coordinator, Accountable Executive, and Legal Counsel)

**Retention Period**: Minimum 7 years for all incidents (aligns with TSA record retention requirements and potential federal investigation timelines)

**Confidentiality**: Notification log is sensitive and contains regulatory case references; access restricted to need-to-know personnel; not shared externally without legal counsel review

---

## 7. INTEGRATION WITH INCIDENT RESPONSE PLAN (IRP)

### 7.1 Relationship Between Incident Reporting and IRP

The Incident Reporting procedures documented in this section are integrated with TransGulf Pipeline LLC's Cybersecurity Incident Response Plan (IRP), which provides detailed procedures for detection, containment, eradication, and recovery.

**Key Integration Points**:

1. **IRP Section 3 (Detection and Initial Analysis)** references this Incident Reporting section for severity classification and escalation criteria
2. **IRP Section 5 (CISA and TSA Notification)** elaborates on detailed notification procedures outlined in this section
3. **IRP Section 6 (Post-Incident Review)** includes after-action review procedures that inform corrective actions reported to CISA in closure reports
4. **IRP Testing** includes annual tabletop exercises simulating incident notification procedures; testing validates that Cybersecurity Coordinator can initiate CISA contact within required timelines

### 7.2 IRP Testing and Incident Reporting Validation

At minimum annually, TransGulf Pipeline LLC conducts a tabletop exercise that includes a **simulated CISA notification scenario**:

**Test Objectives**:
- Cybersecurity Coordinator can contact CISA within 24-hour window
- Required incident information can be compiled and communicated
- Escalation procedures (Accountable Executive, OT operations, legal counsel) function as designed
- Documentation and case reference tracking works correctly

**Test Execution**: Twice annually, Cybersecurity Coordinator initiates a **notification drill** in which all escalation steps and CISA contact (or dry-run with CISA acknowledgment) are executed with sample incident data.

**Test Documentation**: Test results, findings, and any procedural updates are documented and retained.

---

## 8. EXTERNAL COORDINATION AND ASSISTANCE

### 8.1 Information Sharing and Analysis Centers (ISACs)

TransGulf Pipeline LLC participates in sector-specific threat intelligence sharing through designated ISACs:

**Primary ISAC**: Energy ISAC (E-ISAC) / Oil and Natural Gas ISAC (ONG-ISAC)
- **Website**: https://www.eisac.org / https://www.ongisac.org
- **Purpose**: Sector-wide threat intelligence sharing; sanitized incident reporting; peer coordination
- **Incident Reporting**: Following CISA closure, TransGulf considers sharing anonymized incident findings with E-ISAC/ONG-ISAC to provide sector peers with threat intelligence

**Secondary ISAC**: Surface Transportation ISAC (ST-ISAC) for multi-sector coordination
- **Website**: https://www.st-isac.org

**ISAC Participation Benefits**:
- Early warning of emerging threats targeting energy sector
- Access to sanitized incident reports from peer organizations
- Coordination with other operators during sector-wide incidents
- Assistance with threat assessment and impact analysis

### 8.2 Free CISA Technical Assistance

Upon incident reporting, TransGulf Pipeline LLC may request the following free services from CISA:

1. **CISA Rapid Response Team (CIRP)**: On-site forensic and incident response support for significant incidents
2. **Incident Response Support**: Remote technical assistance from CISA's ICS/OT specialists
3. **Threat Intelligence**: Real-time threat intelligence relevant to the incident
4. **Vulnerability Assessment**: CISA CSET (Cybersecurity Evaluation Tool) for post-incident vulnerability assessment
5. **Tabletop Exercises**: CISA facilitation of tabletop exercises to test updated incident response procedures

### 8.3 Law Enforcement Coordination

**FBI Cyber Division**: If incident involves criminal activity (ransomware extortion, insider threat, nation-state activity), TransGulf shall coordinate with FBI Cyber Division

**Contact**: Local FBI field office Cyber Division unit
- FBI Cyber investigates complex cyber incidents and coordinates with CISA

**Coordination Points**:
- Forensic evidence preservation and chain of custody
- Timeline coordination between incident response and FBI investigation
- Communication protocols (what can be disclosed publicly while investigation is ongoing)
- Recovery of ransom payments (if applicable)

---

## 9. CYBERSECURITY METRICS AND PERFORMANCE REPORTING

### 9.1 Incident Reporting Performance Metrics

TransGulf Pipeline LLC tracks the following incident reporting metrics as part of ongoing CRMP effectiveness measurement:

**Metric 1: Reporting Timeliness**
- Measure: Percentage of reportable incidents reported to CISA within 24-hour deadline
- Target: 100% compliance (no incidents reported late)
- Baseline: To be established from incident history

**Metric 2: Detection to Escalation Time**
- Measure: Average time from incident detection to Cybersecurity Coordinator notification
- Target: < 30 minutes
- Baseline: To be established from incident history

**Metric 3: Escalation to CISA Contact Time**
- Measure: Time from Cybersecurity Coordinator notification to CISA phone call
- Target: < 2 hours
- Baseline: To be established from incident history

**Metric 4: Incident Closure Timeliness**
- Measure: Average days from incident identification to full closure (containment, eradication, recovery, and closure report to CISA)
- Target: < 30 days for medium/high severity incidents
- Baseline: To be established from incident history

**Metric 5: False Positive Rate**
- Measure: Percentage of escalated incidents that are determined to be false positives or non-reportable
- Target: < 5% (indicates well-tuned detection; too high a rate indicates alert fatigue or detection issues)
- Baseline: To be established from incident history

### 9.2 Annual Incident Reporting Summary

The Cybersecurity Coordinator prepares an annual summary of incident reporting activity for the Accountable Executive and TSA:

**Summary Contents**:
- Total number of cybersecurity incidents detected and identified
- Number of reportable incidents
- Number of CISA reports submitted
- Average time to CISA notification
- Incidents closed within 30 days
- Incidents with active follow-up or ongoing investigation
- Lessons learned that improved incident response procedures
- Any delays or challenges in meeting 24-hour reporting deadline (with remedial actions)

**Distribution**: Annual summary submitted to Accountable Executive and to TSA as part of annual CRMP effectiveness report.

---

## 10. POLICY COMPLIANCE AND REVIEW

### 10.1 Mandatory Compliance

This Incident Reporting section is mandatory for all covered entities within TransGulf Pipeline LLC. Violation of the 24-hour CISA reporting requirement, failure to escalate to the Cybersecurity Coordinator, or failure to follow notification procedures constitutes a TSA Security Directive violation and may result in TSA enforcement action.

**Compliance Authority**: Cybersecurity Coordinator has the explicit authority and responsibility to ensure all reporting requirements are met, independent of other corporate approval processes.

### 10.2 Training and Awareness

**Annual Training Requirement**:
- All IT and OT personnel with potential incident detection responsibility receive annual training on this Incident Reporting section
- Training covers: incident definition, reportability criteria, escalation path, Cybersecurity Coordinator contact information, CISA reporting procedures
- Training completion tracked and documented

**Incident Response Drills**:
- Twice annually, Cybersecurity Coordinator leads a simulated incident notification drill to ensure procedures function correctly
- All escalation recipients (Accountable Executive, legal counsel, OT operations) participate
- Drill simulates a realistic incident scenario and tests 24-hour CISA notification capability

### 10.3 Annual Review and Updates

This Incident Reporting section shall be reviewed and updated annually by the Cybersecurity Coordinator and approved by the Accountable Executive.

**Review Triggers** (Out-of-Cycle Updates):
- Significant cybersecurity incident occurs; lessons learned require procedure update
- TSA Security Directive updates or CISA guidance changes
- Change in Cybersecurity Coordinator or Accountable Executive contact information
- Organizational restructuring affecting incident response team composition
- Technology or monitoring changes affecting incident detection capability

**Update Process**:
1. Cybersecurity Coordinator drafts proposed updates
2. Accountable Executive reviews and approves
3. Updated section distributed to all personnel with incident response responsibilities
4. Training updated to reflect changes
5. Version history and change log maintained

**Document Version Control**:
- Version: 1.0 (Initial approval by TSA)
- Last Updated: [Date]
- Next Scheduled Review: [Date + 12 months]
- Approved By: [Accountable Executive Name and Title]

---

## 11. GLOSSARY OF TERMS

- **CCS (Critical Cyber Systems)**: Systems whose compromise could result in operational disruption, safety impact, environmental impact, or national security impact
- **CISA**: Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency; receives cybersecurity incident reports
- **CIRCIA**: Cyber Incident Reporting for Critical Infrastructure Act; requires reporting to CISA within 72 hours
- **Cybersecurity Coordinator**: Designated 24/7 point of contact for TSA and CISA; primary authority for incident reporting
- **False Positive**: Security alert that triggers an investigation but is determined not to represent a real cybersecurity incident
- **Incident**: An event that results in or is reasonably likely to result in operational disruption, safety impact, or unauthorized access to CCS
- **Incident Response Plan (IRP)**: Documented procedures for detecting, responding to, and recovering from cybersecurity incidents
- **IT (Information Technology)**: Corporate networks, servers, email, ERP systems, and business applications
- **Lateral Movement**: An attacker moving from an initial compromised system to other systems on the network
- **OT (Operational Technology)**: SCADA, DCS, PLCs, RTUs, HMIs, and field devices controlling pipeline operations
- **Root Cause Analysis**: Systematic investigation to identify why the incident occurred and what technical or procedural failures enabled it
- **SCADA (Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition)**: System for monitoring and controlling remote pipeline equipment
- **TSA**: Transportation Security Administration; issues Security Directives and reviews compliance
- **Unauthorized Access**: Any access to systems or data by parties without proper authorization

# INCIDENT REPORTING SECTION
## TransGulf Pipeline LLC - Cyber Risk Management Program (CRMP)
### TSA Security Directive Compliance

---

## 1. OVERVIEW AND OBJECTIVES

### 1.1 Purpose
This section establishes the Incident Reporting procedures for TransGulf Pipeline LLC to detect, report, and respond to cybersecurity incidents affecting critical pipeline infrastructure. The procedures comply with Transportation Security Administration (TSA) Security Directives, including SD-1571-14-03 and related guidance, ensuring timely notification to appropriate authorities and stakeholders.

### 1.2 Scope
This section applies to all cybersecurity incidents affecting:
- Critical information systems and industrial control systems (ICS)
- Supervisory control and data acquisition (SCADA) systems
- Network and data infrastructure supporting pipeline operations
- Safety and security systems
- All systems with potential impact on pipeline safety, reliability, or data integrity

### 1.3 Objectives
- Establish clear procedures for detecting and identifying cybersecurity incidents
- Define reporting timelines and notification requirements
- Ensure compliance with federal notification requirements
- Maintain incident documentation for regulatory review
- Enable rapid response and containment of security incidents
- Facilitate root cause analysis and preventive measures

---

## 2. INCIDENT CLASSIFICATION AND DEFINITIONS

### 2.1 Incident Categories

#### 2.1.1 Critical Infrastructure Incident (Reportable)
A cybersecurity event that compromises or threatens to compromise the safety, security, resilience, or continuity of critical pipeline infrastructure, including:
- Unauthorized access to SCADA/ICS systems
- Loss of control or monitoring capabilities
- Compromise of safety systems or interlocks
- Data integrity violations affecting operations
- Denial of service attacks impacting operations
- Malware or ransomware affecting industrial control systems

#### 2.1.2 High-Impact Incident (Reportable)
An incident with significant potential consequences including:
- Compromise of systems with direct impact on pipeline operations
- Theft of sensitive operational or security information
- Significant degradation of system functionality
- Breach affecting customer data or confidential business information
- Intrusion into secured networks with evidence of lateral movement
- Successful exploitation of vulnerabilities in critical systems

#### 2.1.3 Medium-Impact Incident (Potentially Reportable)
An incident with moderate risk including:
- Unsuccessful intrusion attempts with evidence of advanced reconnaissance
- Compromise of non-critical systems with potential pathway to critical systems
- Malware detection in operational technology networks without confirmed execution
- Suspicious activity suggesting social engineering targeting critical personnel
- Unauthorized access to low-sensitivity systems

#### 2.1.4 Low-Impact Incident (Internal Tracking)
An incident with minimal security impact including:
- Failed authentication attempts within normal parameters
- Low-risk policy violations
- Software vulnerabilities in non-critical systems
- Minor security control deficiencies
- Antivirus detections of known low-risk threats

### 2.2 Incident Characteristics
For classification purposes, incidents shall be characterized by:
- **Attack Vector**: External, internal, or physical
- **Attack Type**: Malware, intrusion, social engineering, physical tampering, system misconfiguration
- **Affected System**: Critical control systems, business systems, network infrastructure
- **Data Involved**: Operational data, customer data, credentials, proprietary information
- **Business Impact**: Operational disruption, data loss, confidentiality breach, integrity compromise
- **Severity Level**: Critical, High, Medium, Low

---

## 3. INCIDENT DETECTION AND IDENTIFICATION

### 3.1 Detection Mechanisms

#### 3.1.1 Security Monitoring Systems
- Real-time monitoring of network traffic and access logs
- Host-based intrusion detection systems (HIDS) on critical servers
- Network-based intrusion detection systems (NIDS) monitoring OT networks
- Endpoint detection and response (EDR) solutions on critical workstations
- SCADA/ICS system anomaly detection
- Database activity monitoring and file integrity monitoring
- Security information and event management (SIEM) systems

#### 3.1.2 System Alerts and Notifications
- Firewall and access control alerts
- Authentication system failure notifications
- Antivirus and anti-malware detections
- Patch management compliance alerts
- Account lockout notifications
- Vulnerability scanner results
- Configuration change alerts

#### 3.1.3 Manual Detection and Reporting
- User reports of suspicious activity
- System administrator observations
- Regulatory or third-party notifications
- Security audit findings
- Threat intelligence reports
- Physical security observations

### 3.2 Incident Identification Process

#### 3.2.1 Initial Assessment
Upon detection of a potential incident, the initial reporter or system:
1. **Documents** the initial observation with timestamp and context
2. **Notifies** the Security Operations Center (SOC) or on-call security personnel immediately
3. **Preserves** evidence without contamination or alteration
4. **Isolates** affected systems if immediate threat is apparent, subject to operational safety review
5. **Initiates** incident log entry with preliminary information

#### 3.2.2 Preliminary Classification
The initial assessment team shall:
1. Determine the **nature** of the potential incident
2. Assess **affected systems** and data
3. Evaluate **immediate risk** to critical operations
4. Classify **tentative impact level** (Critical/High/Medium/Low)
5. Determine **if reportable** under federal requirements
6. Assign **incident ID** and severity designation

#### 3.2.3 Escalation Criteria
Incidents shall be immediately escalated to incident management leadership if:
- Confirmed compromise of critical infrastructure systems
- Potential impact on pipeline safety or operational reliability
- Compromise affecting multiple systems or departments
- Evidence of advanced persistent threat (APT) activity
- Insider threat indicators
- Regulatory notification requirements triggered
- Media or public notice anticipated

---

## 4. INCIDENT REPORTING REQUIREMENTS

### 4.1 Mandatory Federal Reporting

#### 4.1.1 TSA Notification Requirements
TransGulf Pipeline LLC shall notify the TSA Transportation Security Operations Center (TSOC) of any cybersecurity incident affecting critical pipeline infrastructure within the timeframes specified:

**Immediate Notification (Verbal - 1 hour or less):**
- Any confirmed compromise of SCADA/ICS systems
- Loss of operational visibility or control capabilities
- Active intrusion affecting critical systems
- Incidents with imminent threat to safety or operations
- Any ransomware targeting operational technology systems

**Written Notification (24-72 hours):**
- All Critical or High-impact incidents requiring TSA reporting
- Incidents with confirmed data theft or system compromise
- Incidents indicating sophisticated attack techniques
- Incidents requiring law enforcement engagement

#### 4.1.2 Reporting Contact Information
- **TSA TSOC Hotline**: 1-877-TSA-5272 (1-877-872-5272)
- **TSA Email**: tsoc@tsa.dhs.gov (for written reports)
- **CISA**: For incidents involving national critical infrastructure
- **FBI Cyber Division**: For incidents involving criminal activity

#### 4.1.3 Information to Include in Reports
- **Incident ID**: Unique identifier assigned by TransGulf
- **Date/Time Discovered**: Timestamp of detection
- **Nature of Incident**: Detailed description of what occurred
- **Affected Systems**: Specific systems compromised or threatened
- **Current Status**: Ongoing, contained, resolved
- **Immediate Actions Taken**: Containment, mitigation, evidence preservation
- **Estimated Impact**: Safety implications, operational impact, data involved
- **Contact Information**: Designated incident response team member
- **Initial Assessment of Cause**: Preliminary determination of attack vector
- **Preliminary Indicators of Compromise (IOCs)**

### 4.2 Regulatory and Compliance Reporting

#### 4.2.1 SEC Notification (if applicable)
For incidents meeting materiality thresholds:
- Material cybersecurity incidents affecting publicly-traded parent companies
- Breach notification within timelines specified in SEC guidance
- Disclosure through 8-K filings or annual reports
- Coordination with legal and investor relations departments

#### 4.2.2 Law Enforcement Coordination
- **FBI**: For incidents involving criminal intent or nation-state activities
- **Secret Service**: For financial system compromises
- **State Attorney General**: For incidents involving state residents' personal information
- **Local Law Enforcement**: For physical security incidents or on-site intrusions

#### 4.2.3 Customer and Stakeholder Notification
- Notification to affected customers within regulatory timeframes
- Communication to business partners and vendors as appropriate
- Public notification when required by law or regulatory guidance
- Prepared statement coordination with public affairs department

### 4.3 Internal Reporting Requirements

#### 4.3.1 Incident Reporting Chain
1. **Initial Reporter** → Security Operations Center
2. **SOC/Security Team** → Information Security Manager
3. **Information Security Manager** → Chief Information Security Officer (CISO)
4. **CISO** → Chief Risk Officer / Incident Management Committee
5. **Leadership Committee** → Executive Management and Board (if applicable)

#### 4.3.2 Reporting Timeline
- **Immediate (0-2 hours)**: Verbal notification to on-call security personnel
- **Urgent (0-4 hours)**: CISO notification for Critical/High incidents
- **Formal (0-24 hours)**: Written incident report with preliminary assessment
- **Initial Report (24-48 hours)**: Comprehensive incident summary
- **Investigative Updates (ongoing)**: Daily status updates during active investigation
- **Final Report (5-10 business days)**: Complete incident documentation and root cause analysis

#### 4.3.3 Escalation Notifications
- **Critical Incidents**: CEO, Chief Operating Officer, Board Security Committee
- **High-Impact Incidents**: Executive leadership, relevant department heads
- **Medium-Impact Incidents**: CISO, relevant department management
- **Low-Impact Incidents**: Security team and affected department notification

---

## 5. INCIDENT REPORTING PROCEDURES

### 5.1 Step-by-Step Reporting Process

#### Step 1: Initial Detection and Notification
```
Action: Security personnel or system detects anomalous activity
Timeline: Immediate upon detection
Responsibility: Any employee, system monitor, or automated alert
Output: Incident ID assigned, initial alert logged in SIEM/ticketing system
```

#### Step 2: Preliminary Assessment
```
Action: SOC analyst or on-call security engineer performs initial triage
Timeline: Within 30 minutes of notification
Assessment includes:
  - Verification of incident (not false positive)
  - Identification of affected systems
  - Assessment of immediate risk
  - Preliminary impact classification
Responsibility: Security Operations Center
Output: Incident severity level assigned, escalation decision made
```

#### Step 3: Evidence Preservation
```
Action: Secure evidence without altering systems where operationally possible
Timeline: Immediately upon confirmation
Methods:
  - Preserve system logs and network traffic
  - Document system state (screenshots, memory dumps if appropriate)
  - Preserve communication records and timestamps
  - Maintain chain of custody for evidence
Responsibility: Security team with IT operations coordination
Output: Evidence documentation log, chain of custody records
```

#### Step 4: Immediate Containment (if required)
```
Action: Implement containment measures for active threats
Timeline: As soon as safety permits
Actions may include:
  - Network isolation of compromised systems
  - Credential revocation for compromised accounts
  - Malware quarantine and system cleaning
  - Access control modifications
Responsibility: Security team with operations/IT oversight
Output: Containment action log, system status documentation
```

#### Step 5: Leadership Notification
```
Action: Notify appropriate management levels based on severity
Timeline: Within 2-4 hours for Critical/High, within 24 hours for others
Notification method:
  - Verbal briefing for Critical incidents
  - Email summary for High/Medium incidents
Responsibility: CISO or designated incident commander
Output: Management acknowledgment, authorization for response actions
```

#### Step 6: Regulatory Assessment
```
Action: Determine if incident meets federal reporting thresholds
Timeline: Within 6 hours of classification
Assessment includes:
  - Critical infrastructure impact evaluation
  - CFAA or other federal crime indicators
  - State breach notification requirements
  - SEC materiality considerations
Responsibility: CISO with legal counsel consultation
Output: Reporting determination document, notification timeline decision
```

#### Step 7: Federal Notification (if required)
```
Action: Notify TSA and other federal agencies per requirements
Timeline: Within 1 hour for verbal notification, 24-72 hours for written
Notification method:
  - Telephone for verbal notification to TSA TSOC
  - Email or web portal for written notification
  - Follow-up updates as investigation progresses
Responsibility: CISO or designated company spokesperson
Output: Notification confirmation, incident reference numbers
```

#### Step 8: Investigation Initiation
```
Action: Launch comprehensive incident investigation
Timeline: Begin immediately; intensive investigation within 24 hours
Investigation includes:
  - System forensics and log analysis
  - Network traffic analysis
  - Malware analysis (if applicable)
  - Timeline reconstruction
  - Root cause analysis
  - Attribution analysis
Responsibility: Incident response team with IT forensics specialists
Output: Investigation reports, preliminary findings (daily), final report
```

#### Step 9: Stakeholder Communication
```
Action: Update customers, partners, and other stakeholders
Timeline: As appropriate per contractual and legal requirements
Communication includes:
  - Notification of affected parties
  - Description of incident and response
  - Guidance for remediation (if customer action required)
  - Status updates
Responsibility: CISO with customer service and legal coordination
Output: Communication logs, recipient confirmations
```

#### Step 10: Closure and Post-Incident Review
```
Action: Document lessons learned and implement preventive measures
Timeline: Within 5-10 business days of resolution
Documentation includes:
  - Final incident report
  - Root cause analysis
  - Timeline of events
  - Recommendations for improvement
  - Metrics and impact assessment
Responsibility: Incident management committee
Output: Final report, action items for remediation
```

### 5.2 Incident Report Documentation

#### 5.2.1 Required Report Elements
All incident reports shall include:

**Header Information:**
- Incident ID (unique identifier)
- Report Date and Time
- Reporting Officer/Organization
- Classification Level (if sensitive)

**Incident Summary:**
- Brief description (2-3 sentences)
- Date/Time of Discovery
- Date/Time of Occurrence (if known)
- Current Status (Active/Contained/Resolved)
- Severity Classification (Critical/High/Medium/Low)

**Affected Systems and Data:**
- List of systems compromised or threatened
- Type of systems (SCADA, business, network, etc.)
- Number of affected systems
- Data types affected (operational, customer, proprietary, etc.)
- Estimated volume of data involved (if breach)

**Incident Details:**
- Complete description of what occurred
- Attack vector and method used
- Evidence of compromise (malware, unauthorized access, etc.)
- Scope of compromise (number of systems, accounts, data records)
- Timeline of events with specific timestamps

**Impact Assessment:**
- Operational impact (if any)
- Safety implications (if any)
- Data confidentiality breach description
- Data integrity violations
- Business continuity implications
- Financial impact (estimated if available)

**Immediate Actions Taken:**
- Containment measures implemented
- Systems isolated or taken offline
- Credentials reset or revoked
- Law enforcement or regulatory notifications
- Evidence preservation steps
- Communication notifications sent

**Investigation Status:**
- Current phase of investigation
- Key findings to date
- Systems being analyzed
- Indicators of compromise identified
- Preliminary attribution assessment

**Regulatory Reporting Determination:**
- Does incident meet TSA reporting threshold? (Yes/No/Undetermined)
- Does incident require federal agency notification? (Yes/No)
- Agencies to be notified (TSA, FBI, CISA, etc.)
- Notification timeline and method
- Contact points for coordinating agencies

**Contact Information:**
- Incident Commander name and title
- 24-hour contact number
- Email address
- Backup contact information

**Approvals:**
- CISO signature/approval
- Chief Risk Officer signature (if required)
- Date of approval

#### 5.2.2 Report Distribution
- Original: Incident management file (secure location)
- Copy: CISO office (encrypted storage)
- Copy: Legal counsel (attorney-client privilege)
- Copy: Regulatory file (if required)
- Redacted copy: IT management (operational briefing)
- Executive summary: Executive leadership (if Critical)

### 5.3 Incident Notification Templates

#### 5.3.1 TSA Verbal Notification Script
```
"Good [morning/afternoon]. I am [Name, Title] with TransGulf Pipeline LLC.
We are reporting a cybersecurity incident affecting our critical infrastructure.

Incident ID: [ID Number]
Discovery Time: [Date/Time]
System(s) Affected: [System descriptions]
Nature of Incident: [Brief description]
Current Status: [Active/Contained/Resolved]
Safety Impact: [Immediate threat assessment]

We are implementing containment measures and conducting investigation.
Detailed written report to follow within [24-72 hours].
Primary Contact: [Name/Number]"
```

#### 5.3.2 Regulatory Written Notification Format
```
Subject: Cybersecurity Incident Report - TransGulf Pipeline LLC

To: [TSA TSOC / Other Agency]

INCIDENT INFORMATION:
- Incident ID: [Assigned ID]
- Reporting Organization: TransGulf Pipeline LLC
- Report Submission Date/Time: [ISO 8601 timestamp]
- Date/Time of Incident Discovery: [ISO 8601 timestamp]
- Date/Time of Incident Occurrence: [ISO 8601 timestamp, if known]

INCIDENT DESCRIPTION:
[Detailed narrative of incident, attack methods, affected systems]

SYSTEMS AFFECTED:
[List of critical systems with descriptions]

CURRENT STATUS:
[Containment status, remediation activities]

PRELIMINARY ROOT CAUSE:
[Initial assessment of cause and attribution]

IMPACT ASSESSMENT:
[Operational, safety, and data impact]

CONTACT INFORMATION:
[24-hour incident response contact]

INVESTIGATION TIMELINE:
[Expected updates and final report submission date]
```

## 6. REPORTING TIMELINES AND DEADLINES

### 6.1 Immediate Response Phase (0-2 Hours)
- Incident detection and alert escalation
- Initial notification to on-call security personnel
- Verbal reporting to leadership (Critical incidents)
- Critical containment measures implemented
- Evidence preservation initiated

### 6.2 Urgent Response Phase (2-24 Hours)
- CISO notification and assessment
- Written incident report initiated
- Regulatory reporting determination
- Verbal notification to TSA (if required)
- Investigation team assembled
- Stakeholder notification plan developed

### 6.3 Formal Reporting Phase (24-72 Hours)
- Written notification to TSA and other agencies (if required)
- Comprehensive incident report delivered to leadership
- Investigation narrative completed
- Preliminary root cause assessment
- Customer/partner notifications (if required)
- Initial remediation plan documented

### 6.4 Investigation Phase (Ongoing - 5-10 Business Days)
- Detailed forensic analysis
- Complete timeline reconstruction
- Root cause analysis
- Recommendations for preventive measures
- Final incident report prepared
- Lessons learned documentation

### 6.5 Closure and Follow-up Phase (10+ Business Days)
- Post-incident review meeting
- Implementation of corrective actions
- Preventive measures deployed
- Training and awareness updates
- Regulatory follow-up reports (if applicable)
- Final documentation archival

---

## 7. SPECIAL REPORTING CIRCUMSTANCES

### 7.1 Insider Threat Incidents
For incidents involving or suspected employee involvement:
- Immediate Human Resources notification (confidential)
- Law enforcement coordination for criminal activity
- Legal counsel involvement before employee notification
- Specialized investigation procedures
- Enhanced documentation and chain of custody
- Background investigation protocols

### 7.2 Third-Party/Vendor Incidents
For incidents involving service providers or vendors:
- Vendor incident response activation
- Contract obligation notification
- Supply chain risk assessment
- Customer impact notification (if applicable)
- Vendor cooperation requirements documentation
- Post-incident vendor performance review

### 7.3 Multi-Organization Incidents
For incidents affecting multiple organizations:
- Coordination with affected organizations
- Centralized incident command (if TransGulf is primary)
- Information sharing protocols per legal agreements
- Joint notification to regulators
- Unified response and remediation approach

### 7.4 National Security-Related Incidents
For incidents involving suspected nation-state or foreign intelligence activity:
- Immediate FBI notification
- CISA coordination
- Enhanced classification and compartmentalization
- Restricted information handling (need-to-know)
- Government agency cooperation
- Potential CFAA criminal investigation

### 7.5 Supply Chain Compromises
For incidents affecting supply chain or dependent systems:
- Upstream/downstream notification
- Customer communication regarding service continuity
- Third-party risk assessment
- Coordinated remediation efforts
- Supply chain integrity verification
- Enhanced monitoring of dependent systems

---

## 8. INCIDENT DOCUMENTATION AND RECORDKEEPING

### 8.1 Documentation Standards
All incident reports shall:
- Use consistent formatting and terminology
- Include complete timestamps (ISO 8601 format with timezone)
- Provide objective, factual descriptions without speculation
- Distinguish between confirmed facts and preliminary assessments
- Reference supporting documentation (logs, screenshots, etc.)
- Maintain professional language appropriate for regulatory review
- Include revision history for updated reports

### 8.2 Evidence and Artifact Management
- **Chain of Custody**: Documented for all forensic evidence
- **Log Retention**: Maintain logs per industry standards (minimum 90 days)
- **Secure Storage**: Encrypted storage for sensitive incident documentation
- **Access Controls**: Restrict access per incident classification
- **Archival**: Long-term storage of final reports (minimum 7 years)
- **Destruction**: Secure deletion of evidence per policy completion

### 8.3 Incident Record Retention
TransGulf Pipeline LLC shall maintain:
- Complete incident reports: 7 years minimum
- Forensic evidence: Per legal hold requirements
- Preliminary reports and updates: 3 years minimum
- Regulatory correspondence: Per agency requirements
- Lessons learned documentation: Permanent
- Trend analysis data: 3 years for metrics and reporting

### 8.4 Incident Log and Database
A centralized incident management system shall maintain:
- Unique incident IDs
- Incident classification and severity
- Discovery date/time and incident date/time
- Affected systems and data summary
- Reporter and investigator information
- Current status and resolution date
- Regulatory reporting status
- Key metrics and statistics

- Pre-approved statements for media inquiries

### 13.2 Classification Guidelines Reference

- **Medium**: Compromise of important but non-critical systems
- **Low**: Minor violations or low-impact events

### 13.3 Federal Reporting Decision Tree
1. Is critical infrastructure affected? → Likely TSA reportable
2. Is there evidence of breach/intrusion? → Likely TSA reportable
3. Could there be federal crime implications? → Coordinate with FBI
4. Does it affect customer/personal data? → Check breach notification laws
5. Is parent company publicly traded? → Check SEC materiality requirements

# ISO 42001:2023 Gap Assessment — NexaAI Ltd

**Date:** 25 March 2026
**Organisation:** NexaAI Ltd (SaaS)
**Assessment Type:** Baseline Gap Analysis
**Current AIMS Maturity:** Zero documentation (0/10)
**Target:** ISO 42001:2023 Certification readiness

---

## Executive Summary

NexaAI Ltd is a SaaS company operating as an **AI provider** with three AI-powered features in production:
1. **Automated email drafting** (sales support) — content generation AI
2. **AI-powered resume screening** (HR tool) — decision-support/ranking system
3. **Customer-facing support chatbot** — autonomous decision-making for issue resolution

**Organisational Role Classification:**
- **Primary: AI Provider** — develops and deploys AI systems for paying customers
- **Secondary: AI User** — integrates OpenAI's GPT-4 API as underlying technology

**Current State:** Zero documented AIMS controls. No formal governance, risk assessment, policies, or lifecycle management for the three in-scope AI systems.

**Certification Readiness:** At baseline (Stage 0). Estimated effort to Stage 1 readiness: 8–12 weeks. Stage 2 (full operational implementation): 16–24 weeks.

---
