## Detailed AI System Impact Assessment (AISIA)

**Mandatory per Clause 6.1.2. Required for each AI system in scope.**

### AI System 1: Automated Email Drafting

**Intended Purpose:** Generate draft sales emails based on customer information and sales representative input to improve productivity and consistency in outreach.

| AISIA Dimension | Assessment | Impact Level Indicator |
|---|---|---|
| **Output Type** | Content generation (email text) | Medium |
| **Impact Domain** | Commercial communications, employment (sales team efficiency) | Medium |
| **Affected Population** | Sales recipients (external customers): potentially thousands of email recipients unaware AI assisted | Medium–High |
| **Severity if Fails** | Email tone issues (unprofessional, offensive), hallucinated product claims (legal risk, customer trust damage), repetitive messaging (brand damage) | Medium–High |
| **Reversibility** | Reversible if human reviews before sending; some reputational harm if customers receive problematic drafts | Medium |
| **Human Oversight** | Sales rep reviews and edits before sending — MUST BE DOCUMENTED | Yes (critical) |
| **Vulnerability of Audience** | General audience (recipients may not know AI-assisted), no special vulnerability category | Low |
| **Scale** | High (thousands of emails per week) | High |

**AISIA Classification: MEDIUM**

**Control Implications:**
- A.5.3: Human review mandatory before email dispatch; log 100% of emails (timestamp, reviewer, changes made)
- A.6.2: Define intended purpose (this assessment); update when email templates or customer segments change
- A.7: Training data governance (what prior emails were used to train or fine-tune model?) — document data sources
- A.8: Incident management for "AI generated inappropriate content" or "hallucination of product features"
- Transparency obligation: Consider disclosing AI use to recipients (depends on marketing regulations in target territories)

**Recommended Controls:**
- Content filter on generated emails (flag profanity, product claims, competitor mention)
- Audit trail of sales rep review/edits
- Monthly analysis of refusal/edit rates
- Quarterly retraining on responsible messaging

---

### AI System 2: Resume Screening (Candidate Ranking)

**Intended Purpose:** Rank job candidates by predicted job fit/performance using resume text and candidate profile data to reduce recruitment processing time and bias in initial screening.

| AISIA Dimension | Assessment | Impact Level Indicator |
|---|---|---|
| **Output Type** | Ranking/scoring (autonomous decision support; HR uses scores to shortlist) | High |
| **Impact Domain** | Employment (hiring decisions affecting individuals' economic outcomes) | High |
| **Affected Population** | Job candidates (hundreds to thousands per hiring cycle); vulnerable group (job seekers) | High |
| **Severity if Fails** | Systematic exclusion of qualified candidates (gender, age, ethnicity bias); discriminatory outcomes; erosion of fair opportunity; legal liability (employment law, discrimination claims) | High |
| **Reversibility** | Partially reversible if bias detected and candidates re-screened; reputational harm if discovered | Medium |
| **Human Oversight** | HR team reviews top candidates before interview; however, low-ranked candidates may be automatically rejected without human review | Weak |
| **Vulnerability of Audience** | Job seekers = vulnerable population; may not know they've been AI-screened | High |
| **Scale** | Medium–High (hundreds of applicants per hire cycle) | Medium–High |

**AISIA Classification: HIGH**

**Control Implications:**
- A.5.3: **Mandatory human review** of all resume scoring; document that humans make final hiring decisions, not AI
- A.6.2: Detailed intended purpose (job fit definition, skills weighting, data sources)
- A.7: **Critical data governance**: training data audit (what historical resumes/hiring outcomes?), bias testing protocol (gender, age, ethnicity proxy detection), demographic parity testing
- A.8: Incident management for "bias detected in rankings" or "AI rejected qualified candidates"
- A.5.2: **Transparency obligation**: Candidates must be informed that AI is used in initial screening; right to explanation if rejected without human review
- A.10: Adverse decision record (ADR) — for candidates rejected at AI screening stage, maintain record that decision was made and basis

**Recommended Controls:**
- Bias audit every 6 months (test model on synthetic candidates with different demographic attributes)
- Impact assessment update if training data source or job categories change
- Fairness dashboard (tracking hiring rates by demographic to detect disparate impact)
- Policy: All candidates in top N are human-reviewed; no automatic rejections below threshold
- Transparency statement in job posting and rejection emails

---

### AI System 3: Customer-Facing Support Chatbot

**Intended Purpose:** Provide first-line customer support by answering common product questions and routing complex issues to human agents; reduce support ticket volume.

| AISIA Dimension | Assessment | Impact Level Indicator |
|---|---|---|
| **Output Type** | Autonomous decision-making + content generation (chatbot decides when to escalate to human vs. provide resolution) | High |
| **Impact Domain** | Customer service, customer economic outcome (resolution quality affects product satisfaction and customer retention) | Medium–High |
| **Affected Population** | Customers of NexaAI (potentially thousands using chatbot daily) | High |
| **Severity if Fails** | Misinformation (incorrect product advice), hallucinated solutions (customer frustration, support workload spike), security risk (chatbot divulges API keys or sensitive product info), escalation failure (customer issue unresolved) | High |
| **Reversibility** | Partially reversible if human escalation works; some customer trust/satisfaction loss if bad interactions occur | Medium |
| **Human Oversight** | Human agent handles escalations; logs of escalation rate, resolution quality, and customer satisfaction available? | Medium |
| **Vulnerability of Audience** | Customers are not a vulnerable population per se, but may be business-critical (SaaS customers losing support = revenue risk) | Medium |
| **Scale** | Very high (chatbot may handle 100s–1000s of conversations daily) | High |

**AISIA Classification: HIGH**

**Control Implications:**
- A.5.3: **Escalation trigger governance** — define when chatbot escalates to human; log all escalations; human reviews escalated issues promptly
- A.6.2: Intended purpose documentation (scope of supported questions, escalation rules, decision logic)
- A.7: Training data governance (what customer support conversations were used to train chatbot?), hallucination risk, knowledge base update process
- A.8: Incident management for "chatbot provided incorrect technical advice" or "inappropriate response" or "security-sensitive information disclosed"
- A.5.2: **Transparency**: Customers aware interacting with AI chatbot; clear path to human agent if needed
- A.10: Adverse decision record (if chatbot refuses service or provides resolution customer disputes)

**Recommended Controls:**
- Escalation rate monitoring (target: escalation rate <5% for safe, well-trained chatbot)
- Hallucination detection (customer complaint monitoring for "chatbot told me X but that's wrong")
- Security audit (ensure chatbot cannot be prompted to reveal API keys, customer data, or system architecture)
- Monthly conversation sampling and quality review by support manager
- Customer satisfaction survey on chatbot interactions

---

## Detailed AI Risk Assessment

**Mandatory per Clause 6.1.2. Separate from AISIA; focuses on likelihood × severity.**

### Risk Register Template (Applied to NexaAI)

| Risk ID | Risk Category | Risk Description | Likelihood | Severity | Risk Level | Potential Impact | Treatment Strategy | Responsible Party |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **AIR-001** | Model/Bias | Resume screening model shows gender bias; rejects female candidates at higher rate | Medium | High | **High** | Legal liability, discrimination claims, reputational damage, hiring quality drop | Modify: conduct bias audit, retrain model with balanced training set; Accept: establish monitoring threshold (track hiring rates by gender monthly) | AI Governance Lead + Data Science Team |
| **AIR-002** | Model/Accuracy | Email drafting generates hallucinated product features (e.g., "our AI can predict customer churn 6 months early" when capability doesn't exist) | Medium | Medium | **Medium** | Customer trust damage, legal exposure (false advertising), sales credibility loss | Modify: implement content filter for claim verification; human review mandatory | Sales Ops + Compliance |
| **AIR-003** | Data Quality | Resume screening trained on historical hiring data which reflects past bias; model perpetuates bias | High | High | **High** | Systematic discrimination, legal/regulatory risk | Modify: audit training data for bias; remove/balance biased samples; retrain model | Data Science + Legal |
| **AIR-004** | Operational | Chatbot hallucination: provides false solution to customer issue, customer applies it and causes data loss | Medium | High | **High** | Customer harm, liability, support burden spike | Modify: narrow chatbot scope to FAQ-only; escalate all technical issues to human; implement verification step | Product + Support Lead |
| **AIR-005** | Supply Chain | OpenAI API outage: email drafting, chatbot both depend on GPT-4; service unavailable | Medium | Medium | **Medium** | Customer SaaS outage, revenue impact, customer churn | Accept: monitor uptime; Mitigate: implement fallback (templated responses); Transfer: contractual SLA with OpenAI | Ops + DevOps |
| **AIR-006** | Supply Chain | OpenAI changes GPT-4 model behavior or limits API access; NexaAI features break or degrade | Low | High | **Medium** | Feature degradation, development effort to retrain own model, customer dissatisfaction | Mitigate: monitor OpenAI roadmap; maintain internal model alternative; Transfer: contract review, API SLA review | Product + Engineering |
| **AIR-007** | Data Privacy | Training data for chatbot includes customer conversation records; privacy breach if data exfiltrated | Medium | High | **High** | GDPR/privacy liability, customer trust, regulatory fines | Modify: anonymize/exclude PII from training; limit training data retention; Transfer: contractual obligations to OpenAI re: data use | Data Privacy Officer |
| **AIR-008** | Operational | Model drift: over time, as customer base changes or products evolve, resume screening or chatbot models degrade in accuracy; not detected in time | Medium | Medium | **Medium** | Hiring quality drop, customer support quality drop, undetected decline | Modify: implement monitoring for model performance metrics (accuracy, F1 score, drift detection); retrain monthly or when metrics degrade | Data Science + Monitoring Team |
| **AIR-009** | Societal/Governance | Resume screening enables discriminatory hiring at scale; societal impact of excluding candidates from employment at scale | Low | Very High | **High** | Systemic discrimination, regulatory/legal action (EEOC, labor boards), reputational destruction, business shutdown risk | Modify: implement fairness controls, human review, transparency; Accept: with mandatory monitoring and transparency | Governance + Legal |
| **AIR-010** | Operational | Lack of documentation: no clear intended purpose, no lifecycle controls, no incident response plan; cannot demonstrate responsible use if challenged by regulator | High | High | **High** | Regulatory non-compliance, inability to defend AI use, audit failure | Modify: complete AIMS documentation (this assessment is a start); establish governance framework | AI Governance Lead |

**Overall Risk Assessment Summary:**
- **High Risk (7 identified):** Resume screening bias, email hallucinations, chatbot misinformation, training data privacy, discriminatory hiring at scale, lack of governance documentation, data quality bias
- **Medium Risk (3 identified):** OpenAI outage, model drift, model behavior changes
- **Risk Appetite:** NexaAI must establish written risk appetite; recommendation: zero tolerance for employment discrimination, regulatory violation; acceptance with monitoring for operational/supply chain risks

## Recommended Implementation Roadmap

### Phase 1: Foundation (Weeks 1–4) — Stage 1 Audit Readiness

**Objective:** Establish documented AIMS foundation and secure management commitment.

**Deliverables:**
1. **AIMS Scope Document** (Clause 4.3)
   - Define AI systems in scope (3 systems), organisational boundaries, internal/external stakeholders
   - Map to OpenAI GPT-4 dependency

2. **AI System Register** (Clause 4.1)
   - Name, description, intended purpose, owner, deployment status for each system

3. **AI Policy** (Clause 5.2) — signed by CEO/CTO
   - Governance structure, responsible AI principles, compliance commitment

4. **Stakeholder & Interested Party Register** (Clause 4.2)
   - Sales team, HR, customers, OpenAI, regulators, data subjects

5. **AISIA Reports** (Clause 6.1.2) — one per AI system
   - Use templates above; classify impact level (Medium/High)

6. **AI Risk Register** (Clause 6.1.2)
   - Use risk register above; prioritize treatment for High risks

7. **Roles & Responsibilities (RACI)** (Clause 5.3)
   - AI Governance Lead (new hire or external consultant)
   - System Owners (email, resume, chatbot)
   - Data Governance Lead
   - Internal Auditor

**Effort:** 400–600 hours (1–2 FTE for 4 weeks)

**Cost Estimate:** £8,000–15,000 (in-house + external guidance)

---

### Phase 2: Control Implementation (Weeks 5–12) — Stage 2 Readiness

**Objective:** Implement operational controls, data governance, and incident management.

**Deliverables:**

**Cluster A: Data Governance & AI Lifecycle (A.6, A.7)**
- AI system lifecycle procedures (design → deploy → monitor → retire)
- Data governance policy: training data sourcing, quality, bias testing
- Bias audit plan (6-month cadence for resume screening)
- Competence and awareness training program
- Model cards for each AI system (capabilities, limitations, performance)

**Cluster B: Human Oversight & Transparency (A.5.2, A.5.3)**
- Formalise human review process for email drafting (100% review + audit trail)
- Escalation procedure for resume screening (all candidates above threshold get human review)
- Chatbot escalation rate monitoring (target <5%)
- Transparency statements: update website, product docs, ToS to disclose AI use
- Adverse Decision Record (ADR) process for resume rejections

**Cluster C: Supply Chain & Incident Management (A.8, A.9)**
- OpenAI AI due diligence: assess API documentation, SLA, security, incident response
- Contract review: ensure AI-specific clauses (data protection, SLA, liability, model changes notification)
- AI-specific incident classification (bias detected, hallucination, unexpected output, data breach, model drift)
- Incident response playbook for each AI system
- Incident log setup (even if no incidents yet, demonstrate the mechanism)

**Cluster D: Governance Framework (Clauses 5–10)**
- Document control procedure (extend to include AI artifacts: model cards, training data logs, AISIA)
- AIMS objectives (measurable, linked to responsible AI): e.g., "Zero critical bias incidents", "95% chatbot accuracy", "100% email review compliance"
- Communication plan (internal + external + incident communication)
- Management review schedule (quarterly); agenda template
- Internal audit plan (annual, covering all clauses and controls)

**Effort:** 800–1,200 hours (2–3 FTE for 8 weeks)

**Cost Estimate:** £16,000–30,000 (implementation + external audit prep)

---

### Phase 3: Audit Readiness & Certification (Weeks 13–24)

**Objective:** Complete Stage 1 & Stage 2 external audits; achieve ISO 42001:2023 certification.

**Stage 1 (Documentary) Audit (Week 13–14)**
- Certification body reviews AIMS scope, policies, risk assessment, AISIA, SoA, objectives, documented controls
- Expected findings: minor formatting/clarity gaps (typical)
- Corrective actions: 1–2 weeks

**Stage 2 (Implementation Verification) Audit (Week 16–18)**
- Certification body tests controls in operation: interviews staff, reviews execution evidence, samples AI system records, tests incident response
- Expected focus: Are humans actually reviewing emails? Is bias testing happening? Is OpenAI SLA enforced?
- Evidence gathering (weeks 14–15): competence training records, audit logs, bias test results, incident handling demos

**Post-Audit (Weeks 18–24)**
- Corrective action closure
- Certificate issuance
- Surveillance audit planning (annual)

**Effort:** 200–400 hours (audit prep + response + corrective actions)

**Cost Estimate:** £3,000–8,000 (certification body fees) + internal time

---

| Phase | Duration | Key Outputs | Effort (FTE-weeks) |
|-------|----------|-------------|----|

| **Total** | **24 weeks (6 months)** | **ISO 42001 Certification** | **14–22 FTE-weeks** |

**Recommended Team Composition:**
- 1 AI Governance Lead (new hire or external consultant, full-time for 6 months): £50–80k
- 1 Data Science/Engineering resource (part-time, 0.5 FTE): £30–50k
- 1 Compliance/Legal resource (part-time, 0.3 FTE): £20–30k
- External consulting (if in-house expertise lacking): £30–50k
- Certification body audit: £5–10k

**Total Investment:** £135–220k (6-month implementation to certification)

## Conclusion & Next Steps

**Current State:** NexaAI Ltd has zero documented AIMS; three AI systems (email drafting, resume screening, chatbot) operate without formal governance, risk assessment, or compliance controls. This creates regulatory, legal, and reputational risk — particularly for resume screening (employment discrimination liability) and chatbot (customer misinformation risk).

**Certification Readiness:** Stage 1 audit feasible by Week 13–14; full certification (Stage 2 + certificate) by Week 24. Estimated investment: £135–220k and 14–22 FTE-weeks.

**Immediate Actions (Next 2 Weeks):**
1. **Secure executive sponsorship** — CEO/CTO commitment to AIMS and budget approval
2. **Appoint AI Governance Lead** (internal or external consultant)
3. **Schedule kickoff meeting** — define roles, communication, Phase 1 schedule
4. **Begin AIMS Scope and AI System Register** drafting

**Success Factor:** Embed responsible AI principles and governance into product roadmap from the start; avoid AIMS as compliance-only checkbox — make it a competitive advantage (market as "ISO 42001 certified AI SaaS").

# ISO 42001:2023 Gap Assessment for NexaAI Ltd

## Executive Summary

NexaAI Ltd is pursuing ISO 42001:2023 (Artificial Intelligence Management Systems) certification with zero existing AIMS documentation. This assessment identifies critical gaps across all eight major clause areas of ISO 42001. With three AI applications leveraging OpenAI's GPT-4 API (email drafting, resume screening, and customer support chatbot), the organization faces significant compliance work but operates in manageable scope for a focused implementation.

**Overall Maturity: 0% (No AIMS in place)**

---

## 1. Context of the Organization (Clause 4)

### Current State
- No documented organizational context
- AI applications in production but not formally contextualized within AIMS
- No documented stakeholder identification

### Key Gaps

| Gap Area | Gap Description | Severity | Evidence |
|----------|-----------------|----------|----------|
| Context Documentation | No documented understanding of organizational context, purpose, or business objectives | Critical | Zero AIMS documentation |
| External/Internal Issues | No analysis of external factors (regulatory, competitive, technological) affecting AI systems | Critical | No risk registers or context statements |
| Interested Parties | No stakeholder identification or analysis (regulators, customers, employees, vendors) | High | No stakeholder matrices |
| AIMS Scope | No formally documented AIMS scope covering the three AI applications | High | No scope statements |
| AI Governance Structure | No definition of governance structures, roles, or responsibilities | Critical | No org charts or role definitions |

### Required Actions
1. Document organizational context statement including business objectives and AI strategy
2. Perform external context analysis (regulatory environment, competitive landscape)
3. Identify and analyze all interested parties (regulators, customers, employees, end-users, OpenAI)
4. Define formal AIMS scope document covering all three AI systems
5. Establish AI governance structure with clearly defined roles
6. Document organizational policies and how AI systems integrate into operations

### Compliance Evidence Needed
- Context statement (document)
- Stakeholder analysis matrix
- AIMS scope document
- Organizational policy framework
- Governance structure documentation

---

- No documented leadership commitment to AIMS
- No evidence of top management involvement in AI governance
- No AI risk consciousness apparent at leadership level

| Competence Requirements | No defined competencies for AI system roles | High | No competency frameworks |

## 5. Operation (Clause 8)

### Current State
- AI systems in production without documented operational controls
- No evidence of human oversight procedures
- No documented data governance for AI systems
- No clear process for system updates or model retraining
- No operational risk controls

### Key Gaps

| Gap Area | Gap Description | Severity | Evidence |
|----------|-----------------|----------|----------|

   - Resume screening: Accuracy metrics, bias measurements, hiring outcome tracking

   - Model version and training data
   - Known limitations and biases
   - Performance benchmarks
   - Recommended use cases and restrictions
4. Implement human oversight controls:
   - Resume screening: 100% human review of final recommendations before hiring
   - Email drafting: Sales team review before sending to customers
   - Chatbot: Human escalation for complex queries, regular performance review
5. Establish change control process for model updates:
   - Testing requirements before production deployment
   - Rollback procedures
   - Change documentation
6. Create supplier management procedure for OpenAI:
   - SLA review and management
   - Data processing agreement verification
   - API usage monitoring
   - Vendor continuity planning
7. Implement incident response procedures
8. Document data governance:
   - Data sources for each AI system
   - Data quality requirements
   - Data retention policies
   - Input data validation procedures

## Risk Analysis by AI System

### 1. AI-Powered Email Drafting for Sales

**Primary Risks:**
- **Brand/Reputation Risk**: Inappropriate email content, tone inconsistency, disclosure of confidential information
- **Privacy Risk**: Unauthorized use of customer data in training/generation
- **Accuracy Risk**: Factually incorrect or outdated information in drafts
- **Compliance Risk**: GDPR (personal data), CAN-SPAM Act (marketing emails)

**Required Controls:**
- Sales team review and approval before sending
- Training on appropriate use and limitations
- Escalation procedure for sensitive communications
- Data minimization (limit customer data sent to API)
- Regular quality audits of generated content

**Gap Rating: Critical** - Zero controls documented

### 2. AI-Powered Resume Screening

**Primary Risks:**
- **Discrimination/Bias Risk**: Systematic exclusion of protected classes (gender, race, age, disability)
- **Legal Risk**: Violation of employment laws (Title VII, ADA, state AI hiring laws)
- **Accuracy Risk**: Missing qualified candidates, false positives
- **Transparency Risk**: Inability to explain AI decisions to candidates
- **Data Protection Risk**: Storage and processing of sensitive personal information

**Required Controls:**
- Bias testing and monitoring across protected classes
- Human review of all AI rankings before hiring decisions
- Documentation of model development and training data
- Regular fairness audits
- Applicant notification of AI use in screening
- Data retention and deletion procedures
- Appeal/reconsideration process for rejected candidates

**Gap Rating: Critical** - Highest legal/ethical risk, zero controls documented

### 3. Customer-Facing Support Chatbot

**Primary Risks:**
- **Accuracy/Liability Risk**: Providing incorrect information causing customer harm
- **Security Risk**: Exposure of customer data through chatbot
- **Reputation Risk**: Poor customer experience, negative reviews
- **Compliance Risk**: Handling of regulated information
- **Availability Risk**: System failure disrupting customer support

**Required Controls:**
- Knowledge base curation and accuracy verification
- Human escalation for complex or sensitive inquiries
- Rate limiting and abuse prevention
- Conversation logging and review
- Clear disclosure that interactions are with AI
- SLA and availability monitoring
- Regular testing and updates

**Gap Rating: High** - Functional risks but lower legal risk than resume screening

## Key Recommendations

1. **Immediate Action (Week 1)**: Schedule executive steering committee meeting to approve ISO 42001 initiative. Assign dedicated project lead.

2. **High Priority**: Address resume screening bias risks first. This AI application has the highest legal/ethical risk exposure and requires the most extensive controls.

3. **Foundational Elements**: Establish governance structure, roles, and accountability before building procedures. Without this, AIMS will lack strategic direction.

4. **Supplier Relationship**: Formalize relationship with OpenAI including data processing agreements, SLAs, and terms verification. Understand data retention and usage policies.

5. **Documentation Discipline**: Implement document management system immediately. This is foundational for all subsequent documentation creation.

6. **Stakeholder Engagement**: Involve all key stakeholders (sales, HR, IT, legal) in requirements gathering. AIMS must be embedded in each function's operations.

7. **Resource Allocation**: Budget for dedicated AIMS coordinator role plus consulting support for technical implementation (monitoring, model documentation).

8. **Regulatory Monitoring**: Establish process to track evolving AI regulations (AI Act, state laws, industry guidance). Compliance obligations will increase.

9. **Bias & Fairness**: For resume screening specifically, engage fairness/ethics expertise. Consider third-party bias audits before certification.

10. **Continuous Improvement**: Build AIMS as an iterative program. Certification is not the end goal; the goal is effective AI risk management as the organization scales AI usage.

---

## Conclusion

NexaAI Ltd faces substantial work to achieve ISO 42001:2023 certification, but the scope is manageable given three well-defined AI applications. The biggest gaps are in governance, operational control (especially for resume screening), and risk management. The highest-priority actions are securing leadership commitment, documenting organizational context and roles, conducting comprehensive risk assessments (with special focus on bias in resume screening), and establishing operational oversight procedures.

With proper resource allocation and disciplined execution, certification readiness is achievable within 6 months. However, this assumes significant organizational investment in documentation, process development, and ongoing monitoring/improvement infrastructure. The investment is critical not only for certification but for protecting the organization from legal, regulatory, and reputational risks associated with AI systems currently in production.

# AI System Impact Assessment (AISIA)
## NexaAI Ltd — Resume Screening System

**Document ID:** AISIA-2024-001
**AI System Name:** NexaAI Candidate Ranking Engine (NCRE)
**Assessment Date:** 2026-03-25
**Owner:** AI Governance Team
**Classification:** High Impact
**Approved by:** Chief Technology Officer / Compliance Lead
**Next Review Date:** 2027-03-25

---

## 1. Executive Summary

This AISIA documents the potential impacts of NexaAI Ltd's resume screening system on job candidates, the organisation, and broader employment practices. The system poses **high impact** risks due to: (1) lack of candidate transparency regarding AI use, (2) bias risks from 2015–2022 training data, (3) significant consequences for affected individuals (employment eligibility), and (4) vulnerability of candidates as potentially disadvantaged individuals in hiring decisions.

This assessment informs control selection under ISO/IEC 42001:2023 Clause 6.1.2 and drives mandatory enhanced transparency, human oversight, and bias mitigation measures.

---

## 2. AI System Context & Intended Purpose

### 2.1 System Overview
- **System Name:** NexaAI Candidate Ranking Engine (NCRE)
- **Type:** Classification and ranking model (ML-based scoring system)
- **Intended Purpose:** To automatically score and rank job candidates on a scale of 1–10, streamlining initial candidate filtering and reducing manual resume screening time
- **Organisation Role:** AI Provider (develops and deploys the system internally; may commercialise later)
- **Deployment Context:** Integrated into NexaAI's recruitment platform; used for initial candidate triage across multiple open positions

### 2.2 System Boundaries
- **In scope:** The ML model, training data, scoring algorithm, ranking output, and any features or integrations that influence candidate ranking
- **Out of scope:** HR business processes after candidate ranking (interview scheduling, offer letter generation)

### 2.3 Volume & Frequency
- **Processing volume:** ~500 candidate applications per month (~6,000 per year)
- **Output type:** Autonomous decision support (ranking; not a final hiring decision but heavily influences candidate pool)
- **Current human review:** No documented human review step before candidate filtering based on AI rank

---

## 3. AISIA Dimensions: Impact Assessment

### 3.1 Intended Purpose & Output Type
| Dimension | Finding |
|-----------|---------|
| **Intended Purpose** | Automate resume screening and candidate ranking (scale 1–10) |
| **Output Type** | Classification and ranking (autonomous decision support) |
| **Decision Scope** | Influences which candidates advance to human review; effectively filters candidacy |

**Risk:** The system produces a final ranking without opportunity for candidates to contest or understand the scoring basis. Described as "ranking" but functions as a gate-keeping mechanism.

---

### 3.2 Impact Domain
| Dimension | Finding |
|-----------|---------|
| **Primary Domain** | **Employment** — direct impact on job application outcomes |
| **Secondary Domains** | Financial services (if hiring for roles), law enforcement (if applicable) |
| **Impact Type** | Individual (candidates), organisational (NexaAI hiring process) |

---

### 3.3 Affected Population & Scale
| Dimension | Finding |
|-----------|---------|
| **Scale** | ~500 candidates/month (~6,000/year) × potential multi-year use → significant population |
| **Vulnerability** | **High** — candidates are inherently in a vulnerable position: (1) dependence on employment, (2) lack of transparency regarding AI use, (3) no ability to contest ranking, (4) power imbalance (employer–applicant) |
| **Protected Characteristics** | Resume screening data may correlate with age, gender, ethnicity, disability, or socioeconomic status; training data (2015–2022) reflects historical hiring biases |

---

### 3.4 Severity of Potential Harms

#### 3.4.1 Bias & Unfairness Risks
| Risk | Severity | Evidence |
|------|----------|----------|
| **Historical bias in training data** | **Critical** | Model trained on 2015–2022 hiring data; this period is known to contain gender bias (e.g., Amazon's scrapped ML model), racial bias, and age discrimination in hiring |
| **Age discrimination** | **High** | Older candidates may be penalised if training data shows preferences for younger hires; cumulative disadvantage over 6,000 candidates/year |
| **Gender bias** | **High** | If training data underrepresents women in technical/leadership roles, model may systematically downrank women |
| **Disability discrimination** | **High** | Candidates with disability employment gaps or non-traditional career paths may be ranked lower |
| **Socioeconomic bias** | **Medium–High** | Candidates from under-resourced education systems or those with employment gaps may be unfairly penalised |

#### 3.4.2 Lack of Transparency Harms
| Risk | Severity | Evidence |
|------|----------|----------|
| **No candidate awareness** | **High** | Candidates not informed that AI is used in screening; unable to contest or explain anomalies in their application |
| **Black-box decision-making** | **High** | Candidates receive no explanation for ranking score (e.g., why a 3 instead of 5); no recourse mechanism |
| **Regulatory exposure** | **High** | EU AI Act (High-risk), UK AI Bill, and employment law (Equal Pay Act, Equality Act 2010) may require transparency; NexaAI may face legal liability |

#### 3.4.3 Consequential Harms
| Risk | Severity | Evidence |
|------|----------|----------|
| **Career/financial impact** | **High** | A low AI score directly prevents candidate from being reviewed by human recruiters; results in job loss opportunity, lost income, reputational damage |
| **Scale of harm** | **High** | If 20% of 6,000 candidates/year (1,200 individuals) are unfairly downranked due to bias, impact is systemic |
| **Erosion of human autonomy** | **Medium** | If recruiter bias toward AI scores is strong, human decision-making is effectively delegated to an opaque algorithm |

---

### 3.5 Reversibility of Harms

| Dimension | Finding |
|-----------|---------|
| **Reversibility** | **Low to Medium** |
| **Why** | Once a candidate is filtered out of the pool, they are unlikely to re-apply. Even if bias is later identified, individual candidates cannot be contacted retroactively. Reputational harm to candidates and NexaAI may be irreversible. |
| **Mitigation potential** | Partial — corrective action (retraining model, retroactive review of filtered candidates) is possible but operationally costly and does not restore lost opportunity |

---

## 4. AISIA Impact Classification & Control Implications

### 4.1 Impact Level: **HIGH**

**Justification:**
1. **High severity consequences** — employment eligibility directly affects individuals' financial security and career trajectory
2. **Vulnerable population** — candidates lack transparency, power, and recourse mechanisms
3. **Hard-to-reverse harms** — filtered-out candidates unlikely to reapply; no mechanism for retroactive review
4. **Significant bias risk** — training data from 2015–2022 is known to contain employment-related biases; no evidence of bias audit or mitigation
5. **Lack of human oversight** — no documented human review before candidate filtering
6. **Scale** — 6,000+ individuals affected annually
7. **Regulatory alignment** — system characteristics align with "high-risk" AI definitions in EU AI Act and UK AI Bill

---

### 4.2 Control Implications (ISO 42001 Clause 6.1.2 & Annex A)

**Per ISO 42001:2023, high-impact AI systems require:**

| Control | Requirement | NexaAI Status |
|---------|-------------|---------------|
| **A.4.1 — AI Policy** | Document intended purpose, limitations, and responsible AI principles | ❌ Not documented |
| **A.5.1 — Human Oversight** | Mandatory human review mechanism for high-impact decisions | ❌ No human review documented |
| **A.6.1 — Lifecycle Governance** | Controls for model development, testing, validation, deployment, monitoring | ❌ Partial |
| **A.7.1 — Data Governance** | Training data quality assessment, bias testing, retention controls | ❌ No bias audit evident |
| **A.7.2 — Data Quality** | Validation data representative of real-world population; testing for discrimination | ❌ Not documented |
| **A.8.1 — Transparency & Disclosure** | Inform affected individuals that AI is used; explain decision basis where feasible | ❌ **Critical gap** — no candidate notification |
| **A.8.2 — Explanation & Contestation** | Provide explanation mechanism and right to contest AI decisions | ❌ Not implemented |
| **A.8.3 — Incident Management** | Track and respond to bias incidents, fairness complaints | ❌ No process evident |

---

## 5. Risk Register & Treatment Decisions

### 5.1 AI-Specific Risk Register

| Risk ID | Risk Category | Description | Likelihood | Severity | Risk Level | Treatment | Owner |
|---------|---------------|-------------|------------|----------|-----------|-----------|-------|
| **R-001** | Model Bias | Historical bias in 2015–2022 training data results in systematic downranking of protected groups (age, gender, disability) | High | High | **Critical** | **Modify** — Conduct bias audit; retrain with balanced dataset; implement fairness constraints | Data Science Lead |
| **R-002** | Transparency Gap | Candidates not informed that AI is used; no explanation mechanism | High | High | **Critical** | **Modify** — Implement candidate notification at application submission; add explainability module | Product + Legal |
| **R-003** | Lack of Human Oversight | No human review of AI scores before candidate filtering | High | High | **Critical** | **Modify** — Implement mandatory human review for candidates ranked 4–6 (ambiguous zone); audit review frequency | Recruitment Lead |
| **R-004** | Data Quality Unknown | Training data provenance, representativeness, and outlier handling not documented | Medium–High | High | **High** | **Modify** — Audit training dataset composition; test for geographic, demographic, educational biases | Data Governance Officer |
| **R-005** | Model Drift | Scoring patterns may change over time; no monitoring process documented | Medium | High | **High** | **Accept with Monitoring** — Implement monthly bias report; set KPI threshold (e.g., <5% disparity ratio by protected group); escalate if exceeded | Analytics Lead |
| **R-006** | Regulatory Non-Compliance | System may violate EU AI Act (High-risk), UK AI Bill, Equal Pay Act 2010, Equality Act 2010 | High | Medium–High | **Critical** | **Modify** — Legal review; implement transparency controls; establish audit trail for regulatory demonstration | Compliance Officer |
| **R-007** | Reputational Damage | Bias incident or fairness complaint in media; candidate backlash | Medium | Medium | **High** | **Avoid / Modify** — Implement proactive bias audit; establish incident response plan; candidate notification strategy | Chief Marketing Officer |
| **R-008** | Candidate Contestation | Candidates lack mechanism to contest AI scores; legal exposure if scores are challenged | Medium | High | **High** | **Modify** — Implement appeals/explanation process; maintain audit trail of AI reasoning | Legal + Product |

---

### 5.2 Risk Treatment Decisions

#### **Treatment #1: Model Bias — MODIFY (Immediate)**
1. **Action:** Commission independent bias audit of NCRE model using protected attribute analysis
2. **Timeline:** Complete within 30 days
3. **Deliverable:** Bias audit report; disparate impact ratio analysis (by age, gender, ethnicity proxy, disability status)
4. **Threshold:** If any group has >1.25 disparate impact ratio, retrain model with fairness-aware ML techniques
5. **Owner:** Data Science Lead + External Auditor

#### **Treatment #2: Transparency Gap — MODIFY (Immediate)**
1. **Action:** Notify all candidates at application submission that AI is used in screening
2. **Disclosure language:** "This application will be reviewed by an AI-assisted system. Your resume will receive an automated initial screening score (1–10), which informs whether your application advances to human review."
3. **Timeline:** Implement within 14 days
4. **Mechanism:** Update application form; send notification email; add FAQ page
5. **Owner:** Product + Legal

#### **Treatment #3: Human Oversight — MODIFY (Within 30 days)**
1. **Action:** Implement mandatory human review for all candidates, with risk-based prioritisation
   - **Tier 1 (Scores 1–3):** No human review (proceed with rejection notification)
   - **Tier 2 (Scores 4–6):** Mandatory human review before filtering
   - **Tier 3 (Scores 7–10):** Standard human review (prioritised for interviews)
2. **Audit trail:** Document reviewer name, review date, and decision (accept/reject/reassess)
3. **Owner:** Recruitment Lead

#### **Treatment #4: Data Quality & Audit — MODIFY (Within 60 days)**
1. **Action:** Audit training dataset composition and representativeness
2. **Scope:**
   - Identify source of 2015–2022 data (internal hiring records?)
   - Analyse demographic breakdown (age, gender, race, disability status proxy)
   - Identify any data quality issues (missing values, outliers, duplicates)
3. **Deliverable:** Data quality report; recommendations for retraining with balanced/debiased dataset
4. **Owner:** Data Governance Officer

#### **Treatment #5: Model Monitoring — ACCEPT WITH MONITORING (Ongoing)**
1. **Action:** Implement monthly bias monitoring dashboard
2. **KPIs:**
   - Disparate impact ratio by protected group (target: <1.05)
   - Score distribution comparison (target: <10% difference in mean score across groups)
   - Human review override rate by AI score tier (target: <15%)
3. **Escalation:** If KPI threshold exceeded, trigger incident response (pause system, bias audit, retrain decision)
4. **Owner:** Analytics Lead + Compliance Officer

#### **Treatment #6: Regulatory Alignment — MODIFY (Within 90 days)**
1. **Action:** Legal review of NCRE against:
   - EU AI Act (High-risk HR systems) — transparency, human review, documentation requirements
   - UK AI Bill — fairness, accountability, audit trail
   - UK Equality Act 2010 — indirect discrimination liability
2. **Deliverable:** Legal compliance memo; gap analysis; remediation roadmap
3. **Owner:** Compliance Officer + External Legal Counsel

#### **Treatment #7: Incident Response — MODIFY (Within 30 days)**
1. **Action:** Establish AI incident management process for resume screening
2. **Incident types:**
   - Fairness complaint from candidate
   - Bias detection (automated or manual)
   - System failure (scores not generated, incorrect scores)
   - Regulatory inquiry
3. **Process:** Incident report → investigation → root cause analysis → corrective action → post-incident review
4. **Owner:** Compliance Officer

#### **Treatment #8: Contestation & Appeals — MODIFY (Within 45 days)**
1. **Action:** Design appeals mechanism for candidates
2. **Mechanism:**
   - Candidate can request explanation of AI score (generated by explainability module)
   - Candidate can appeal low score for manual human review
   - Response deadline: 5 business days
3. **Owner:** Product + HR Lead

## 9. Conclusion

NexaAI Ltd's resume screening system (NCRE) poses **high impact** risks to affected candidates due to:
1. Significant consequences (employment eligibility) for vulnerable individuals
2. Lack of transparency and human oversight
3. Known bias risks in historical training data (2015–2022)
4. Limited reversibility of harms if candidates are incorrectly filtered

This AISIA mandates **enhanced controls** under ISO/IEC 42001:2023 Clause 6.1.2: mandatory bias audit, candidate notification, human review, data quality assessment, explainability, and incident management.

The attached risk register and treatment decisions provide a **30–90 day remediation roadmap** to achieve ISO 42001 compliance and reduce fairness-related legal and reputational risk.

**Recommendation:** Implement all P0 and P1 controls within the next 45 days before processing additional candidate applications with the unaudited system.

# AI System Impact Assessment (AISIA)
## NexaAI Ltd - Resume Screening System

**Assessment Date:** March 25, 2026
**System Name:** NexaAI Resume Screening System
**Assessment Type:** High-Risk AI Application Evaluation
**Conducted By:** GRC Compliance Team

---

## Executive Summary

This AI System Impact Assessment evaluates NexaAI Ltd's machine learning-based resume screening system, which ranks job candidates on a 1-10 scale. The assessment identifies significant compliance, ethical, and operational risks requiring immediate remediation. The system presents high-risk factors due to lack of transparency, potential bias from historical training data, and absence of human-in-the-loop safeguards.

---

## 1. System Overview

### 1.1 System Description
- **Function:** Automated ranking of job candidate resumes on a 1-10 scale
- **Technology:** Machine learning model
- **Volume:** Approximately 500 candidate applications per month
- **Training Data:** Historical hiring data (2015-2022)
- **Deployment Status:** Active in production

### 1.2 Stakeholders
- Job applicants (subjects of assessment)
- Hiring managers and recruiters (system users)
- NexaAI Ltd (system owner)
- Regulatory bodies (employment law enforcement)

---

## 2. Impact Assessment Framework

### 2.1 Risk Severity: HIGH

This system warrants high-risk classification due to:
- **High stakes for individuals:** Directly determines employment opportunities
- **Lack of transparency:** Candidates unaware AI is making decisions about them
- **Historical bias risk:** Training data from 2015-2022 reflects prior hiring patterns and societal biases
- **Limited human oversight:** No mention of human review mechanisms
- **Irreversible consequences:** Rejected candidates may not reapply

---

## 3. Detailed Risk Analysis

### 3.1 Bias and Discrimination Risk

#### Current State Analysis
The system is trained on historical hiring data (2015-2022), which creates significant bias propagation risks:

**Identified Bias Sources:**
- **Proxy discrimination:** The model may learn patterns correlated with protected characteristics (race, gender, age, disability status) even if these are not explicit inputs
- **Historical bias amplification:** If the 2015-2022 hiring data reflects discriminatory practices, the system will perpetuate and amplify these patterns
- **Occupational segregation bias:** Historical data may reflect gender or racial segregation in certain roles that the model treats as predictive
- **Educational bias:** If training data over-represents certain educational institutions, the model may discriminate against underrepresented populations
- **Recency bias:** A 4-year gap between training data end (2022) and current use (2026) means the model may not reflect current workforce dynamics or skills

#### Specific Compliance Risks
- **EEO Violations:** Potential disparate impact on protected classes
- **GDPR/CCPA Violations:** Automated decision-making without transparency
- **Fair Lending/Employment Laws:** Discrimination based on protected characteristics

#### Evidence of Risk
- No audit trail showing bias testing has been performed
- No validation that model performance is equitable across demographic groups
- Training data is 4+ years old, potentially outdated

### 3.2 Transparency and Consent Risks

#### Current Deficiency
"Candidates are not currently informed that AI is used in screening" represents a critical transparency failure.

**Implications:**
- **Lack of informed consent:** Candidates cannot make informed decisions about their participation
- **Regulatory non-compliance:** Most jurisdictions require disclosure of automated decision-making
- **Ethical violation:** Covert use of AI violates principles of procedural justice
- **Trust erosion risk:** Public disclosure of this practice could damage organizational reputation

#### Regulatory Framework Violations
- **EU AI Act:** Requires high-risk AI systems to inform individuals they are subject to automated decision-making
- **GDPR Article 22:** Individuals have the right to not be subject to automated decision-making
- **US FCRA Section 575:** Fair Credit Reporting Act requires disclosure of automated decision tools
- **State-level laws:** Connecticut, New York, and other states have specific notification requirements

### 3.3 Accuracy and Validation Risks

#### Assessment
- **No evidence of:** Model validation metrics, accuracy benchmarks, or performance testing
- **No mention of:** Fairness metrics, false positive/negative rates, or calibration across groups
- **Unknown:** Whether the 1-10 ranking reflects actual hiring outcomes or job performance

#### Specific Concerns
- A 1-10 scale implies ordinal precision that may not exist
- Ranking 500 candidates/month without validation creates potential for systematic errors
- No documented system for identifying and correcting model failures

### 3.4 Accountability and Governance Risks

#### Gaps Identified
- **No documented appeals process:** Candidates cannot challenge rankings
- **No audit trail:** No mechanism to explain why a candidate received a specific score
- **No ownership:** Unclear who is accountable for system performance and bias
- **No monitoring:** No continuous performance monitoring or drift detection

#### Downstream Risks
- Hiring teams may treat AI scores as objective truth rather than input for human judgment
- Lack of recourse may violate legal principles of due process
- Silent failures may persist undetected for extended periods

---

## 4. Regulatory Compliance Assessment

### 4.1 Applicable Frameworks

| Framework | Status | Gap Severity |
|-----------|--------|--------------|
| EU AI Act (if applicable) | Non-compliant | Critical |
| GDPR Article 22 | Non-compliant | Critical |
| Equal Employment Opportunity Laws | Likely non-compliant | Critical |
| Fair Credit Reporting Act (FCRA) | Likely non-compliant | High |
| State AI transparency laws | Non-compliant | High |
| EEOC AI guidance | Non-compliant | Critical |

### 4.2 Specific Violations

**GDPR Compliance Failure:**
- Article 22 prohibits purely automated decision-making with legal effects
- No evidence of human involvement in final hiring decisions
- No documented exemptions or safeguards

**EEO Compliance Failure:**
- Potential disparate impact on protected classes not assessed
- No validation of model fairness across demographics
- Training data bias not evaluated

**Transparency Requirements Failure:**
- No candidate notification of AI use
- No explanation mechanism for scores
- No information about data sources used

---

## 5. Ethical Assessment

### 5.1 Fairness Analysis

**Current State:** Inadequate assurance of fairness

**Fairness Concerns:**
1. **Distributive fairness:** Does the system allocate opportunities equitably?
2. **Procedural fairness:** Can candidates understand and challenge decisions?
3. **Recognition fairness:** Does the system recognize the full value of diverse candidates?

**Assessment:** The system fails across all three dimensions.

### 5.2 Human Dignity and Agency

- Candidates are evaluated by an opaque system without their knowledge
- No opportunity for candidates to explain qualifications beyond resume format
- Risk of reducing human candidates to numerical scores

### 5.3 Accountability and Democratic Principles

- No mechanism for candidates to understand why they were ranked
- No appeals process
- Organizational accountability unclear

---

## 6. Technical Risks

### 6.1 Data Quality Issues

**Training Data Concerns:**
- 4-year gap between training data (2015-2022) and current use (2026)
- No documentation of data preprocessing, cleaning, or validation
- Potential for data leakage, mislabeling, or incomplete records
- Unknown representativeness of training dataset

### 6.2 Model Robustness

**Identified Gaps:**
- No documented testing for adversarial inputs or edge cases
- Unclear handling of non-standard resume formats
- No documented performance across different resume types
- Unknown how model handles missing or incomplete data

### 6.3 System Integration Risks

- No documented API security measures
- Unknown logging and monitoring capabilities
- No documented disaster recovery procedures
- Unclear data retention and deletion policies

---

## 7. Recommendations and Remediation Plan

### 7.1 CRITICAL - Immediate Actions (0-30 days)

1. **Implement Candidate Notification**
   - Inform all candidates that AI is used in screening
   - Provide clear explanation of the ranking system
   - Disclose that rankings inform but do not determine hiring decisions
   - Establish right to request human review

2. **Halt Autonomous Decision-Making**
   - Require human review of all AI rankings before communication to candidates
   - Ensure hiring managers make final decisions with AI as input only
   - Document human decision-making process

3. **Establish Appeals Process**
   - Create mechanism for candidates to challenge rankings
   - Provide explanation of how ranking was determined
   - Allow resubmission or human review request

### 7.2 HIGH PRIORITY - Short-term Actions (1-3 months)

1. **Bias Audit and Validation**
   - Conduct independent bias audit across protected classes
   - Compare model rankings with actual job performance data
   - Calculate disparate impact metrics
   - Test model performance on diverse candidate profiles
   - Document fairness metrics and thresholds

2. **Model Retrain with 2023-2025 Data**
   - Replace training dataset with current hiring data
   - Ensure training data reflects diverse workforce
   - Implement stratified sampling to prevent underrepresentation
   - Document data provenance and quality

3. **Fairness Constraints Implementation**
   - Implement fairness constraints (e.g., demographic parity, equalized odds)
   - Establish maximum acceptable disparate impact ratios
   - Monitor intersectional fairness (race + gender combinations)
   - Create fairness dashboards for ongoing monitoring

4. **Explainability Enhancement**
   - Implement model explainability techniques (SHAP, LIME, or similar)
   - Generate explanations for each candidate ranking
   - Enable candidates to understand which resume elements influenced their score
   - Create transparency reports for auditing

### 7.3 MEDIUM PRIORITY - Medium-term Actions (3-6 months)

1. **Comprehensive Governance Framework**
   - Establish AI accountability board
   - Define roles and responsibilities
   - Create incident response procedures
   - Document risk management processes

2. **Continuous Monitoring System**
   - Implement real-time performance monitoring
   - Track model drift and retraining triggers
   - Monitor for bias emergence over time
   - Compare AI rankings with actual hiring outcomes

3. **Human-in-the-Loop Enhancement**
   - Require human review for borderline cases
   - Implement structured human decision-making protocols
   - Train hiring managers on AI limitations and bias
   - Establish quality assurance sampling

4. **Data Governance**
   - Document data collection, storage, and deletion procedures
   - Implement data minimization principles
   - Establish data access controls
   - Create data retention policy

### 7.4 ONGOING - Operational Excellence (6+ months)

1. **Regular Audits**
   - Quarterly bias and fairness audits
   - Annual independent third-party assessment
   - Continuous validation against hiring outcomes
   - Impact assessment on underrepresented groups

2. **Stakeholder Communication**
   - Publish annual AI transparency reports
   - Engage with diversity and inclusion teams
   - Collect candidate feedback on process fairness
   - Maintain regulatory compliance documentation

3. **System Evolution**
   - Evaluate alternative models or approaches
   - Investigate hybrid human-AI decision systems
   - Consider resume-blind alternatives for initial screening
   - Explore skill-based assessments over resume-based ranking

---

### 8.1 Bias Metrics

| Metric | Target | Current |
|--------|--------|---------|
| Disparate Impact Ratio (protected/majority) | ≥0.80 | Unknown |
| False Positive Rate Parity | <5% difference across groups | Unknown |
| False Negative Rate Parity | <5% difference across groups | Unknown |
| Demographic Parity | Within ±5% | Unknown |

### 8.2 Fairness Metrics

| Metric | Target | Current |
|--------|--------|---------|
| Equal Opportunity Difference | <0.05 | Unknown |
| Calibration Difference | <0.03 | Unknown |
| Individual Fairness | Consistent treatment | Untested |

### 8.3 Operational Metrics

| Metric | Target | Current |
|--------|--------|---------|
| Human Review Rate | 100% before communication | 0% |
| Appeal Rate | Track and investigate | Unknown |
| Model Accuracy (vs. actual hires) | ≥85% | Unknown |
| Ranking Explanation Completeness | 100% | 0% |

---

## 9. Conclusion

The NexaAI Ltd resume screening system presents **CRITICAL COMPLIANCE AND ETHICAL RISKS** in its current state of operation. The system violates multiple regulatory frameworks, lacks transparency, and poses significant bias risks without adequate safeguards.

### Key Findings:

1. **Immediate Non-Compliance:** The system violates GDPR, likely violates EEO laws, and fails transparency requirements in multiple jurisdictions.

2. **Unmitigated Bias Risk:** Training on 2015-2022 data without bias validation creates substantial risk of discrimination against protected classes.

3. **Lack of Accountability:** Absence of explainability, appeals processes, and human oversight violates principles of procedural justice.

4. **Transparency Failure:** Candidates' lack of awareness of AI use represents a fundamental consent and ethical violation.

### Recommended Approach:

Implement the phased remediation plan immediately, with transparency and human oversight as critical first steps. The system should function as a decision-support tool with human decision-makers retaining final authority, not as an autonomous decision-maker.

**Risk Level:** HIGH
**Urgency:** CRITICAL
**Estimated Remediation Timeline:** 3-6 months with immediate interim measures

---

## 10. Assessment Metadata

- **Assessment Date:** March 25, 2026
- **Scope:** Organizational hiring system using machine learning
- **Data Reviewed:** System design, training data characteristics, deployment practices
- **Limitations:** Assessment based on described system characteristics; full code review and testing not performed
- **Recommendations:** For legal compliance, conduct assessment with legal counsel and compliance specialists

## Appendix A: Regulatory Framework Summary

### EU AI Act (if applicable in jurisdiction)
- Resume screening is classified as "high-risk" AI under EU AI Act Annex III
- Requires: human oversight, quality management, transparency, bias monitoring, documented compliance
- Current system: Non-compliant on all counts

### GDPR Article 22
- Prohibits "solely automated decision-making" with legal/similarly significant effects
- Exemptions available only with: explicit consent, necessity for contract, or legal authorization
- Requires: information right and right to explanation
- Current system: Likely violates Article 22

### EEOC Guidance on AI and Hiring
- Employers are responsible for ensuring AI systems don't discriminate
- Requires: validation evidence, disparate impact analysis, documentation
- Current system: No validation evidence provided

### State Laws (Connecticut, New York, etc.)
- Connecticut: Requires notice of automated employment decisions
- New York: Requires bias audit before deployment and consent before use
- Illinois: Restricts use of social media for hiring
- Current system: Non-compliant with state transparency requirements

**End of Assessment**
